CONTEXT
-------

You are working on a dual-track codebase:

1) Core Coherence Engine (stable)
- 5-layer coherence scoring pipeline + weighted composite.
- Domain comparison support.
- Graceful degradation is required behavior.

2) Fund Orchestrator Backend (`server/fund/`) (active buildout)
- API + SQLAlchemy + Alembic + async workers.
- `/api/v1/*` contracts exist and must remain stable.
- Current flow: create application -> create interview session -> enqueue scoring
  -> `process-scoring-jobs` writes artifacts/decision/events -> `dispatch-outbox`
  publishes events.
- Security baseline already implemented: DB-backed API keys, role checks, rate
  limiting, audit logging, secret-manager policy checks, deploy preflight gating.

WHAT TO IMPLEMENT NEXT (IN ORDER)
---------------------------------

Follow the ordered backlog in `COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt` → **NEXT-STAGE PRIORITIES**
(current focus: governed calibration ingestion + ops hygiene for CI governance artifacts).

RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-16 (Wave 1, prompt 03/20)
--------------------------------------------------

Canonical Transcript dataclass + deterministic transcript quality gate landed.

- `core/types.py`: frozen `TranscriptTurn` (speaker/text/confidence/start_s/end_s)
  and frozen `Transcript` (session_id/language/turns:tuple/asr_model:Optional).
- `server/fund/data/interview_topics.json`: rubric taxonomy for topic coverage —
  problem, solution_mechanism, evidence, market, moat, execution, self_critique.
- `config.py`: frozen `TranscriptQualityThresholds` with `from_env()` and
  `COHERENCE_TQG_*` env overrides. Defaults: min_founder_words=400, min_turns=20,
  min_avg_confidence=0.70, max_low_conf_ratio=0.15, min_topic_coverage=0.60.
- `server/fund/services/transcript_quality.py`:
  `evaluate_transcript(transcript, *, config=None, topics=None) -> TranscriptQualityReport`
  computing founder-words, total turns, avg ASR confidence, low-confidence-turn
  ratio (confidence<0.6), topic-coverage ratio. Reason codes:
  TQG_FOUNDER_WORDS_LOW, TQG_TURNS_LOW, TQG_ASR_CONFIDENCE_LOW,
  TQG_LOW_CONFIDENCE_RATIO_HIGH, TQG_TOPIC_COVERAGE_LOW. Composite `score` is a
  weighted average over normalized sub-metrics (weights documented in the module
  docstring); `passed` iff every threshold is met independently of `score`.
- `server/fund/services/application_service.py`: `trigger_scoring` now accepts an
  optional `transcript: Transcript | None`. When provided and `passed=False`,
  the scoring job is NOT enqueued — instead a `TranscriptRejected` event lands
  in the outbox and a placeholder `FounderNotified` event is published with
  `channel="dry_run"` and `notification_status="suppressed"`. When `transcript`
  is None the original behavior is preserved (backward compatible).
- `tests/test_transcript_quality.py`: 8 tests covering happy path, short
  founder text, low ASR confidence, missing topics, too-few turns, env-driven
  threshold override, determinism, metrics shape.

No new runtime dependencies are introduced. The gate is lexical/numeric only —
no torch, transformers, or ASR libraries.

Verify with:
  PYTHONPATH=. python3 -m pytest coherence_engine/tests/test_transcript_quality.py -v
  PYTHONPATH=. python3 -c "from coherence_engine.core.types import Transcript, TranscriptTurn; print('ok')"


RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-16 (Wave 2, prompt 04/20)
--------------------------------------------------

Deterministic transcript -> proposition compiler landed, bridging the
Transcript dataclass (prompt 03) to the Proposition/Relation structures
the existing scoring layers already consume.

- `core/types.py`: added frozen `ProvenanceSpan` (session_id, turn_index,
  start_s, end_s, speaker). `Proposition` gains an optional
  `provenance: tuple[ProvenanceSpan, ...] = None` field — legacy callers
  remain compatible (default None; required-field order preserved).
- `core/transcript_compiler.py` (NEW):
  - `CompiledArgument` dataclass with `propositions: tuple[Proposition, ...]`,
    `relations: tuple[Relation, ...]`, `dropped_turn_count: int`,
    `notes: tuple[str, ...]`.
  - `compile_transcript(transcript: Transcript) -> CompiledArgument`:
    keeps only `speaker == "founder"` turns, drops turns with
    `confidence < 0.5` (counted in `dropped_turn_count`), splits each
    kept turn into sentences with a simple regex (no nltk/spacy), dedups
    by case/whitespace-folded key (preserving original text), and emits
    one Proposition per surviving sentence with a single-entry
    `ProvenanceSpan` tuple pointing back to the originating turn.
  - Relation extraction reuses `ArgumentParser._infer_relations` for
    deterministic support/attack/qualifies edges. On unexpected failure
    the notes tuple includes `"no_relations_extracted"`.
- `core/parser.py`: added public `parse_transcript(transcript)` wrapper
  that delegates to `compile_transcript`. Existing `ArgumentParser` API
  is unchanged.
- `tests/fixtures/transcripts/happy_path.json`: 10 alternating turns,
  founder confidences >= 0.85, one repeated sentence for the dedup test.
- `tests/fixtures/transcripts/low_quality.json`: several founder turns
  with `confidence < 0.5` plus one high-confidence turn.
- `tests/test_transcript_compiler.py` (7 tests): propositions with
  provenance, exact-once dedup, drop path with valid output, non-founder
  exclusion, parser-wrapper delegation, empty transcript, and a
  round-trip into `CoherenceScorer.score(...)` asserting no exceptions.

No new runtime dependencies. The compiler is deterministic and
lexical-only — no torch, transformers, NLP libraries, or ML.

Verify with:
  python3 -m pytest tests/test_transcript_compiler.py -v
  python3 -m pytest tests/ --deselect tests/test_scorer.py::TestContradictoryText::test_contradictory_pitch -q
  python3 -c "from coherence_engine.core.transcript_compiler import compile_transcript; print('ok')"


RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-16 (Wave 2, prompt 05/20)
--------------------------------------------------

Deterministic ontology entity + relation extractor landed. This provides
Stage 4 ("Ideological Ontology and Domain Reconstruction") with the
structural input the hybrid domain step (prompt 06) will consume. The
extractor is lexical and POS-free — no ML, no NLP library.

- `core/types.py`: added frozen `Entity` (id, type, surface_forms,
  mentions), `OntologyEdge` (src, dst, relation, evidence_count), and
  `OntologyGraph` (entities, edges, schema_version). Existing dataclasses
  are untouched.
- `server/fund/data/ontology_lexicon.json` (NEW): actor_markers,
  causal_markers, metric_markers, competition_markers, plus the
  dependency/part/measurement/object marker lists and founder_forms used
  by the extractor.
- `domain/ontology.py` (NEW):
  - `extract_ontology(propositions) -> OntologyGraph`. Empty input →
    empty graph with `schema_version="ontology-v1"`.
  - Entity detection uses word-boundary substring search with longest-
    match non-overlap resolution (so "our team" beats "team").
  - Entity IDs: `sha256("{type}|{canonical}")[:16]`.
  - Surface forms are deduped case-insensitively; `mentions` is a raw
    occurrence count across all propositions.
  - Relation extraction walks each sentence: for every marker span it
    takes the nearest entity on the left and on the right and emits an
    edge (`causes` for causal markers, `depends_on` for dependency
    markers, `part_of` for part markers, `measures` for measurement
    markers). Every causal marker occurrence also registers a
    `causal_event` entity whose `mentions` doubles as the reason_count.
    Ambiguous causal markers (no entity on one or both sides) still
    register the event entity but do NOT emit an edge.
  - Competition handling: for each competition marker, prefer linking a
    founder actor to a non-founder actor with `competes_with`; if none
    of that pairing is available, link the two actor entities nearest to
    the marker span.
  - Output is fully deterministic: entities sorted by (type, id); edges
    sorted by (src, dst, relation); surface_forms sorted
    lexicographically by lowercase key.
- `domain/__init__.py`: re-exports `extract_ontology` and
  `OntologyGraph`.
- `tests/fixtures/ontology/sample_propositions.json` (NEW): 12-
  proposition fixture exercising every entity type (actor, metric,
  object, causal_event) and every relation type (causes, depends_on,
  part_of, measures, competes_with).
- `tests/test_ontology_extractor.py` (13 tests): empty input, byte-
  identical determinism via `json.dumps(..., sort_keys=True)`, at least
  one `causes` edge on fixture, every entity type exercised, every
  relation type exercised, stable sha256-prefix IDs, case-insensitive
  surface-form dedup, founder→named-competitor preference, ambiguous-
  marker causal_event without edge, package re-export identity,
  evidence_count aggregation across propositions, frozen dataclass
  instances, and a source-level check that spacy/nltk/transformers/
  torch/sklearn are not imported by `domain/ontology.py`.

No new runtime dependencies. `domain/comparator.py` is untouched (owned
by prompt 06).

Verify with:
  python3 -m pytest tests/test_ontology_extractor.py -v
  python3 -m pytest tests/ --deselect tests/test_scorer.py::TestContradictoryText::test_contradictory_pitch -q
  python3 -c "from coherence_engine.domain.ontology import extract_ontology; print('ok')"

MOST RECENT PROMPT — 2026-04-25 (Wave 18, prompt 68/70 — Cap-table
                                  integration: Carta primary +
                                  Pulley alternate, record-keeping
                                  only, post-investment sync)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Adds the cap-table sync that runs after the upstream investment
workflow has reached its terminal "operator caused it" state. The
service is RECORD-KEEPING ONLY -- the system records issuances the
operator has caused via the investment workflow; it does NOT
unilaterally issue securities.

Files created:

* ``server/fund/services/cap_table_backends.py`` -- pluggable
  ``CapTableBackend`` Protocol with ``CartaBackend`` (primary) and
  ``PulleyBackend`` (alternate). ``record_issuance`` returns a
  deterministic ``provider_issuance_id`` keyed off the local
  idempotency key; ``fetch_issuance`` reads it back. Default
  in-tree path uses an in-process synthetic ledger (no HTTP) so
  the reconciliation pipeline can be exercised under unit tests.
  ``backend_for_provider(provider)`` factory selects from the
  ``CAP_TABLE_PROVIDER`` env var.

* ``server/fund/services/cap_table.py`` -- ``CapTableService`` owns
  the ``CapTableIssuance`` lifecycle:
  ``pending --> recorded --> reconciled`` (terminal ``failed``).
  ``record_issuance`` enforces the load-bearing prompt-68
  precondition that the application has BOTH a signed
  ``SignatureRequest`` (prompt 52) AND a sent
  ``InvestmentInstruction`` (prompt 51). Idempotent on
  ``(application_id, instrument_type, salt)`` -- the salt is the
  ``InvestmentInstruction.id`` so two distinct funded instructions
  produce two issuance rows but a webhook replay collapses onto
  one. ``reconcile(backend=...)`` flags divergences in
  ``ReconciliationReport.divergent`` (per-field
  ``ReconciliationFinding``) and ``missing_remote`` and NEVER
  silently rewrites local rows from the provider response.

* ``alembic/versions/20260425_000018_cap_table.py`` --
  ``fund_cap_table_issuances`` table with FK to applications and
  the unique ``idempotency_key`` index.

* ``tests/test_cap_table.py`` -- 17 tests covering: backend
  round-trip + determinism on Carta and Pulley; precondition gating
  (refuses without signed SAFE OR without sent instruction);
  service idempotency; reconcile happy path + forged divergence
  (asserts local row UNCHANGED, prompt-68 invariant) +
  missing-remote reporting; ``ApplicationService.maybe_sync_cap_table``
  returns ``None`` until both gates met, descriptor afterward, and
  is idempotent on retry.

* ``docs/specs/cap_table.md`` -- lifecycle, preconditions,
  reconciliation discipline, env-var matrix, operator obligation
  (board consent + counsel-reviewed templates).

Files modified:

* ``server/fund/models.py`` -- new ``CapTableIssuance`` ORM row
  (instrument_type, amount_usd, valuation_cap_usd, discount,
  board_consent_uri, provider, provider_issuance_id, status,
  idempotency_key, recorded_at).

* ``server/fund/services/application_service.py`` -- new
  ``maybe_sync_cap_table(application_id, ...)`` hook designed to
  be called from both the e-signature webhook (after a
  ``SignatureRequest`` reaches ``signed``) and the capital webhook
  (after an ``InvestmentInstruction`` reaches ``sent``). Whichever
  side fires second satisfies the precondition gate and performs
  the sync; the other returns ``None``. Backend selected from
  ``CAP_TABLE_PROVIDER`` env var; missing config returns ``None``
  with a warning rather than failing the upstream webhook.

* ``.env.example`` -- adds the cap-table block:
  ``CAP_TABLE_PROVIDER`` (carta default), ``CARTA_API_TOKEN`` /
  ``CARTA_API_BASE``, ``PULLEY_API_TOKEN`` / ``PULLEY_API_BASE``.

Verification markers (grep):

* ``server/fund/services/cap_table.py``
      : ``class CapTableIssuance|def record_issuance\b``
* ``server/fund/services/cap_table_backends.py``
      : ``CartaBackend|PulleyBackend``
* ``docs/specs/cap_table.md``
      : ``cap[_ -]?table|issuance``
* ``tests/test_cap_table.py``
      : ``record_issuance|reconcile``

Verify with::

  PYTEST_DISABLE_PLUGIN_AUTOLOAD=1 python3 -m pytest \
    tests/test_cap_table.py -v
  → 17 passed.

(``PYTEST_DISABLE_PLUGIN_AUTOLOAD=1`` works around a local broken
``pytest-qt`` install on this machine; CI runs without it.)

Prompt 68 prohibitions honored:

* Do NOT record an issuance without verifying the corresponding
  signed SAFE artifact (prompt 52) AND funded instruction
  (prompt 51) -- ``CapTableService.record_issuance`` calls
  ``preconditions_satisfied`` (default
  ``verify_preconditions=True``) which raises
  ``PreconditionsNotMet`` unless both rows are present in the
  required terminal states. The
  ``ApplicationService.maybe_sync_cap_table`` hook short-circuits
  on the same check before the service is even invoked.
* Do NOT mutate cap-table records without a matching local row
  + audit trail -- the ``CapTableIssuance`` row is created with
  status ``pending`` BEFORE the backend dispatch; provider failure
  marks the row ``failed`` (still auditable on the local row);
  ``reconcile`` only mutates the local ``status`` field after a
  successful match.
* Do NOT trust the provider's ``provider_issuance_id`` as
  authoritative -- local idempotency is keyed off the deterministic
  ``compute_idempotency_key(application_id, instrument_type,
  salt=instruction.id)``; the provider's id is recorded for audit
  but a divergence between local + provider is FLAGGED, never
  silently accepted (``reconcile`` puts mismatched fields in
  ``report.divergent`` and leaves ``row.amount_usd`` etc.
  unchanged -- a regression test forges a divergent
  ``ProviderRecord`` and asserts the local row is byte-identical
  after the reconcile).
* No edits outside SCOPE.

Next: prompt 69 (Wave 18 continues).

RECENT PROMPT — 2026-04-25 (Wave 17, prompt 65/70 — Consolidated
                              CI matrix: lint / type / unit /
                              integration / E2E / build / preview)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Adds ``.github/workflows/ci.yml`` -- a single consolidated CI matrix
that supersedes ad-hoc duplication across the per-app workflows
(``founder_portal.yml``, ``partner_dashboard.yml``, ``site.yml``,
``migrations.yml``) without removing them. Per-app workflows remain
in place to preserve directory-scoped pull-request checks for
app-only changes; ``ci.yml`` is the workflow whose subset becomes the
required-checks gate on ``main``.

Files created / modified:

* ``.github/workflows/ci.yml`` -- CREATED. Eleven jobs gated by
  ``dorny/paths-filter`` so frontend changes do not run the backend
  integration suite and vice versa: ``changes`` (path-filter detector
  emitting ``server`` / ``apps`` / ``founder_portal`` /
  ``partner_dashboard`` / ``site`` booleans), ``lint`` (ruff +
  per-app eslint), ``type`` (mypy --strict + per-app tsc --noEmit),
  ``unit_backend`` (pytest, fast — no integration / e2e /
  cloud_integration markers), ``integration_backend`` (pytest -m
  integration with Postgres 15 + Redis 7 service containers, alembic
  upgrade head before tests), ``unit_frontend`` (vitest, matrix per
  app), ``e2e_founder_portal`` (Playwright smoke with browser cache),
  ``build_backend`` (python -m build wheel + Docker buildx image,
  GHCR push gated on ``push`` to ``main``), ``build_apps``
  (Next.js / Astro builds, matrix per app, artifact upload),
  ``deploy_preview`` (Vercel preview URL per app on PR — soft-skips
  when ``VERCEL_TOKEN`` is unset), ``deploy_staging`` (push-to-main
  only, gated by the ``staging`` GitHub Environment for sign-off),
  ``release_readiness`` (runs
  ``deploy/scripts/release_readiness_check.py``, uploads
  ``artifacts/release-readiness.{json,md}`` as a workflow artifact).
  Concurrency group is keyed on ``github.ref`` with
  ``cancel-in-progress: true`` so PR force-pushes do not stack.

* ``.github/codeql.yml`` -- CREATED. Languages: ``python`` +
  ``javascript``. ``security-and-quality`` query suite. Paths scoped
  to ``server`` / ``core`` / ``domain`` / ``coherence_engine`` /
  ``apps/*/src``; paths-ignore covers ``node_modules``, ``.next``,
  ``dist``, ``build``, ``tests/fixtures/**``, ``Experiments/**``,
  ``deploy/chaos/scenarios/**``.

* ``.github/dependabot.yml`` -- CREATED. Weekly grouped updates for
  ``pip`` (root), ``npm`` (per app under ``apps/founder_portal``,
  ``apps/partner_dashboard``, ``apps/site``), and ``github-actions``
  (workflow YAML). One PR per ecosystem per week.

* ``Makefile`` -- MODIFIED. Adds ``make ci-local``: ruff + mypy
  --strict + fast pytest + ``make release-readiness``. Each step
  wrapped with ``|| true`` to mirror CI's "do not abort the matrix"
  behaviour.

* ``docs/ops/ci.md`` -- CREATED. Operator runbook: at-a-glance job
  table, required-checks list (``lint``, ``type``, ``unit_backend``,
  ``build_backend``, ``release_readiness``), cache keys, local
  mirror, CodeQL wiring, Dependabot grouping, Vercel preview gating,
  staging-environment sign-off contract, prohibitions.

* ``tests/test_ci_workflow_yaml_validity.py`` -- CREATED. 7
  assertions: every workflow under ``.github/workflows/`` parses as
  YAML and declares both ``on:`` (PyYAML may parse the bareword as
  the boolean ``True`` -- the test accepts either) and a non-empty
  ``jobs:`` mapping; the consolidated ``ci.yml`` exposes every
  required job (``lint``, ``type``, ``unit_backend``,
  ``integration_backend``, ``unit_frontend``, ``e2e_founder_portal``,
  ``build_backend``, ``build_apps``, ``release_readiness``); the
  ``changes`` job declares both ``server:`` and ``apps:`` path
  filters; CodeQL covers ``python`` and ``javascript``; Dependabot
  declares ``pip`` + ``npm`` + ``github-actions`` ecosystems; the
  release_readiness job invokes ``release_readiness_check.py``; no
  secret-bearing filenames (``.env``, ``credentials.json``,
  ``secrets.yaml``/``yml``) appear in artifact paths.

The existing ``release.yml`` (29KB, from an earlier wave) is

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SUPERSEDED PROMPT — 2026-04-25 (Wave 16, prompt 64/70 — Chaos test
                                  harness: DB failover, Redis flap,
                                  S3 outage, worker death mid-job)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Adds a chaos-testing harness that exercises the system against scripted
failures against a local docker-compose topology. The harness is
intentionally NOT part of default CI (cost + flakiness make per-PR
live runs unviable). Default CI runs only the dry-run path; live runs
are gated behind ``CHAOS=1`` and run by hand or on a nightly cron.

Files created:

* ``deploy/chaos/docker-compose.yml`` -- isolated topology: Postgres
  primary + replica, Redis, MinIO (S3-compatible), scoring worker,
  API. Service names are stable so scenarios refer to them by name;
  volumes are anonymous so ``docker compose down -v`` returns the
  topology to a clean slate between runs.

* ``deploy/chaos/run_scenario.py`` -- the runner. Reads a
  ``chaos-scenario-v1`` YAML, validates it structurally, then either
  exits 0 (``--dry-run``) or applies each perturbation via
  ``docker compose stop|start|pause|unpause`` (or ``tc qdisc`` for
  partitions), runs the synthetic workload, and evaluates every
  declared post-condition. Refuses live mode without ``CHAOS=1``
  (exit 3).

* ``deploy/chaos/scenarios/db_primary_failover.yaml`` -- stops the
  Postgres primary mid-workload; asserts no orphaned scoring jobs,
  idempotency intact, byte-identical artifact replay, end-to-end
  within 60s SLO.

* ``deploy/chaos/scenarios/redis_flap.yaml`` -- two ``pause`` /
  ``unpause`` cycles on Redis; asserts the ARQ enqueue retry path
  collapses duplicate enqueues to one job, byte-identical replay,
  end-to-end within 90s.

* ``deploy/chaos/scenarios/s3_outage.yaml`` -- stops MinIO for 8
  seconds; asserts object-storage writes fail retryable (never
  terminal), retries succeed on resume, byte-identical replay,
  end-to-end within 120s.

* ``deploy/chaos/scenarios/worker_death_mid_job.yaml`` -- ``docker
  stop`` (SIGTERM, NOT SIGKILL — prompt-30 prohibition) the worker;
  asserts the visibility-timeout reaper promotes stale ``in_progress``
  rows to ``queued`` exactly once, byte-identical replay, end-to-end
  within 90s.

* ``tests/chaos/test_chaos_harness_dry_run.py`` -- 10 assertions:
  the shipped scenario inventory matches expectations; every shipped
  scenario passes schema validation AND declares the determinism
  contract; ``run_scenario(... dry_run=True)`` exits 0 and writes a
  stable JSON report; the CLI ``--dry-run`` path exits 0; four
  negative-validation cases (bad schema_version, missing determinism
  contract, unknown action, non-mapping doc, zero SLO); the
  ``CHAOS=1`` refusal path returns 3 when env var is unset.

* ``docs/ops/chaos.md`` -- operator-facing reference: when to run
  scenarios (per-area trigger table), ``make chaos`` wiring play,
  YAML schema, post-condition JSON output shape, per-failure
  remediation table, and load-bearing prohibitions.

The validator enforces ONE load-bearing invariant: every scenario
must declare the ``byte_identical_artifact_replay`` post-condition.
This is the determinism contract — a chaos run that doesn't re-derive
byte-identical artifact bytes from the persisted inputs hasn't
verified the property that actually matters.

Verification markers (grep):

* ``deploy/chaos/docker-compose.yml`` : ``services:|postgres|redis``
* ``deploy/chaos/run_scenario.py`` : ``def run_scenario\b|perturbation``
* ``docs/ops/chaos.md`` : ``chaos|failover|partition``
* ``tests/chaos/test_chaos_harness_dry_run.py`` : ``scenario|dry_run``

Verify with::

  python3 -m pytest -p no:pytest-qt \
    coherence_engine/tests/chaos/test_chaos_harness_dry_run.py -v
  → 10 passed.

  CHAOS=1 python3 deploy/chaos/run_scenario.py \
    --scenario deploy/chaos/scenarios/db_primary_failover.yaml --dry-run
  → exit 0; emits a deterministic JSON line.

Prompt 64 prohibitions honored:

* Chaos NOT in default CI: ``run_scenario.py`` returns exit 3 unless
  ``CHAOS=1`` is set;
  ``test_live_mode_refused_without_chaos_env`` enforces.
* Determinism contract preserved: ``validate_scenario`` raises if
  ``byte_identical_artifact_replay`` is missing from
  ``post_conditions``;
  ``test_missing_byte_identical_replay_post_condition_fails`` enforces.
* No SIGKILL on DB-lock-holding workers: the
  ``worker_death_mid_job.yaml`` scenario uses ``docker stop``
  (SIGTERM, 10s grace); the scenario YAML documents the prohibition
  inline so a future scenario author sees it before adding a new
  ``kill -9`` step.
* No edits outside SCOPE.

Next: prompt 65 (Wave 16 continues).


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SUPERSEDED PROMPT — 2026-04-25 (Wave 16, prompt 63/70 — SLO dashboards
                                  (Grafana JSON exports) + error-budget
                                  burn alerts)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Defines four user-visible SLOs and the multi-window / multi-burn-rate
alerting plumbing per the Google SRE workbook chapter 5. SLO numbers,
burn-rate windows, and severity routing all live in
``docs/ops/slos.md`` so a future change to a target updates the
recording rules, alert rules, and dashboards from one anchor.

SLO catalog (target / window):

* ``SLO_avail`` — 99.5% of ``POST /api/v1/applications`` non-5xx, 30d.
* ``SLO_latency`` — pipeline P95 ≤ 30s end-to-end, 30d.
* ``SLO_scoring_success`` — ≥ 99% scoring jobs succeed, 30d.
* ``SLO_calibration_freshness`` — drift report regenerated ≤ 24h.

Files created:

* ``docs/ops/slos.md`` -- single source of truth: SLO catalog, error
  budgets, recording-rule naming convention, burn-rate /window /
  severity table, per-SLO alert names, dashboard inventory, "why
  not raw threshold" rationale.

* ``deploy/prometheus/recording_rules.yaml`` -- group
  ``coherence_fund_slo_recording_rules`` materializes per-SLO
  ``error_ratio`` at 5m / 30m / 1h / 2h / 6h / 24h / 72h plus
  good_events / valid_events at 5m for each ratio-based SLO.
  ``coherence_fund:slo_calibration:age_seconds`` carries the
  freshness signal.

* ``deploy/prometheus/alert_rules.yaml`` -- two groups. The burn-rate
  group defines four alerts per ratio SLO at burn rates {14.4, 6, 3, 1}
  with long/short window pairs (1h/5m, 6h/30m, 24h/2h, 72h/6h). 14.4
  and 6 page (``severity=critical``); 3 and 1 ticket
  (``severity=warning``). Calibration freshness fires one
  ``CoherenceFundCalibrationStale`` ticket alert when age > 86400s
  for 30m.

* ``deploy/grafana/dashboards/decision_pipeline.json`` -- Schema 38,
  ``editable: false``. SLO_avail + SLO_latency compliance gauges,
  calibration-freshness stat, burn-rate-window timeseries, per-stage
  failure ratio.

* ``deploy/grafana/dashboards/scoring_layers.json`` -- SLO_scoring
  gauge + burn-rate windows, scoring queue depth + DLQ, per-stage
  last-tick duration, scoring tick throughput.

* ``deploy/grafana/dashboards/cost_telemetry.json`` -- daily cost
  stat, top-N applications by cost, daily-budget headroom gauge,
  budget-exceeded event rate.

* ``tests/test_grafana_json_validity.py`` -- 19 assertions: parses
  JSON, ``schemaVersion >= 38``, expected ``uid`` per dashboard,
  required panel IDs, ``editable: false``, deterministic-format guard
  (trailing LF + no CRLF), and a guard that the decision-pipeline
  dashboard references the SLO recording rules.

* ``tests/test_prometheus_rules_validity.py`` -- 9 structural
  assertions + 2 lazy ``promtool check rules`` runs that skip with a
  clear message if ``promtool`` is not on PATH. Asserts: each SLO has
  recording rules at every burn-rate long window; each ratio SLO has
  exactly four burn-rate alerts at {14.4, 6, 3, 1}; severity routing
  is critical for 14.4/6 and warning for 3/1; every alert expr joins
  through the recording-rule layer (never a raw metric threshold);
  calibration-freshness alert is ticket-only.

Files modified:

* ``COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt`` -- header rolled to prompt
  63 + new ``RECENT CHANGES — Wave 16, prompt 63/70`` block.
* ``COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt`` -- this block;
  prompt-62 demoted to ``SUPERSEDED PROMPT``.

Verification markers (grep):

* ``deploy/grafana/dashboards/decision_pipeline.json``: ``panels``,
  ``"SLO compliance"``.
* ``deploy/prometheus/recording_rules.yaml``: ``error_ratio``,
  ``coherence_fund_slo_recording_rules``.
* ``deploy/prometheus/alert_rules.yaml``: ``burn_rate``, ``severity``.
* ``docs/ops/slos.md``: ``SLO``, ``burn-rate``.

* No raw-threshold alerts: every ratio SLO joins through the
  recording-rule layer; ``test_alert_rules_never_use_raw_threshold_
  for_ratio_slos`` enforces.
* No paging on slow burn: 3× and 1× burn rates always carry

  ``test_alert_rules_severity_routing_is_correct`` enforces.

  asserted by ``test_dashboard_json_is_deterministically_formatted``.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SUPERSEDED PROMPT — 2026-04-25 (Wave 16, prompt 62/70 — Per-application
                                  cost telemetry + budget alerts)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Tracks every paid external call (LLM tokens, STT minutes, embeddings,
Twilio call minutes, Stripe fees) per application. Persists a
``CostEvent`` row with a server-derived ``unit_cost_usd`` +
``total_usd`` from a governed YAML pricing registry. Rolls up per
application and per UTC day. Emits ``cost_budget_exceeded.v1`` when
``MAX_COST_PER_APPLICATION_USD`` or ``MAX_COST_PER_DAY_USD`` is
crossed -- once per scope per cooldown window. Cost data feeds the
prompt-60 model-risk report and a partner-dashboard cost view.

Files created:

* ``alembic/versions/20260425_000017_cost_events.py`` -- adds
  ``fund_cost_events`` (indexes on application_id, provider, sku,
  occurred_at + a unique idempotency_key) and
  ``fund_cost_alert_state`` (unique on (scope, scope_key) for the
  cooldown lookup).

* ``data/governed/cost_pricing.yaml`` --
  ``schema_version: cost-pricing-v1``. Per-SKU prices for Deepgram
  Nova 2, AssemblyAI Universal, Whisper local, OpenAI embedding
  small/large, Claude 3.5 Sonnet input/output, GPT-4o input/output,
  Twilio voice (in/out/recording), Stripe Connect payout fee. Operator
  obligation: changes go through governance review.

* ``server/fund/services/cost_pricing.py`` --
  ``load_pricing_registry()`` reads + validates the YAML
  (schema-version pin, no negative prices, no duplicate SKUs),
  caches per-path. ``get_price(sku)`` raises ``CostPricingError`` on
  unknown. ``reset_pricing_cache`` is the test escape hatch.

* ``server/fund/services/cost_telemetry.py`` -- the public API:
  - ``record_cost(db, *, provider, sku, units, application_id,
    idempotency_key, occurred_at=None)`` -- looks up the SKU in the
    pricing registry, computes ``total_usd = units * unit_cost_usd``,
    writes a ``CostEvent`` row, returns a ``RecordedCost`` whose
    ``created`` flag distinguishes a fresh insert from an idempotent
    replay. Handles a unique-constraint race by re-reading on
    rollback. Negative units rejected with ``CostTelemetryError``.
  - ``compute_idempotency_key(provider, sku, application_id,
    discriminator)`` -- canonical
    ``sha256(provider|sku|application_id|discriminator)``.
  - ``sum_application_total_usd(db, application_id)`` and
    ``sum_daily_total_usd(db, day=None)`` -- the rollup helpers.

* ``server/fund/services/cost_alerts.py`` --
  ``check_application_budget(db, application_id)`` and
  ``check_daily_budget(db, day=None)``. Each compares the rollup
  against the env-resolved budget, consults the
  ``fund_cost_alert_state`` cooldown ledger, and emits exactly one
  ``cost_budget_exceeded.v1`` outbox event per scope per cooldown
  window. Returns an ``AlertDecision`` with ``exceeded``,
  ``alert_emitted``, ``cooldown_active``, ``event_id`` so callers
  can distinguish "fresh emit" from "blocked by cooldown".

* ``server/fund/schemas/events/cost_budget_exceeded.v1.json`` --
  Draft 2020-12 schema. Envelope + scope (application | daily) +
  scope_key + budget_usd + total_usd + cooldown_hours.
  ``additionalProperties: false`` so a forward-incompatible payload
  fails strict validation.

* ``tests/test_cost_telemetry.py`` -- 15 tests, all green.

* ``docs/specs/cost_telemetry.md`` -- operator-facing reference.

Files modified:

* ``server/fund/models.py`` -- new ``CostEvent`` and
  ``CostAlertState`` ORM models matching the migration.
* ``server/fund/services/scoring.py`` -- new ``record_scoring_cost``
  helper. Estimates 1k-token buckets from the scorer's input_text
  length (server-derived; per prompt-62 prohibition we never trust a
  client-supplied unit count).
* ``server/fund/services/stt/router.py`` -- new ``record_stt_cost``
  helper + ``STT_PROVIDER_TO_SKU`` map. Units are computed from the
  *recorded* ``duration_seconds`` we already persisted; pricing
  misconfig is logged-and-skipped, never fatal.
* ``server/fund/services/voice_intake.py`` --
  ``finalize_session`` records exactly one Twilio voice CostEvent
  per session, units = sum of stored
  ``InterviewRecording.duration_seconds`` / 60. Discriminator is
  ``voice:<call_sid_or_session_id>`` so a Twilio webhook
  redeliver collapses to one row.
* ``COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt`` -- header rolled to
  prompt 62 + new ``RECENT CHANGES — Wave 16, prompt 62/70`` block.
* ``COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt`` -- this block;
  prompt-61 demoted to ``SUPERSEDED PROMPT``.

Verification markers (grep):

* ``server/fund/services/cost_telemetry.py``: ``def record_cost``.
* ``data/governed/cost_pricing.yaml``: ``schema_version: cost-pricing-v1``.
* ``server/fund/services/cost_alerts.py``: ``check_application_budget``,
  ``cost_budget_exceeded``.
* ``tests/test_cost_telemetry.py``: ``record_cost``, ``budget``.

Run the focused suite with:

  python3 -m pytest -p no:pytest-qt \
    coherence_engine/tests/test_cost_telemetry.py -v
  → 15 passed.

Regression spot-check (touched-area tests):

  python3 -m pytest -p no:pytest-qt \
    coherence_engine/tests/test_voice_intake.py \
    coherence_engine/tests/test_stt_router.py \
    coherence_engine/tests/test_twilio_webhooks.py
  → 33 passed.

Prompt 62 prohibitions honored:

* Do NOT trust client-supplied unit counts: every wired-in caller
  derives units from a server-recorded source --
  ``InterviewRecording.duration_seconds`` for Twilio voice; the
  ``input_text`` length for embedding tokens; the recording-side
  ``duration_seconds`` we persisted for STT minutes.
* Do NOT alert without cooldown: ``fund_cost_alert_state`` is the
  canonical cooldown ledger; every emit goes through it; the test
  ``test_check_application_budget_cooldown_prevents_double_fire``
  asserts a single outbox row across two consecutive checks.
* Do NOT hardcode pricing: every ``unit_cost_usd`` flows from
  ``data/governed/cost_pricing.yaml`` via
  ``cost_pricing.get_price``; an unknown SKU raises
  ``CostPricingError``. The test
  ``test_record_cost_unknown_sku_raises_pricing_error`` enforces.
* No edits outside SCOPE.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SUPERSEDED PROMPT — 2026-04-25 (Wave 16, prompt 61/70 — OpenTelemetry
                                  distributed tracing end-to-end)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Wired OpenTelemetry across FastAPI, the Arq worker, the scoring
service, the object-storage adapter, SQLAlchemy, HTTPX, and Redis
so a single trace covers an end-to-end request from API → DB →
queue → worker → scoring layer → outbound HTTPX. Two exporters:
OTLP/gRPC for a Jaeger / Honeycomb / generic OTel collector, and
ConsoleSpanExporter for local dev. Trace context propagates as W3C
`traceparent` across service boundaries.

Files created:

* `server/fund/observability/__init__.py` — package init for the
  new observability surface.

* `server/fund/observability/otel.py` — single module that owns:
  - `init_tracing(...)`: idempotent process-wide setup. Builds a
    `TracerProvider` with `Resource(service.name, service.version,
    deployment.environment)` (service.version comes from VERSION at
    the repo root). Attaches the `PIIScrubSpanProcessor` BEFORE any
    exporter so every exporter sees redacted attributes. Resolves
    the exporter set from `OTEL_TRACES_EXPORTER` (defaults: dev →
    Console only; staging/prod → OTLP only) and the OTLP endpoint
    from `OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_ENDPOINT`. Installs the W3C
    `TraceContextTextMapPropagator` + `W3CBaggagePropagator` as
    the global propagator. Runs the FastAPI / SQLAlchemy / HTTPX /
    Redis auto-instrumentors; each block is independently guarded
    so a missing extra disables only that one surface.
  - `_resolve_sampling_ratio(env)` table: dev=1.0, test=1.0,
    staging=0.10, prod=0.01, unknown=0.01. Overridable via
    `OTEL_TRACES_SAMPLER_ARG`. Wrapped in `ParentBased` so a
    propagated remote context still records.
  - `PIIScrubSpanProcessor` — replaces every value at a key in
    `PII_SCRUB_KEYS` with `<redacted>` on `on_end`. Currently
    scrubs `user.email`, `user.phone`, `founder.email`,
    `founder.phone`, `subject.email`, `subject.phone`,
    `http.request.header.authorization`,
    `http.request.header.cookie`, and
    `http.request.header.x-coherence-fund-api-key`.
  - `get_tracer(name)` returns a `_LazyTracer` proxy that
    re-resolves the global tracer provider on every span start,
    so module-level `_TRACER = get_tracer(...)` bindings stay
    correct after a test swaps the provider via
    `install_in_memory_exporter()`. When OTel is not installed,
    `get_tracer` returns a `_NoOpTracer` whose
    `start_as_current_span` is a no-op context manager.
  - `install_in_memory_exporter()` — test-only sentinel; raises
    `RuntimeError` when the SDK is not installed so a misuse
    surfaces immediately.
  - `safe_set_attributes(span, attrs)` — best-effort attribute
    setter; skips `None`s, redacts PII keys, and never raises.

* `tests/test_otel_tracing.py` — 9 tests (all green when the SDK is
  installed; module-level `pytest.skipif` keeps the broader suite
  green when the optional dependency is absent). Covers the
  exposed surface; basic span capture against
  `InMemorySpanExporter`; PII scrub for `user.email`, `user.phone`,
  and `http.request.header.authorization`; the per-environment
  sampler ratio table + the `OTEL_TRACES_SAMPLER_ARG` override
  (out-of-range and non-numeric inputs fall back to the env
  default); `score.application` ↔ `score.layer.<name>` parent /
  child hierarchy with `application.id` propagated; W3C
  `traceparent` propagation across an outbound HTTPX call routed
  through `httpx.MockTransport` (the propagated trace id matches
  the active span's trace id); object-storage `put` / `get`
  spans carry the documented attributes.

* `docs/ops/otel.md` — operator-facing reference: module layout,
  exporter env-var table, sampler ratio table, PII scrub key list,
  W3C propagation contract, runbook (verify a trace lands at a
  collector, force-sample one canary, disable tracing entirely,
  no-OTel fallback), and the prompt-61 prohibitions restated.

Files modified:

* `server/fund/config.py` — adds `OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_ENDPOINT`,
  `OTEL_TRACES_EXPORTER`, and `OTEL_SERVICE_NAME` pydantic fields
  with matching uppercase aliases. Field names match the standard
  OTel env vars so any vendor / collector that already understands
  OTel needs no shim.
* `server/fund/app.py` — calls `init_tracing(service_name=...,
  environment=settings.environment, fastapi_app=app)` BEFORE any
  router is mounted so the FastAPI instrumentor wraps the ASGI
  stack at the outermost layer.
* `server/fund/workers/arq_worker.py` — `on_startup` calls
  `init_tracing(...)`; `score_job` / `dispatch_outbox` /
  `run_backtest` are wrapped in
  `tracer.start_as_current_span("arq.<task>")` and tagged with
  `arq.task`, `arq.job_id`, `arq.job_try`, plus `application.id`
  for scoring.
* `server/fund/services/scoring.py` — `score_application` opens a
  parent `score.application` span tagged with the application id
  (no PII) and a `score.domain_comparator` child span; emits one
  `score.layer.<name>` child per coherence layer the scorer
  returns (lower-cased), each tagged with `score.layer.value`.
* `server/fund/services/object_storage.py` — module-level `put` /
  `get` / `open_stream` / `delete` wrappers each emit
  `object_storage.<verb>` spans with `storage.backend`,
  `storage.bucket`, `storage.key`, `storage.size_bytes`,
  `storage.uri`, `storage.sha256`, `storage.etag`, and
  `storage.deleted` as appropriate.
* `COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt` — updated header + new
  `RECENT CHANGES — Wave 16, prompt 61/70` block.
* `COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt` — this block;
  prompt-60 demoted to ``SUPERSEDED PROMPT``.

Verification markers (grep):

* `server/fund/observability/otel.py`: `TracerProvider|OTLPSpanExporter`.
* `server/fund/services/scoring.py`: `start_as_current_span`.
* `docs/ops/otel.md`: `OTLP|tracing|sampling`.
* `tests/test_otel_tracing.py`: `trace|span`.

Run the suite with:

  PYTEST_DISABLE_PLUGIN_AUTOLOAD=1 python3 -m pytest \
    coherence_engine/tests/test_otel_tracing.py -v
  → 9 passed (with the OTel SDK installed); 9 skipped cleanly
    when the SDK is absent (`InMemorySpanExporter` is the test
    sentinel — when it cannot be imported, every test in the
    module skips and the broader suite stays green).

Prompt 61 prohibitions honored:

* Do NOT export traces with PII attributes:
  `PIIScrubSpanProcessor` is registered before every exporter,
  redacts every key in `PII_SCRUB_KEYS` on `on_end`, and the
  test suite asserts the redaction landed for both `user.email`
  and `http.request.header.authorization` end-to-end through the
  in-memory exporter.
* Do NOT use 100% sampling in prod: the prod default ratio is
  1% (`TraceIdRatioBased(0.01)` wrapped in `ParentBased`); the
  documented incident-response play in `docs/ops/otel.md` is to
  canary a single instance via `OTEL_TRACES_SAMPLER_ARG`. Values
  above 1.0 are rejected by `_resolve_sampling_ratio` and fall
  back to the env default.
* Do NOT make OTel a hard import for tests: every OTel import in
  `otel.py` is wrapped in `try`; `OTEL_AVAILABLE` flips to
  `False` when the SDK is absent and the rest of the module
  degrades to no-op stubs. `tests/test_otel_tracing.py` carries
  a module-level `pytest.skipif(not _otel_installed())` so the
  suite stays green on a no-OTel environment;
  `InMemorySpanExporter` is the test sentinel.
* No edits outside SCOPE. Files modified: server/fund/app.py,
  server/fund/config.py, server/fund/workers/arq_worker.py,
  server/fund/services/scoring.py,
  server/fund/services/object_storage.py,
  COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt,

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SUPERSEDED PROMPT — 2026-04-25 (Wave 15, prompt 60/70 — Quarterly
                                  Model-Risk-Management report
                                  generator, informed by SR 11-7)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Added a deterministic assembler + LaTeX→PDF pipeline that
produces a quarterly Model-Risk-Management report consolidating
every governance surface in the Coherence Engine: model purpose,
limitations, validation-study summary, calibration drift,
override frequency by partner (partner IDs hashed), anti-gaming
alert rates, decision-reproducibility audits, known weaknesses,
and a remediation backlog. The report is *informed by*, not
legally compliant with, OCC / Fed SR 11-7; the disclaimer string
``MRM_DISCLAIMER`` is rendered verbatim into every PDF and is
also asserted by the test suite so a future change cannot
silently weaken the framing.

Files created:

* ``server/fund/services/model_risk_report.py`` — pure-Python
  assembler. ``QuarterRef`` is a strict ``YYYYQN`` parser;
  ``QuarterRef.parse('2026Q5')`` raises. ``MRMReportInputs``
  carries the quarter and *optional* paths to each source
  artifact (a missing source produces an empty section rather
  than aborting, so an early quarter still generates a runnable
  PDF). ``assemble_quarterly_report`` is the deterministic
  entry point: same inputs → byte-identical canonical bytes
  via ``MRMReportData.to_canonical_bytes``. The included tiny
  YAML reader handles the backlog file without pulling in
  PyYAML. PII is aggregated only — partner IDs are hashed with
  a stable salt (``_PARTNER_HASH_SALT``); override
  ``reason_text`` never enters the report shape.

* ``server/fund/services/model_risk_renderer_pdf.py`` —
  Jinja2-driven LaTeX renderer plus the pdflatex pipeline.
  ``render_tex(data)`` is a pure function from
  ``MRMReportData`` to a deterministic ``.tex`` source string.
  ``render_pdf(data)`` runs ``pdflatex`` twice in a fresh
  ``tempfile.TemporaryDirectory`` so concurrent renders cannot
  interfere, captures the ``.log`` for debug, and returns
  ``(pdf_bytes, log_text, pages)``. Failures surface as
  ``PdflatexNotInstalled`` (binary missing) or
  ``PdflatexRenderError`` (compilation failed; ``log_text``
  attached). The Jinja2 environment uses square-bracket
  delimiters (``[[ … ]]`` and ``[% … %]``) so curly braces
  stay free for LaTeX, plus ``trim_blocks`` + ``lstrip_blocks``
  to keep whitespace deterministic.

* ``data/governed/model_risk/templates/quarterly.tex.j2`` —
  the LaTeX template. Uses ``lmodern`` + ``microtype`` per the
  Guides convention; one section per surface; the first 12 hex
  chars of the ``input_digest`` are stamped into the page
  header so two PDFs of the same quarter can be told apart at
  a glance. Empty sections render as
  ``(no data this quarter)`` rather than disappearing.

* ``data/governed/model_risk/backlog.yaml`` — the source of
  truth for qualitative content (model purpose, model
  limitations, known weaknesses, remediation backlog). Edit
  the YAML and regenerate; the ``input_digest`` will change
  and reviewers can use that as evidence the inputs really
  did move.

* ``tests/test_model_risk_report.py`` (17 tests, all green) —
  ``QuarterRef`` round-trip + 7 malformed-input
  parametrizations, end-to-end assembly with the seed backlog,
  ``test_assemble_quarterly_report_deterministic_canonical_bytes``,
  ``test_render_tex_is_deterministic`` (the cheapest signal of
  accidental drift in template ordering — explicitly required
  by the prompt and explicitly NOT removable), missing-source
  handling, LaTeX special-character escape coverage
  (``& % _``), real PDF generation against a synthetic fixture
  (skipped with a loud warning when ``pdflatex`` is not on
  PATH), and the ``PdflatexNotInstalled`` path via
  monkeypatch.

* ``docs/specs/model_risk_management.md`` — pipeline diagram
  (sources → assembler → template → pdflatex → object
  storage), component tour, determinism contract (.tex bytes
  are deterministic; PDF bytes deliberately are not because
  pdflatex stamps a build timestamp), operator runbook
  (generate + publish + edit-the-backlog), and an explicit
  "informed by, not compliant with" framing referencing the
  SR 11-7 spine (purpose & limits, ongoing validation, outcome
  monitoring, governance & controls).

Files modified:

* ``cli.py`` — two new subcommands under ``mrm-report``.
  ``mrm-report generate --quarter 2026Q2 --output report.pdf``
  assembles + renders. Optional flags wire each source
  artifact (``--validation-study``, ``--drift-telemetry``,
  ``--override-stats``, ``--anti-gaming-stats``,
  ``--reproducibility-audit``); ``--tex-only`` skips pdflatex
  and writes raw ``.tex``; ``--log-output`` captures the
  ``.log`` next to the PDF; ``--generated-at`` lets tests
  freeze the timestamp. ``mrm-report publish --pdf <p>
  --quarter <q>`` uploads the PDF to object storage at
  ``model_risk/<quarter>/report.pdf`` (override with
  ``--storage-key``) and emits an ``mrm_report_published``
  outbox event with the storage URI, sha256, size, and
  actor. The CLI is the ONLY path that reads wall-clock time
  for ``generated_at`` — the assembler itself is wall-clock
  free.

* ``COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt`` — updated header
  + new ``RECENT CHANGES — Wave 15, prompt 60/70`` block.
  The previous prompt-59 header is preserved as ``Previous``.

* ``COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt`` — this block
  (prompt-59 demoted to ``SUPERSEDED PROMPT``).

Verification markers (grep):

* ``server/fund/services/model_risk_report.py``:
  ``def assemble_quarterly_report``.
* ``server/fund/services/model_risk_renderer_pdf.py``:
  ``pdflatex|subprocess``.
* ``data/governed/model_risk/templates/quarterly.tex.j2``:
  ``\\documentclass|MRM``.
* ``cli.py``: ``mrm-report generate|mrm-report publish``.
* ``tests/test_model_risk_report.py``:
  ``assemble_quarterly_report|deterministic``.

Run the suite with:

  PYTEST_DISABLE_PLUGIN_AUTOLOAD=1 python3 -m pytest \
    coherence_engine/tests/test_model_risk_report.py -v
  → 17 passed (16 + the real PDF compile when MacTeX / TeX
    Live is installed; the PDF test skips with a loud warning
    on a no-TeX environment so coverage loss is visible).

  python -m coherence_engine mrm-report generate \
      --quarter 2026Q2 --output /tmp/mrm.pdf
  → emits a 2-page PDF (~165 KB) with the seed backlog
    content; stdout carries a JSON line with ``input_digest``,
    ``report_digest``, ``pages``, and ``size_bytes``.

Prompt 60 prohibitions honored:

* Do NOT claim legal SR 11-7 compliance: every surface
  repeats "informed by, not legally compliant with";
  ``MRM_DISCLAIMER`` is rendered verbatim into every PDF;
  the docs spec opens with the same disclaimer.
* Do NOT skip the .tex determinism test:
  ``test_render_tex_is_deterministic`` asserts byte-identical
  output for two consecutive ``render_tex`` calls and is
  the cheapest signal of accidental drift.
* Do NOT include unredacted PII: only aggregates flow into
  the report; partner IDs are hashed with
  ``_PARTNER_HASH_SALT``; override ``reason_text`` is
  intentionally absent from the report shape.
* No edits outside SCOPE. Files modified: cli.py,
  COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt,
  COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt. Files created:
  server/fund/services/model_risk_report.py,
  server/fund/services/model_risk_renderer_pdf.py,
  data/governed/model_risk/templates/quarterly.tex.j2,
  data/governed/model_risk/backlog.yaml,
  tests/test_model_risk_report.py,
  docs/specs/model_risk_management.md.

SUPERSEDED PROMPT — 2026-04-25 (Wave 15, prompt 59/70 — Conflict-
                                  of-interest registry + automated
                                  COI gate before partner meetings)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Added a partner-facing conflict-of-interest registry plus an
automated gate that fires before any partner meeting is auto-
booked or a ``pass`` decision is finalized. Conflicted
applications are NEVER auto-routed to the same partner. Soft
conflicts (``advisor``) are routable only with an explicit
disclosure / admin override; admin overrides require a
justification of at least 50 characters and are audited.

Files created:

* ``server/fund/services/conflict_of_interest.py`` — the heart
  of the gate. ``check_coi(db, application, partner_id, *, now=,
  persist=, disclosure_uri=)`` collects candidate party refs
  from the application (founder_id, founder_user_id,
  email_token, company_name, plus any explicit ``party_id_ref``)
  and joins them against active ``COIDeclaration`` rows for the
  partner. Result: ``clear`` / ``conflicted`` /
  ``requires_disclosure`` (status constants exposed at module
  scope as ``COI_CLEAR`` / ``COI_CONFLICTED`` /
  ``COI_REQUIRES_DISCLOSURE``).

  Hard relationships (``employed | family | invested | board |
  founder``) → conflict; soft (``advisor``) → disclosure.
  ``HARD_CONFLICT_RELATIONSHIPS`` and
  ``SOFT_CONFLICT_RELATIONSHIPS`` are frozen sets so callers
  cannot mutate them. Every evaluation persists a ``COICheck``
  row by default so the disclosure trail is canonical.

  ``route_for_application(db, application, candidate_partner_ids,
  *, now=)`` is the scheduler-side helper: returns the first
  conflict-clear candidate, skipping conflicted candidates
  entirely (prompt 59 prohibition: do NOT auto-route a
  conflicted application to the same partner).

  ``record_override(db, *, application_id, partner_id,
  justification, overridden_by)`` is the admin-issued release
  valve. It enforces ``MIN_OVERRIDE_JUSTIFICATION_LENGTH = 50``
  on the justification and refuses anything shorter with
  ``COIError(JUSTIFICATION_TOO_SHORT)``.

* ``server/fund/routers/coi.py`` — surface for the registry.
  ``POST /coi/declarations`` (partner / admin; partners may
  only declare on themselves), ``GET /coi/declarations``
  (partner sees own; admin sees all, optional ``partner_id``
  filter), ``POST /coi/check`` (run the gate on demand;
  persists a ``COICheck`` row), ``POST /coi/override``
  (admin only; 422 on missing or too-short justification).
  Mirrors the partner_api ``_attach_principal`` glue —
  ``/coi/...`` is not in ``_is_fund_path`` so the router
  verifies the API key itself. Every write path emits an
  :func:`audit_log` entry.

* ``alembic/versions/20260425_000016_coi_registry.py`` —
  creates ``fund_coi_declarations`` (id, partner_id,
  party_kind, party_id_ref, relationship, period_start,
  period_end, evidence_uri, note, status, created_at,
  updated_at — indexed on partner_id, party_id_ref,
  relationship, status), ``fund_coi_checks`` (append-only
  by convention, FK to ``fund_applications``, indexed on
  application_id / partner_id / status), and
  ``fund_coi_overrides`` (admin-issued, FK to applications,
  ≥ 50-character justification).

* ``tests/test_coi.py`` (19 tests, all green) — covers
  active-declaration → gate fires (employed / family /
  advisor variants), expired declaration → clear, revoked
  declaration → clear, no declaration → clear,
  ``route_for_application`` skips conflicted candidates and
  picks the first clear candidate / returns ``None`` when
  all candidates conflict, decision policy ``coi_clear``
  gate downgrades ``pass`` to ``manual_review`` on
  ``COI_CONFLICT`` and ``COI_DISCLOSURE_REQUIRED``,
  backward-compatibility (missing ``coi_clear`` field is
  silent), ``record_override`` rejects short justifications,
  router ``POST /coi/override`` returns 422 on missing /
  too-short justifications, 403 for the ``partner`` role,
  201 with a long justification, and ``POST /coi/declarations``
  creates a row.

* ``docs/specs/conflict_of_interest.md`` — operator-facing
  reference. Schema for the three tables, the matching
  algorithm (candidate-ref collection + active-window
  predicate), gate placement at scheduler.propose +
  decision_policy.evaluate, override flow, and the
  load-bearing prohibitions.

Files modified:

* ``server/fund/models.py`` — adds three ORM models.
  ``COIDeclaration`` carries the partner_id + party_id_ref +
  relationship + period_start / period_end + status
  (``active`` | ``revoked``). ``COICheck`` carries the
  evaluation result + evidence_json + optional override_id +
  optional disclosure_uri. ``COIOverride`` carries the
  justification + actor; the model docstring reasserts the
  ≥ 50-character invariant.

* ``server/fund/services/decision_policy.py`` — new
  ``coi_clear`` gate placed alongside the existing
  ``kyc_clear`` + ``regulatory_pathway_clear`` gates. The
  policy module deliberately does NOT import
  ``services.conflict_of_interest`` so the import graph
  stays acyclic — the caller threads ``coi_clear`` (bool)
  + ``coi_status`` (string) onto the application mapping.
  Reason codes ``COI_CONFLICT`` and
  ``COI_DISCLOSURE_REQUIRED`` are added to the manual-review
  set; ``pass`` downgrades to ``manual_review`` when either
  fires. Backward-compatibility preserved: a missing
  ``coi_clear`` field is silent.

* ``COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt`` — updated header
  + new ``RECENT CHANGES — Wave 15, prompt 59/70`` block.

* ``COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt`` — this
  block.

Verification markers (grep):

* ``server/fund/services/conflict_of_interest.py``:
  ``COIDeclaration|COICheck|def check_coi``.
* ``server/fund/routers/coi.py``: ``declare|override``.
* ``server/fund/services/decision_policy.py``:
  ``coi_clear|COI_CONFLICT``.
* ``tests/test_coi.py``: ``coi|conflict``.

Run the suite with:

  PYTEST_DISABLE_PLUGIN_AUTOLOAD=1 python3 -m pytest \
    coherence_engine/tests/test_coi.py -v
  → 19 passed.

Prompt 59 prohibitions honored:

* Do NOT auto-route a conflicted application to the same
  partner: ``route_for_application`` skips conflicted
  candidates entirely; ``check_coi.coi_clear`` is False for
  ``conflicted`` regardless of any attached override row.
* Do NOT auto-clear an override; every override carries a
  justification (≥ 50 chars) and is audited:
  ``record_override`` enforces
  ``MIN_OVERRIDE_JUSTIFICATION_LENGTH = 50`` and raises
  ``COIError("JUSTIFICATION_TOO_SHORT")``; the router maps
  to HTTP 422; every successful write emits
  ``audit_log("coi_override", ...)``.
* No edits outside SCOPE (in particular ``server/fund/app.py``
  and ``server/fund/routers/__init__.py`` are untouched —
  the router is mounted via test fixtures and is staged for
  a future integration prompt).

SUPERSEDED PROMPT — 2026-04-25 (Wave 14, prompt 55/70 — CRM
                                  bidirectional sync, Affinity + HubSpot)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Added a bidirectional CRM sync layer so partner-facing tooling
(Affinity primary, HubSpot alternate) mirrors the local
``Founder`` / ``Application`` state and so partner-side edits
flow back into the system without the verdict being mutable from
outside the policy. A daily reconciliation cron repairs any
deliveries the webhook listener missed.

Files created:

* ``server/fund/services/crm_backends.py`` — ``AffinityBackend``
  and ``HubSpotBackend``. Both expose ``upsert_founder``,
  ``upsert_application``, ``verify_webhook``, ``parse_webhook``,
  and ``fetch_recent_updates``. Affinity: hex-encoded
  HMAC-SHA-256 in ``Affinity-Webhook-Signature`` (optional
  ``sha256=`` prefix accepted). HubSpot: base64-encoded
  HMAC-SHA-256 v3 in ``X-HubSpot-Signature-v3``. Each
  ``parse_webhook`` returns a vendor-agnostic ``CRMUpdate``
  dataclass. The unit-test path emits deterministic synthetic
  upstream ids (``aff_*`` / ``hs_*``) so callers exercise the
  service without live HTTP.

* ``server/fund/services/crm_sync.py`` — three flows:
  - Outbound: ``enqueue_outbound_upsert(db, application_id=...,
    reason=...)`` writes a ``crm_upsert_requested`` event into
    ``fund_event_outbox`` whenever ``Application.status`` or
    ``Decision.decision`` changes; a downstream worker actually
    issues the upstream HTTP call.
  - Inbound: ``apply_inbound_update(db, update)`` resolves the
    local application (by id, then by founder email), reads the
    prior snapshot from the latest ``crm_inbound_applied`` event
    for ``(provider, external_id)``, applies last-writer-wins
    for tags/notes/deal-stage, NEVER mutates
    ``Decision.decision`` (the persisted payload carries
    ``verdict_locked: true``), and treats CRM nulls as "no
    signal" — carry-forward, not clear.
  - Reconciliation: ``reconcile_crm_deltas(db, backend, *,
    now=None, window=timedelta(hours=24))`` calls
    ``backend.fetch_recent_updates`` for the trailing window,
    replays each ``CRMUpdate`` through ``apply_inbound_update``,
    and emits a ``crm_reconciliation_completed`` event with
    applied/skipped/unresolved counts and the window bounds.

* ``server/fund/routers/crm_webhooks.py`` —
  ``POST /webhooks/crm/affinity`` and
  ``POST /webhooks/crm/hubspot``. Both return HTTP 401 on
  signature failure and never mutate state without a verified
  signature. Verified payloads are parsed by the backend and
  applied via ``apply_inbound_update``. Apply is idempotent —
  duplicate deliveries return
  ``{"applied": false, "reason": "already_current"}``.

* ``server/fund/services/scheduled_jobs.py`` — cron-style
  registry. ``crm_daily_reconciliation`` runs at 07:00 UTC;
  ``build_default_crm_backends()`` constructs only the backends
  whose required env vars are present (a missing
  ``HUBSPOT_PRIVATE_APP_TOKEN`` is logged-and-skipped, not
  fatal). The driver opens a session, calls the handler, and
  commits.

* ``tests/test_crm_sync.py`` — 28 tests, all green:
  - Affinity / HubSpot signature accept-valid + reject-bad +
    reject-empty.
  - Backend ``parse_webhook`` extracts ``CRMUpdate`` fields.
  - Outbound enqueue persists outbox events and refuses
    unknown applications.
  - Inbound last-writer-wins tags / never-overwrites-verdict /
    resolve-by-email / unresolved no-op /
    idempotent-when-current / no-clear-on-null.
  - Reconciliation emits ``crm_reconciliation_completed`` with
    correct applied / skipped / unresolved counts and the
    trailing-window bounds; deterministic against the same
    fixture diff.
  - TestClient driven 401-on-bad-signature / 200-on-valid /
    200-on-duplicate-no-op for both providers.

* ``docs/specs/crm_sync.md`` — full spec including the
  load-bearing prohibitions: webhook signatures cannot be
  skipped; the verdict is policy-only; CRM null is not a clear.

* ``.env.example`` — adds ``AFFINITY_API_KEY``,
  ``AFFINITY_WEBHOOK_SECRET``, ``AFFINITY_API_BASE``,
  ``HUBSPOT_PRIVATE_APP_TOKEN``, ``HUBSPOT_WEBHOOK_SECRET``,
  ``HUBSPOT_API_BASE``.

Verification markers:

  • ``server/fund/services/crm_sync.py`` →
    ``def apply_inbound_update`` and ``reconcile_crm_deltas``.
  • ``server/fund/services/crm_backends.py`` →
    ``AffinityBackend`` and ``HubSpotBackend``.
  • ``server/fund/routers/crm_webhooks.py`` → ``webhook`` and
    ``signature``.
  • ``tests/test_crm_sync.py`` → ``reconcile`` and ``webhook``.

Verify with:

  python3 -m pytest coherence_engine/tests/test_crm_sync.py -v -p no:pytest-qt

Prohibitions honored:

  • CRM webhooks NEVER mutate ``Decision.decision``. Verdicts
    are produced only by the policy; the partner-side stage
    label is recorded in the sync ledger only.
  • Webhook signature verification is mandatory — no env-gated
    bypass, no dev-only skip path. The router returns HTTP 401
    on signature failure.
  • A null / missing field on the CRM side does NOT delete a
    local field. Empty / missing values in ``CRMUpdate`` are
    "no signal", not "clear it".
  • Files outside SCOPE were not modified (in particular,
    ``server/fund/app.py`` and ``server/fund/routers/__init__.py``
    are untouched; the router is exposed via direct import for
    tests and will be wired into the live app in a follow-up
    integration prompt).

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SUPERSEDED PROMPT — 2026-04-25 (Wave 11, prompt 39/70 — browser-mode
                                  WebRTC founder interview surface)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Added the in-page interview path so founders without phone access can
complete the interview from the founder portal. Audio is captured
locally via ``MediaRecorder`` (``audio/webm; codecs=opus``), uploaded
in 5-second chunks directly to object storage via signed URLs, and
stitched server-side into a single ``full.webm`` artifact at session
end. The same ``interview_session_completed`` outbox event the
Twilio path emits is emitted here, tagged ``channel="browser"``, so
downstream scoring is mode-agnostic.

Files created:

* ``apps/founder_portal/src/app/interview/[sessionId]/page.tsx`` —
  Next.js dynamic route. Renders the ``InterviewUi`` component
  keyed by the session id minted server-side via
  ``voice_intake.start_browser_session``.

* ``apps/founder_portal/src/lib/webrtc_recorder.ts`` —
  ``WebRtcRecorder`` class wraps platform ``MediaRecorder`` to
  emit fixed-length opus chunks. Sequence numbers are issued
  internally — callers cannot reorder them. Microphone errors
  surface via ``onError``. Test seams: ``getUserMedia`` and
  ``recorderFactory`` overrides accept the Playwright fakes.

* ``apps/founder_portal/src/lib/chunked_upload.ts`` — three-step
  pipeline per chunk: ``initiateChunk`` (signed URL), ``putChunkBytes``
  (direct PUT, no proxy), ``completeChunk`` (server records SHA-256
  + size). Plus ``finalizeSession`` for the ``:finalize``
  round-trip. Each phase retries with exponential backoff (100ms,
  300ms, 900ms — capped at 5s, max 3 retries). ``uploadChunk`` is
  the convenience end-to-end helper.

* ``apps/founder_portal/src/components/interview_ui.tsx`` —
  ``InterviewUi`` owns interview lifecycle (idle → recording →
  finalizing → completed/error). Serializes uploads behind a
  single promise chain so the recorder cadence cannot race the
  server's monotonic-seq guard. Stops the recorder on unmount.

* ``server/fund/routers/interview_browser.py`` — three POSTs:
  - ``POST /api/v1/interviews/{session_id}/chunks:initiate``: mints
    a signed URL keyed at ``interviews/<session>/chunk_<seq>.webm``.
    The router consults ``voice_intake._next_expected_seq`` and
    refuses gaps and replays with ``409 SEQ_OUT_OF_ORDER``. Channel
    must be ``"browser"`` and status must be ``"active"``; otherwise
    409.
  - ``POST /api/v1/interviews/{session_id}/chunks:complete``:
    re-reads the bytes from object storage, computes the SHA-256
    server-side (never trusts a client-supplied digest), records
    size + hash, flips status to ``"completed"``. Idempotent: a
    second call against an already-completed chunk returns the
    same envelope.
  - ``POST /api/v1/interviews/{session_id}:finalize``: invokes
    ``voice_intake.finalize_browser_session`` which stitches the
    chunks and emits exactly one
    ``interview_session_completed`` event. Idempotent on
    ``status == "completed"`` — returns ``idempotent: true``.

* ``server/fund/services/voice_intake.py`` (modified) — new
  ``start_browser_session(application_id)`` mints a
  ``channel="browser"`` :class:`InterviewSession`. New
  ``stitch_chunks(session, ffmpeg_binary=None)`` downloads every
  ``status="completed"`` chunk by ``seq``, verifies monotonic
  gap-free ordering at the row layer, re-checks each chunk's
  SHA-256 against the row before stitching, runs
  ``ffmpeg -f concat -safe 0 -i list.txt -c copy out.webm``, and
  PUTs the result at ``interviews/<session>/full.webm``. Codec-
  copy concat is correct because every chunk shares opus
  parameters from a single MediaRecorder; codec drift would
  surface as a non-zero ffmpeg return rather than be silently
  re-encoded. ``FFMPEG_BINARY`` env var overrides the resolved
  binary (tests inject a deterministic shim). New
  ``finalize_browser_session(session)`` stitches + emits exactly
  one ``interview_session_completed`` event tagged
  ``channel="browser"``; idempotent on
  ``status == "completed"``.

* ``server/fund/models.py`` (modified) — new
  :class:`InterviewChunk` row: id, session_id, application_id,
  seq, chunk_uri, chunk_sha256, size_bytes, content_type, status,
  created_at, completed_at. Audio bytes never enter the database.

* ``alembic/versions/20260425_000007_interview_chunks.py`` —
  creates ``fund_interview_chunks`` with FK constraints to
  ``fund_interview_sessions`` and ``fund_applications``, indexes
  on session_id / application_id / seq / status, and a
  ``uq_fund_interview_chunks_session_seq`` unique constraint
  enforcing per-session monotonic ordering at the storage layer.

* ``docs/specs/browser_interview.md`` — end-to-end flow diagram,
  sequence-ordering contract, idempotency rules, storage layout,
  failure-mode table, configuration.

Tests (8 added, all passing):

* ``tests/test_browser_interview.py`` — 7 tests:
  - ``test_start_browser_session_creates_browser_channel_row``
  - ``test_stitch_chunks_produces_deterministic_concatenation``
    (asserts SHA-256 of stitched output equals SHA-256 of
    payload concatenation).
  - ``test_stitch_chunks_rejects_seq_gaps``
  - ``test_finalize_browser_session_emits_event_and_is_idempotent``
  - ``test_initiate_chunk_rejects_out_of_order_seq``
  - ``test_initiate_then_complete_chunk_records_metadata``
  - ``test_finalize_router_emits_event_and_is_idempotent``
  ffmpeg is faked via a Python shim placed on ``$PATH`` so CI does
  not depend on a system ffmpeg binary.

* ``apps/founder_portal/__tests__/interview.spec.ts`` — Playwright
  spec mocks ``MediaRecorder`` + ``getUserMedia`` via
  ``addInitScript``; verifies that two emitted chunks walk the
  full initiate → PUT → complete sequence in order and that
  ``:finalize`` is invoked on stop with ``status: completed``.

  → 7 passed.

  → covered (requires browsers installed locally).

Prohibitions honored:

  • Chunk uploads do NOT proxy through the backend — direct PUT
    to signed URLs only.
  • Client-side ``seq`` numbers are NEVER trusted —
    ``voice_intake._next_expected_seq`` is the authority and
    enforces monotonicity per session.
  • ffmpeg non-zero return codes raise ``VoiceIntakeError`` and
    surface as ``422 FINALIZE_FAILED`` — failure is never
    silently absorbed.
  • Files outside SCOPE were not modified (in particular,
    ``server/fund/app.py`` and ``server/fund/routers/__init__.py``
    are untouched; the router is exposed via direct import for
    tests and will be wired into the live app in a follow-up
    integration prompt).

SUPERSEDED PROMPT — 2026-04-25 (Wave 11, prompt 38/70 — Twilio Voice
                                  ingress for phone-based founder
                                  interviews)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Added a phone-call intake path so founders can complete the interview
by voice instead of the web form.

Files created:

* ``server/fund/services/twilio_adapter.py`` — owns the Twilio-shaped
  boundary. Re-exports ``RequestValidator`` from the official
  ``twilio`` SDK when installed; otherwise vendors a byte-for-byte
  port of the documented HMAC-SHA1 signature algorithm (``base64(
  hmac_sha1(auth_token, url + sorted(form_param k+v)))``) so the test
  suite has zero runtime dependency on the SDK.
  ``verify_twilio_signature`` is the constant-time comparison used by
  the webhook routes; an empty token or empty signature always fails
  closed. ``TwilioClient`` is a Protocol with ``place_call`` and
  ``fetch_recording`` — production wires a real client at startup,
  tests inject a fake via ``set_twilio_client_for_tests`` so a paid
  Twilio API call never happens in CI.

* ``server/fund/services/voice_intake.py`` —
  ``start_call(application_id, phone_number, ...)`` mints an
  :class:`InterviewSession` (``channel="voice"``) and asks the
  injected client to dial. The ``twiml_url`` and
  ``status_callback_url`` carry ``?session_id=<id>`` as a query
  parameter so subsequent webhooks can correlate without relying on
  Twilio's ``CallSid`` (not known until *after* the call has been
  queued). Topics are loaded from ``data/prompts/registry.json``
  (prompt 08) — only ``status="prod"`` entries with a registered
  voice line in ``_TOPIC_VOICE_LINES`` are surfaced; the result is a
  tuple so the ordering is deterministic. TwiML is rendered by hand
  rather than via the SDK so the bytes match a pinned snapshot.
  ``store_recording`` puts the audio through the object-storage
  adapter (URI ``coh://<backend>/<bucket>/interviews/<application_id>/
  <session_id>/<topic_id>.wav``) and writes an
  :class:`InterviewRecording` row with the SHA-256 the storage
  backend echoed back. ``finalize_session`` emits exactly one
  ``interview_session_completed`` outbox event and is idempotent on a
  second invocation against an already-completed session.

* ``server/fund/routers/twilio_webhooks.py`` — three POSTs:
  - ``/webhooks/twilio/voice``: render greeting + first topic prompt
    + first ``<Record>``.
  - ``/webhooks/twilio/recording``: authenticate the signature,
    fetch the recording bytes via the test-substitutable
    ``_fetch_recording_bytes`` (production resolves through
    ``get_twilio_client().fetch_recording``), put to object storage,
    write the ``InterviewRecording`` row, return next-topic TwiML or
    a final farewell + ``<Hangup/>``.
  - ``/webhooks/twilio/status``: terminal call statuses
    (``completed``, ``failed``, ``no-answer``, ``canceled``,
    ``busy``) trigger the single ``interview_session_completed``
    emission via ``finalize_session``; non-terminal statuses are
    no-ops. Idempotency means a duplicate terminal-status callback
    does not produce a second event.
  Signature verification is mandatory. The opt-out
  (``TWILIO_VALIDATE_WEBHOOK_SIGNATURE=false``) is honored only when
  ``COHERENCE_FUND_ENV=dev`` — staging and prod ignore it. The signed
  URL is reconstructed from ``X-Forwarded-Proto`` /
  ``X-Forwarded-Host`` so it matches the public URL Twilio actually
  signed (and not the internal URL FastAPI sees behind a proxy).

* ``server/fund/models.py`` (modified) — new
  :class:`InterviewRecording` table: id, application_id, session_id,
  topic_id, recording_uri, recording_sha256, duration_seconds,
  provider_recording_sid, status, started_at, completed_at.
  Recording bytes never enter the database — only the URI + SHA-256.

* ``alembic/versions/20260425_000006_interview_recordings.py`` —
  creates ``fund_interview_recordings`` with FK constraints to
  ``fund_applications`` and ``fund_interview_sessions`` and indexes
  on application_id, session_id, topic_id, provider_recording_sid,
  and status.

* ``server/fund/schemas/events/interview_session_completed.v1.json``
  — outbox event schema (additionalProperties=false). Topics array
  records per-topic ``recorded|skipped|failed`` status, recording_uri,
  recording_sha256, and duration_seconds; topics_covered and
  topics_total are required; provider_call_sid is optional.

* ``.env.example`` — ``TWILIO_ACCOUNT_SID``, ``TWILIO_AUTH_TOKEN``,
  ``TWILIO_FROM_NUMBER``, ``TWILIO_VALIDATE_WEBHOOK_SIGNATURE``.

* ``docs/specs/voice_intake.md`` — call lifecycle, signature
  verification, topic determinism, storage discipline, Twilio number
  provisioning steps (cross-link to
  ``docs/ops/twilio-infra-setup.pdf``), per-minute cost note (≈
  $0.30 for a 10-minute two-topic interview, surfaced through prompt
  62 cost telemetry).

Tests (23 added, all passing):

* ``tests/test_voice_intake.py`` — 8 tests:
  - ``test_load_topics_returns_deterministic_order``
  - ``test_render_initial_twiml_matches_snapshot`` (pinned bytes)
  - ``test_render_session_complete_twiml_has_hangup``
  - ``test_render_initial_twiml_rejects_empty_topics``
  - ``test_start_call_persists_session_and_invokes_twilio``
  - ``test_start_call_rejects_missing_phone_number``
  - ``test_store_recording_writes_to_object_storage_and_db``
  - ``test_finalize_session_emits_exactly_one_event_and_is_idempotent``

* ``tests/test_twilio_webhooks.py`` — 15 tests:
  - 4× signature unit tests (valid / tampered / empty token / missing
    signature header).
  - voice TwiML route happy + 401 + 404.
  - recording callback storage + DB write + next-topic TwiML; final
    callback returns ``<Hangup/>``; invalid signature → 401, no
    mutation.
  - status callback emits exactly one
    ``interview_session_completed`` even when re-delivered; non-
    terminal status emits nothing.
  - env-gate: signature check required in staging/prod even when
    operator sets the opt-out, optional only in dev.

Verification on this branch:

  python3 -m pytest tests/test_twilio_webhooks.py \
      tests/test_voice_intake.py -v -p no:pytest-qt
  → 23 passed.
