SUPERSEDED PROMPT — 2026-04-25 (Wave 10, prompt 37/70 — API gateway:
                                  rate limiting, CORS, request signing,
                                  request-ID header)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Built the API gateway middleware stack at ``server/fund/middleware/``
and wired it into the FastAPI app via ``install_gateway_middleware``.
The gateway sits *outside* the existing ``FundSecurityMiddleware``: a
request flows through ``RequestId → CORS → RequestSigning →
RateLimit → FundSecurity → route``. Every layer has its own
``server/fund/middleware/<name>.py`` so it can be unit-tested in
isolation; the package ``__init__`` only stitches them in the right
order.

Files created:

* ``server/fund/middleware/__init__.py`` — exports
  ``install_gateway_middleware`` (the public entry point) plus the
  individual middleware classes for tests.

* ``server/fund/middleware/rate_limit.py`` — token-bucket rate
  limiter. Keyed on the API-key prefix (first 8 chars of
  ``X-API-Key`` / ``Authorization: Bearer …``) when present,
  otherwise on the client IP from ``X-Forwarded-For`` or
  ``request.client.host``. Refill rate is the API-key row's
  ``rate_limit_per_minute`` if it has been resolved on
  ``request.state.api_key`` by an inner dep; otherwise
  ``settings.RATE_LIMIT_DEFAULT`` (env
  ``COHERENCE_FUND_RATE_LIMIT_DEFAULT``, default 120). The limiter
  attempts a Redis Lua-script bucket when ``WORKER_BACKEND=arq`` and
  ``redis`` is importable + reachable; on any Redis hiccup it falls
  back transparently to the process-local
  ``_InProcessRateLimiter``. Denials return 429 with
  ``Retry-After: <int>`` and a JSON body
  ``{"error":"rate_limited","retry_after_seconds":<int>}``. Health,
  ``/docs``, and CORS preflights skip the limiter entirely.

* ``server/fund/middleware/request_signing.py`` — HMAC-SHA-256
  signing on ``/api/v1/internal/*`` only. Headers
  ``X-Coherence-Timestamp`` (RFC 3339 UTC) and
  ``X-Coherence-Signature: v1=<hex>``; canonical string is
  ``f"{ts}\\n{METHOD}\\n{path}\\n{sha256_hex(body)}"`` keyed on
  ``REQUEST_SIGNING_SECRET``. ±300 s skew window
  (``REQUEST_SIGNING_MAX_SKEW_SECONDS``); a bounded LRU
  (``REPLAY_CACHE``, capacity 10 000) rejects re-presentation of
  the same ``(ts, sig)`` pair. Body is replayed back into
  ``request._receive`` after consumption so route handlers can
  re-read it. Denials are logged with the signature truncated to
  ``v1=<first 8 chars>...``; the secret is never logged. SHA-1 /
  MD5 are not accepted — only the ``v1=`` (SHA-256) prefix is
  recognised.

* ``server/fund/middleware/cors.py`` — explicit allow-list from
  ``CORS_ALLOWED_ORIGINS`` (comma-separated). A literal ``*``
  raises ``RuntimeError`` at install time outside the dev
  environment so a misconfigured staging/prod deploy fails
  loudly. Methods: GET/POST/PUT/DELETE/OPTIONS. Allowed headers
  include ``Authorization``, ``Content-Type``, ``X-Request-ID``,
  ``X-Coherence-Signature``, ``X-Coherence-Timestamp``,
  ``X-API-Key``. Exposed: ``X-Request-ID``.

* ``server/fund/middleware/request_id.py`` — reads
  ``X-Request-ID`` from the caller or mints a new one (UUID4 hex
  — UUIDv7 is the eventual goal but the runtime stdlib doesn't
  ship it; uniqueness across a request lifetime is the actual
  invariant we need). The id is stored on ``request.state`` and a
  module-level ``ContextVar`` so a logging filter
  (``RequestIdLogFilter``) can attach it to every record. The
  middleware echoes the id back on every response, including 4xx
  denials produced by deeper layers.

* ``server/fund/config.py`` (modified) — added four fields:
  ``CORS_ALLOWED_ORIGINS`` (comma-separated string),
  ``RATE_LIMIT_DEFAULT`` (int, default 120),
  ``REQUEST_SIGNING_SECRET`` (``SecretStr``, default empty),
  ``REQUEST_SIGNING_MAX_SKEW_SECONDS`` (int, default 300). UPPER
  case property accessors mirror the rest of the config surface.

* ``server/fund/app.py`` (modified) — calls
  ``install_gateway_middleware(app)`` immediately after the
  existing ``FundSecurityMiddleware`` is attached. Because
  Starlette's ``add_middleware`` prepends to the executed stack,
  the request-id layer ends up outermost and security ends up
  innermost — denials at any layer still get a request-id stamp.

Tests (``tests/test_middleware_*.py``, 16 cases, all passing):

* ``test_middleware_rate_limit.py`` — 5 requests against a
  capacity-3 bucket → 3×200, 2×429; 429 carries ``Retry-After``
  and the JSON body shape; distinct API-key prefixes get
  independent buckets; ``/health`` skips the limiter.
* ``test_middleware_request_signing.py`` — valid signature 200,
  tampered body 401, replay-within-window 401, skewed timestamp
  401, public path skip, missing headers 401.
* ``test_middleware_cors.py`` — request-id round-trip (caller-
  supplied vs. minted), preflight allow-listed origin emits
  ``Access-Control-Allow-Origin``, non-allowed origin does not,
  ``*`` outside dev raises at install, ``*`` allowed in dev.

Documentation: ``docs/specs/api_gateway.md`` covers the middleware
order, denial shapes, configuration, and the canonical signature
construction.

Verification on this branch:

  python3 -m pytest tests/test_middleware_rate_limit.py \
      tests/test_middleware_request_signing.py \
      tests/test_middleware_cors.py -v
  → 16 passed.

Pre-existing failures observed in the wider suite during this prompt
(``test_fund_backend.py::test_bootstrap_admin_token_from_secret_manager``
and the ``test_arq_worker`` / ``test_worker_backend_switch`` /
``test_upload_initiate`` / ``test_migration_registry`` /
``test_openapi_and_sdk::test_set_scoring_mode_endpoint_toggles_mode``
failures) reproduce with the prompt-37 changes stashed, so they belong
to earlier in-progress work and are not introduced here.

Built ``apps/site/`` as an Astro 4.16 static project: marketing pages

deployable to Vercel as a separate project from the founder portal
and partner dashboard (the repo-root ``vercel.json`` is reserved for
the FastAPI fund API; ``apps/site/vercel.json`` configures the site
deploy).

Files created:

  Playwright 1.47, TypeScript 5.5.

* ``apps/site/astro.config.mjs`` — static output, integrations: mdx,
  tailwind, sitemap; remark-math + rehype-katex registered for MDX
  and standard markdown; site URL via ``SITE_URL`` env (default
  placeholder). MDX integration is wired to the same plugin chain so

  (``type: 'content'``) with zod schema for title, summary, authors,

* ``apps/site/src/content/research/cosine_paradox.mdx`` — pairwise

  "Householder|reflection|direction" all present.

* ``apps/site/src/content/research/reverse_marxism.mdx`` — reflection

Known local-only quirk: Vite ``import.meta.glob`` cannot enumerate
``src/content/research/*.mdx`` when the absolute project path
contains an apostrophe (the user's local Mac path includes
``Michael's``). CI / Vercel paths do not have apostrophes, so
production builds are unaffected. Workaround documented in
``apps/site/README.md``: copy the directory to ``/tmp`` and build
from there for local development.

    page via ``CaveatBanner.astro``.


SUPERSEDED PROMPT — 2026-04-25 (Wave 10, prompt 35/70 — Partner dashboard
                                  pipeline + decision artifact viewer +
                                  manual override flow)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Built ``apps/partner_dashboard/`` (Next.js 14 App Router) and a new
JSON namespace ``/api/v1/partner/*`` on the FastAPI backend. RBAC is
enforced via ``require_role(("partner", "admin"))`` on every router
endpoint (re-exported from
``server/fund/services/decision_overrides.py``); viewer / analyst
tokens get a structured 403. The legacy HTMX admin (prompt 19) at
``/admin`` is preserved as a fallback per prompt-35 prohibition.

Backend additions:

* ``server/fund/models.py`` — ``DecisionOverride`` ORM entity backing
  partner / admin manual overrides. Indexed on ``application_id``,
  ``override_verdict``, ``reason_code``, ``status``, ``overridden_by``.

* ``alembic/versions/20260425_000005_decision_overrides.py`` — schema
  migration creating ``fund_decision_overrides`` plus the five
  indexes; clean down-migration.

* ``server/fund/services/decision_overrides.py`` — ``DecisionOverride
  Service`` enforces:
    – closed ``reason_code`` enum (``factual_error``,
      ``policy_misalignment``, ``regulatory_constraint``,
      ``manual_diligence``)
    – ``reason_text`` ≥ 40 chars
    – memo (``justification_uri``) required for any pass→reject
      override
    – idempotency on ``(application_id, status="active")`` —
      duplicate writes return the existing row without re-emitting
      events; ``unrevise=True`` is the only way to supersede a prior
      row.
  Every successful write emits a ``decision_overridden.v1`` outbox
  event (``producer="partner_dashboard"``).

* ``server/fund/routers/partner_api.py`` — JSON router with:
    – ``GET /partner/pipeline`` (cursor-paginated; URL-driven
      ``domain`` / ``verdict`` / ``mode`` filters; over-fetch by 1 to
      detect ``has_more``)
    – ``GET /partner/applications/{id}`` (full detail + decision
      artifact + active override)
    – ``POST /partner/applications/{id}/override`` (validates payload,
      stamps audit log, emits event)
    – ``GET /partner/audit`` (read-only audit-log feed)
  Mounted at both ``/partner`` and ``/api/v1/partner`` from
  ``server/fund/app.py``.

Frontend additions (``apps/partner_dashboard/``):

* Mirrors founder-portal scaffolding: Next.js 14, App Router,
  Tailwind, Vitest, Playwright. Port 3002. ESLint
  ``next/core-web-vitals``. ``SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY`` is
  intentionally absent from ``.env.example`` (service-role belongs on
  the backend).

* ``src/lib/supabase.ts`` — SSR cookie wiring; ``isPartnerOrAdmin``
  reads ``user.app_metadata.role``.

* ``src/lib/api_client.ts`` — typed client over the partner namespace;
  ``PartnerApiError`` for envelope-aware error surfacing.

* ``src/lib/pipeline_filter.ts`` — pure URL parser / serializer.
  Closed enums for ``verdict`` / ``mode``; unknown values silently
  degrade to "any"; limit clamped to 100; default-limit omitted from
  serialization for clean links.

* ``src/components/decision_artifact_viewer.tsx`` — collapsible tree
  view of a decision artifact: summary block, coherence-vs-threshold
  bars, optional per-layer score bars, failed-gates / reason-code
  list. Verification markers: ``decision_artifact|per_layer``.

* ``src/app/pipeline/page.tsx`` — server-rendered pivot table. URL-
  driven filters ⇒ refresh + share-links work. Cursor-based
  pagination via ``next_cursor``.

* ``src/app/applications/[id]/page.tsx`` — application detail with the
  artifact viewer, override-status panel, CTA to override page.

* ``src/app/applications/[id]/override/page.tsx`` — server-action
  form. Client-side validation in ``./validate.ts`` (≥40 chars, closed
  reason-code enum, memo required for any reject override). On
  validation / API failure, redirects with ``?error=`` so the form
  re-renders with the human-readable cause; on success, redirects to
  the detail page.

* ``src/app/audit/page.tsx`` — read-only audit feed with action +
  application_id filters.

Tests:

* ``tests/test_decision_overrides.py`` — 14 cases covering service-
  level validation (unknown reason_code, short reason_text,
  pass→reject memo requirement, idempotent duplicate, unrevise +
  supersede, event payload shape) and router-level RBAC (401, 403
  viewer, 201 partner, 201 admin, 400 short reason, 200 idempotent,
  pipeline filter, audit-log emission).

* ``apps/partner_dashboard/__tests__/pipeline.spec.ts`` — Playwright
  spec covering pipeline filter parsing (defaults, known-enum
  acceptance, unknown-value rejection, limit clamp, round-trip
  serialization) and override form validation (reject without memo,
  short reason, complete payload, unknown reason code).

CI:

* ``.github/workflows/partner_dashboard.yml`` — pnpm install + lint +
  ``tsc --noEmit`` + ``next build`` + Vitest + Playwright; secondary

Prohibitions held:

* Legacy HTMX admin at ``/admin`` is preserved untouched as a

* Overrides are blocked without both a closed-enum ``reason_code``

SUPERSEDED — 2026-04-25 (Wave 10, prompt 34/70 — Founder portal
                          application + status flow + transcript upload)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Multi-step apply form (company → product → market → ask → upload) with
``localStorage`` autosave keyed on a UUID draft-id, direct-PUT signed-URL
file upload (deck + supporting), real-time polling of application status
with exponential backoff on errors, and a stage-by-stage status timeline.
Accessibility is gated by axe-core (zero WCAG 2 A/AA violations on every
page).

Backend additions (``server/fund/routers/applications.py``):

* ``POST /api/v1/applications/{id}/uploads:initiate`` — body
  ``{ filename, content_type, size_bytes, kind }``, returns
  ``{ upload_id, upload_url, headers, expires_at, key, uri,
  max_bytes }``. The router dispatches signed-URL minting on the
  active storage backend (S3 ``generate_presigned_url("put_object")``;
  Supabase ``/storage/v1/object/<bucket>/<key>`` with bearer auth;
  local synthetic ``local://upload/...`` URL for in-process tests).
  Validation: filename ``^[A-Za-z0-9._\\- ]{1,255}$``; content_type ∈
  pdf / pptx / ppt / png / jpeg / plain; size_bytes ∈ (0, 25 MiB];
  kind ∈ {deck, supporting}. Founder JWT path checks ownership;
  service-role path retains the existing role gate. Upload state
  persisted in ``IdempotencyRecord`` under namespaced
  ``upload:{application_id}`` endpoint key (no schema migration). The
  intended URI is also stamped onto ``Application.transcript_uri`` for
  the deck slot so a partial upload still leaves a forensic trail.

* ``POST /api/v1/applications/{id}/uploads:complete`` — body
  ``{ upload_id }``. Verifies the object exists in storage
  (``backend.get(uri)``), records the **server-observed** size on the
  upload record (the client-supplied ``size_bytes`` from initiate is
  never trusted as ground truth), and returns the canonical envelope.
  Idempotent: re-calling with the same ``upload_id`` short-circuits to
  the previously-stored response. Returns 409 ``UPLOAD_NOT_FOUND`` if
  the client never PUT.

Frontend additions (``apps/founder_portal/``):

* ``src/components/multi_step_form.tsx`` (NEW) — five steps; per-step
  validation; keyboard-driven (``aria-current="step"`` on the indicator,
  ``aria-invalid``/``aria-describedby`` on every field, ``role="alert"``
  for errors, ``aria-live="polite"`` autosave hint). Draft is keyed on
  a UUID and persisted to ``localStorage`` as a versioned blob with a
  14-day TTL; cleared on successful submit. No PII-bound row from the
  created application is ever written to ``localStorage`` — only the
  in-flight form values.

* ``src/components/file_upload.tsx`` (NEW) — uses ``XMLHttpRequest`` so
  upload progress is observable (fetch() doesn't expose Upload progress
  in browsers as of 2026); ARIA progressbar; disabled-during-upload to
  prevent double-trigger.

* ``src/components/step_indicator.tsx``,
  ``src/components/form_field.tsx``,
  ``src/components/status_timeline.tsx``,
  ``src/components/application_status_view.tsx`` (NEW) — primitives,
  status timeline (Intake → Interview → Scoring → Decision) tone-coded
  with explicit ``sr-only`` labels.

* ``src/lib/upload.ts`` (NEW) — three-step helper:
  ``initiateUpload`` → ``putToSignedUrl`` (direct XHR PUT to the signed
  URL with backend-issued headers; the browser never sees storage
  credentials) → ``completeUpload``. ``UploadError`` distinguishes
  ``initiate`` / ``put`` / ``complete`` failure phases.

* ``src/hooks/use_application_status.ts`` (NEW) — polls every 5 s; on
  error, exponentially backs off (5s → 10s → 20s → 40s, cap 60s) and
  resets to 5 s on the next success. Stops polling on terminal status
  (``decision_pass`` / ``decision_fail`` / ``decision_manual_review`` /
  ``escalated``). Cancellation via ``cancelledRef`` so unmounts during
  in-flight fetches don't leak ``setState`` calls.

* ``src/lib/api_client.ts`` extended with ``getApplication``,
  ``initiateUpload``, ``completeUpload``.

* ``src/app/api/auth/route.ts`` extended with ``upload_initiate``,
  ``upload_complete`` (POST) and ``application_status`` (GET) actions
  over the existing seam.

* ``src/app/apply/page.tsx`` rewritten as a thin shell around
  ``MultiStepApplicationForm``; ``src/app/applications/[id]/page.tsx``
  rewritten to delegate to the polling-driven
  ``ApplicationStatusView``.

Tests:

* ``tests/test_upload_initiate.py`` (NEW) — 7 pytest cases covering
  signed URL + expiry + key prefix; 422 on disallowed content-type or
  oversized payload; ``complete`` finalizes after backend put and
  reports the storage-observed size; ``complete`` is idempotent
  across repeated calls; ``complete`` returns 409 ``UPLOAD_NOT_FOUND``
  if the client never PUT; ``initiate`` against an unknown application
  returns 404.
  Run with ``python3 -m pytest tests/test_upload_initiate.py -v
  -p no:pytest-qt`` → 7 passed.

* ``apps/founder_portal/__tests__/apply_flow.spec.ts`` (NEW) —
  Playwright happy-path: walks all four data steps, submits, uploads
  a deck against a mocked signed URL, and lands on the status page
  where the polled status appears in the timeline.

* ``apps/founder_portal/__tests__/a11y.spec.ts`` (NEW) — axe-core via
  ``@axe-core/playwright`` 4.10.0. Asserts zero WCAG 2 A/AA violations
  on landing, every step of the apply form, and the status page.

Prohibitions held:

* Files are NEVER proxied through the Next.js layer — backend mints
  the signed URL, browser PUTs directly to storage.
* The client-supplied ``size_bytes`` is NEVER trusted on
  ``:complete``; the server uses ``len(backend.get(uri))``.
* Autosave drops the draft once the application is created and never
  serializes the resulting decision artifact, application_id, or any
  founder-id-bound row to ``localStorage``.
* No edits outside SCOPE.

Verification:
  python3 -m pytest tests/test_upload_initiate.py -v -p no:pytest-qt
    # 7 passed
  cd apps/founder_portal && pnpm install && pnpm playwright test
    # apply_flow.spec.ts + a11y.spec.ts (after `pnpm install` adds

SUPERSEDED — 2026-04-25 (Wave 9, prompt 32/70 — Feature-flag service +
                                  LaunchDarkly / PostHog adapter (defaults
                                  to local YAML))
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Replaced ad-hoc ``if config.experimental_x:`` gates with a single
typed feature-flag service. Flags live in
``data/governed/feature_flags.yaml`` (``schema_version:
feature-flags-v1``); the resolver consults a configured backend
(LaunchDarkly / PostHog, both lazy-imported) before falling back to
the YAML default and the caller's default. Decision-policy-affecting
flags are ``restricted`` — flipping one writes a JSONL audit row AND
emits a ``decision_policy_flag_changed.v1`` event so backtests can
replay against the old flag state.

What landed:

* ``data/governed/feature_flags.yaml`` (NEW) — six seed flags with
  type / default / restricted / client_visible / owner / description.
  Restricted: ``anti_gaming.enabled``,
  ``decision_policy.shadow_mode``, ``scoring.uncertainty_floor``.

* ``server/fund/services/feature_flags.py`` (NEW) — ``FeatureFlags``
  class with ``get_bool`` / ``get_string`` / ``get_percent``,
  ``set_unrestricted`` / ``set_restricted``, ``invalidate_cache``,
  ``list_flags``, ``public_flags``. ``MissingFlag``,
  ``RestrictedFlagViolation``, ``FlagTypeError`` are the public
  exceptions. 60-second cache with TTL configurable via the ctor.
  ``FlagSpec.coerce`` enforces type semantics on every read.
  Module-level ``get_feature_flags()`` lazily constructs a singleton
  wired to ``jsonl_event_emitter()`` so any caller that does not
  construct its own instance still satisfies the audit invariant.

* ``server/fund/services/feature_flag_backends.py`` (NEW) —
  ``FeatureFlagBackend`` Protocol; ``NullBackend``,
  ``LaunchDarklyBackend``, ``PostHogBackend``. Both remote backends
  perform a *lazy import* inside ``__init__``; missing SDK or API key
  raises ``FeatureFlagBackendError`` with a remediation message.

* ``server/fund/schemas/events/feature_flag_changed.v1.json`` (NEW) —
  ``DecisionPolicyFlagChangedV1`` schema. Required fields:
  ``key``, ``flag_type``, ``restricted`` (const true), ``old_value``,
  ``new_value``, ``actor``, ``source`` (enum: yaml | launchdarkly |
  posthog | cli). additionalProperties=false.

* ``server/fund/services/event_publisher.py`` (MOD) — added
  ``publish_decision_policy_flag_changed(audit_row)`` which
  validates against the new schema (best-effort jsonschema, same
  fallback as registered events) and persists via the existing
  ``EventOutbox``. The JSONL fallback used by the CLI lives in
  ``feature_flags.jsonl_event_emitter`` and writes envelopes to
  ``data/governed/feature_flag_events.jsonl``.

* ``cli.py`` (MOD) — new ``flags list`` (table / json) and
  ``flags set --key K --value V [--actor A --reason R]``.
  Restricted flags require ``--actor`` and ``--reason``; the CLI
  routes through the JSONL emitter so audit + event hit disk even
  without a DB session.

* ``docs/specs/feature_flags.md`` (NEW) — registry schema,
  resolution order, restricted-flag audit invariant, Python +
  Next.js consumption (``GET /api/v1/flags/public`` returns the
  ``client_visible`` non-restricted subset).

Tests (``tests/test_feature_flags.py``, 28 cases):

* Registry parsing happy path + four hard rejections (schema
  version mismatch / missing enum / restricted+client_visible /
  invalid default).
* Resolution order: YAML default; backend overrides YAML; string
  ``"true"`` coerced to ``True``; out-of-enum backend value falls
  through; ``MissingFlag`` for unknown keys; ``FlagTypeError`` on
  type mismatch; caller default round-trip.
* 60s cache stability + ``invalidate_cache()`` flush.
* Restricted-flag audit invariant: audit JSONL row written, event
  publisher called exactly once; missing actor / missing reason /
  wrong direction all raise ``RestrictedFlagViolation``;
  ``event_publisher=None`` raises on first restricted flip.
* Backend factory: default ``NullBackend``; unknown provider
  raises; LD/PostHog without API key raise.
* ``public_flags()`` excludes restricted flags.
* JSONL emitter writes a valid envelope.
* Governance YAML loads through the singleton path.

SUPERSEDED — 2026-04-25 (Wave 9, prompt 31/70 — 12-factor config
                                  audit + multi-environment gating
                                  (dev / staging / prod))
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Audited every config read for 12-factor compliance: the runtime now has
exactly one ``Settings`` model (Pydantic v2), exactly one place that
reads ``os.environ`` (``server/fund/config.py``), and exactly one
module that decides what differs across environments
(``server/fund/services/env_gates.py``). The auditor itself walks the
codebase with ``ast`` and records remaining violations in
``data/governed/config_audit_report.json``.

What landed:

* ``server/fund/config.py`` rewritten as a Pydantic v2 ``BaseSettings``
  with a strict ``environment: Literal["dev","test","staging","prod"]``
  field. Aliases (``production``, ``stage``, ``development``, ...) are
  normalized; unknown values raise. A ``model_validator(mode="after")``
  rejects ``STORAGE_BACKEND=local``, ``AUTO_CREATE_TABLES=true``,
  ``sqlite:`` URLs, and ``SECRET_MANAGER_PROVIDER=disabled`` when the
  env is ``prod``. Backwards-compatible UPPER_CASE alias properties
  preserve every legacy ``settings.DATABASE_URL`` style read.
  ``to_redacted_dict()`` powers ``config show`` (SecretStr fields are
  blanked, never printed).

* ``server/fund/services/env_gates.py`` — single source of truth for
  env-conditional behavior: ``is_prod()``, ``is_staging_or_prod()``,
  ``allow_dry_run_backends()``, ``allow_debug_routes()``,
  ``allow_local_storage_backend()``, ``allow_auto_create_tables()``,
  ``allow_print_secret_value()``, ``require_https()``,
  ``strict_secret_resolution()``. Each gate reads
  ``settings.environment`` and documents *why* the split exists. New
  gates must too.

* ``deploy/scripts/audit_twelve_factor.py`` — AST walker. Flags four
  rule families: env reads outside the allowlist (ERROR in
  ``server/fund/``, WARN in tooling), hardcoded ``http(s)://`` URLs,
  ``print`` outside CLI/scripts/tests, and ``requests``/``httpx``
  calls missing ``timeout=``. Deterministic JSON; exit 2 on any
  errors.

* ``data/governed/config_audit_report.json`` — first-run snapshot:
  total=145 (error=50, warn=95). The 50 errors all live in
  ``server/fund/`` files outside this prompt's SCOPE; they are the
  remediation backlog for the next config-touching prompts.

* ``cli.py`` — new ``config audit`` and ``config show`` subcommands
  (the auditor runs in-process via ``importlib``). The
  ``secrets manifest`` and ``secrets resolve`` subcommands now read
  ``settings.environment`` and delegate the prod-block to
  ``env_gates.allow_print_secret_value()`` instead of poking
  ``os.getenv("COHERENCE_FUND_ENV")``.

* ``docs/specs/twelve_factor.md`` documents the env taxonomy, the
  gate pattern, the allowlist tiers, the auditor rules, and the
  remediation backlog. ``tests/test_twelve_factor_audit.py`` (15
  cases, all passing) covers auditor fixtures, ``Settings``
  invariants, ``env_gates.is_prod()`` semantics, and the
  redacted-dump path.

Verification:

  python -m coherence_engine config audit --format summary  # exit 2 (backlog)
  python -m coherence_engine config show                    # JSON, redacted

Prohibitions held: no implicit hostname-based environment detection;
no per-environment hardcoded constants; no ``print`` for runtime
logging; no edits outside SCOPE.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SUPERSEDED — 2026-04-25 (Wave 9, prompt 30/70 — Background worker:
                                  Arq + Redis with WORKER_BACKEND poll/arq
                                  switch)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Replaced the cron-style poll worker with an Arq-based async worker
(Redis-backed) for scoring jobs, outbox dispatch, and
calibration/backtest jobs — keeping the polling worker behind a
``WORKER_BACKEND=poll|arq`` env switch as the failsafe. Arq is the
right substrate here: pure-async, no Celery overhead, Redis-only, and
deterministic-test runner support. Both backends call the SAME pure-
function task units, so business logic lives in one place.

- ``server/fund/workers/`` (NEW package):
  * ``tasks.py`` — pure-function task units shared by both backends:
      ``run_scoring_job(application_id) -> dict``,
      ``dispatch_outbox_batch(limit) -> int``,
      ``run_backtest_async(config) -> dict``.
    No new business logic; thin adapters around the existing
    ``ApplicationService.process_next_scoring_job`` /
    ``OutboxDispatcher.dispatch_once`` / ``backtest.run_backtest``.
  * ``dispatch.py`` — async enqueue helpers
    (``enqueue_scoring_job``, ``enqueue_outbox_dispatch``,
    ``enqueue_backtest``). Each is a no-op when ``WORKER_BACKEND=poll``
    so request handlers can call them unconditionally. Idempotency is
    enforced by passing the caller-supplied ``idempotency_key`` to Arq
    as ``_job_id`` (Arq's documented dedup contract): the first call
    schedules; subsequent calls with the same key return ``None``.
    The Arq Redis pool is acquired lazily and cached at module scope.
  * ``arq_worker.py`` — ``WorkerSettings`` class with
    ``functions=[score_job, dispatch_outbox, run_backtest]``,
    ``max_jobs=4`` (CPU-heavy scoring vs outbox starvation guard),
    ``max_tries=3``, ``job_timeout=900`` (15 min wall-clock cap),
    ``keep_result=86400`` (24-hour result retention), and lifecycle
    hooks (``on_startup`` / ``on_shutdown`` / ``on_job_start`` /
    ``on_job_end``). Each async stub offloads its sync body via
    ``asyncio.to_thread`` so the event loop stays responsive while a
    job runs. ``arq`` is lazy-imported so deployments staying on
    ``WORKER_BACKEND=poll`` are not forced to install the dep.

- ``server/fund/scoring_worker.py`` (MODIFIED): extracted
  ``run_scoring_job(application_id, *, db=None)`` as the pure-function
  unit of work. The legacy ``process_once`` / ``run_loop`` polling
  loop is unchanged and remains the failsafe.

- ``server/fund/config.py`` (MODIFIED): adds ``WORKER_BACKEND``
  (default ``poll``), ``REDIS_URL`` (default
  ``redis://localhost:6379/0``), ``ARQ_QUEUE_PREFIX``
  (default ``coherence_fund``).

- ``server/fund/app.py`` (MODIFIED): exposes the three enqueue helpers
  on ``app.state`` so request handlers can wire them through FastAPI's
  ``BackgroundTasks`` (never inline) — request-side Redis hiccups must
  never block the response. Adds an ``on_event("shutdown")`` hook that
  closes the Arq Redis pool.

- Tests:
  * ``tests/test_arq_worker.py`` — pure-function smoke
    (``run_scoring_job`` end-to-end against in-memory SQLite),
    enqueue idempotency on a stub Arq pool (same key → second call
    deduped), distinct-keys-schedule-separately, missing-key
    ``ValueError``, no-op behavior on poll backend, and a
    ``pytest.importorskip("arq")``-guarded ``WorkerSettings`` smoke
    that asserts the configured tunables.
  * ``tests/test_worker_backend_switch.py`` — verifies the env
    switch end-to-end: ``WORKER_BACKEND=arq`` causes
    ``enqueue_scoring_job`` to call ``pool.enqueue_job``;
    ``WORKER_BACKEND=poll`` returns ``None`` and never reaches the
    pool; the existing polling worker still drains a freshly-created
    ``ScoringJob`` row to ``completed`` under ``poll`` mode (regression
    guard for the failsafe path).

- Documentation: ``docs/ops/worker_runbook.md`` (NEW) — backend-
  selection matrix, start/drain/restart procedures, Upstash quirks
  (TLS endpoint vs REST API), re-enqueueing a stuck job
  (``asyncio.run(enqueue_scoring_job(...))`` with a unique idempotency
  key), failure-handling and observability (``arq.score_job.start`` /
  ``arq.score_job.done`` log markers, ``worker_ops_snapshot`` reuse),
  and the env/WorkerSettings configuration reference.

- Deployment artifacts under ``deploy/arq/``:
  * ``coherence-fund-arq-worker.service`` — systemd unit invoking
    ``python -m coherence_engine.server.fund.workers.arq_worker``;
    ``TimeoutStopSec=950`` exceeds ``job_timeout`` so the kernel does
    not SIGKILL during a graceful drain.
  * ``run_arq_worker.sh`` — shell launcher used by the unit and ad-hoc
    operator runs (sources ``/etc/default/coherence-fund``, validates
    the minimum env block, ``exec``s the python entrypoint).
  * ``values.yaml`` — Helm values block for the umbrella chart
    (``arqWorker.enabled=false`` by default; replicaCount, env,
    resources, livenessProbe, ``terminationGracePeriodSeconds=950``).
  * ``upstash.env.example`` — Upstash Redis env template (TLS
    ``rediss://`` only; the REST API is incompatible with Arq).
  * ``README.md`` — file index.

Verification:

    python3 -m pytest tests/test_arq_worker.py \
                      tests/test_worker_backend_switch.py -v
  → 11 passed (or 10 passed, 1 skipped if ``arq`` is not installed).

      -q
  → 16 passed, 1 deselected (the deselected case is the pre-existing
    prompt-28 security-package-refactor failure; it predates this
    prompt).

Prohibitions honored:

* Polling worker is NOT removed — ``server/fund/scoring_worker.py``
  and ``server/fund/worker.py`` are untouched in their loop bodies;
  only an additional pure-function entrypoint was added.
* CI default ``REDIS_URL`` is local-loopback; no public-network host
  is pinned anywhere in code.
* Request handlers were NOT modified — ``server/fund/routers/*`` is
  out of scope; the enqueue helpers are surfaced on ``app.state`` and
  must be invoked via ``BackgroundTasks`` by the next prompt that
  touches the score endpoint.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SUPERSEDED — 2026-04-25 (Wave 9, prompt 29/70 — Object-storage
                          adapter for transcripts + artifacts)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Introduced a single, storage-agnostic adapter that every code path writing
or reading a large blob (transcripts, argument propositions / relations,
decision-artifact bodies) goes through. Three backends ship in this
prompt; selection is environment-keyed and the local backend is the CI-
safe default.

- ``server/fund/services/object_storage.py`` (NEW):
  * URI grammar: ``coh://<backend>/<bucket>/<key>``. ``backend`` ∈
    ``local`` | ``s3`` | ``supabase``. ``parse_uri`` and ``format_uri``
    are the only sanctioned producers/consumers; never hand-build URIs.
  * ``PutResult(uri, sha256, size, etag)`` — every successful put
    returns this; the ``sha256`` is recomputed from the bytes the
    backend actually persisted, not the bytes the caller supplied.
  * ``StorageHashMismatch`` / ``StorageNotFound`` /
    ``StorageBackendError`` — distinct exception classes; callers
    surface ``StorageHashMismatch`` as data corruption (fatal).
  * Module-level ``put`` / ``get`` / ``open_stream`` / ``delete``
    delegate to the process-wide backend resolved by
    ``get_object_storage()`` (env-keyed off ``STORAGE_BACKEND``).
  * ``set_object_storage`` / ``reset_object_storage`` are test-only
    swap points.

- ``server/fund/services/storage_backends.py`` (NEW):
  * ``LocalFilesystemBackend`` — atomic writes via tempfile + fsync +
    rename; tombstones under ``<root>/<bucket>/.tombstone/<key>``;
    range reads via ``seek``; rejects ``../`` and absolute keys.
  * ``S3Backend`` — boto3 lazy-imported in ``_client_for``; reads use
    HTTP ``Range: bytes=A-(B-1)`` (HTTP range is inclusive on the upper
    bound; we translate from Python-slice ``[A, B)``); soft delete is
    ``copy_object`` to ``tombstone/<key>`` then ``delete_object``;
    ``signed_url(uri, expires_in=...)`` mints a presigned GET URL.
  * ``SupabaseStorageBackend`` — httpx lazy-imported; ``client=`` kwarg
    accepts an injected stub for tests; calls authenticate with the
    service-role JWT (server-side only — never exposed to the
    portal); ``signed_url`` parses ``signedURL`` / ``signedUrl`` /
    ``url`` from the response; ``delete`` uses Supabase's atomic
    ``move`` REST verb.

- ``server/fund/services/decision_artifact.py`` (MODIFIED):
  ``persist_decision_artifact`` now dual-writes — DB ``payload_json``
  remains the authoritative store; the same canonical bytes are also
  written through ``object_storage.put`` at
  ``decision_artifacts/<application_id>/<artifact_id>.json`` and the
  returned ``sha256`` is verified against the locally-computed
  digest. ``StorageHashMismatch`` is fatal; transient transport
  failures are logged but do not abort the DB write.

- ``server/fund/services/transcript_quality.py`` (MODIFIED): adds
  ``store_transcript(transcript, application_id) -> uri``,
  ``load_transcript_bytes(uri) -> bytes``, and
  ``load_transcript_text(uri) -> str``. The store helper canonicalizes
  the ``Transcript`` to JSON, ``put``s through the configured backend,
  and verifies the round-trip digest before returning the URI.

- ``server/fund/services/scoring.py`` (MODIFIED):
  ``_build_input_text`` falls back to
  ``transcript_quality.load_transcript_text(uri)`` whenever the
  application has no inline ``transcript_text`` but does have a
  ``coh://`` URI. Legacy ``db://`` placeholder URIs are left alone to
  keep existing tests stable.

- ``.env.example`` — documents ``STORAGE_BACKEND``,
  ``LOCAL_STORAGE_ROOT``, ``LOCAL_STORAGE_BUCKET``, ``S3_BUCKET``,
  ``SUPABASE_STORAGE_BUCKET``.

- ``docs/specs/object_storage.md`` (NEW) — URI grammar, hash
  discipline, range-read contract, soft-delete / tombstone /
  ``--purge`` lifecycle, retention defaults (transcripts 90 days,
  decision artifacts indefinite), founder-portal signed-URL handout
  flow, and prohibitions (no top-level boto3/httpx imports, no
  client-supplied hashes for high-value artifacts, no synchronous
  hard-deletes in production paths).

- Tests:
  * ``tests/test_object_storage.py`` (16) — URI round-trip + malformed
    rejection, put/get/delete tombstone, hash-mismatch detection,
    range read [1000:2000] of a 10 MB blob with exact-byte equality,
    open-ended range, slice-range bounds-check, global backend swap.
  * ``tests/test_storage_backends.py`` (14, 5 skipped when ``moto``
    is absent) — local atomic put, unsafe-key + bucket-mismatch
    rejections, S3 put/get/range/tombstone/signed-url under
    ``moto.mock_aws``, Supabase header / range / signed-URL / move-
    endpoint-delete using an injected stub httpx client.

Verification:

  python -m pytest tests/test_object_storage.py tests/test_storage_backends.py -v
  → 25 passed, 5 skipped (S3 cases skip when ``moto`` is not installed).

  Pre-existing test failures unrelated to this prompt:
  ``test_decision_artifact::test_validate_rejects_artifact_missing_decision_policy_version``
  (jsonschema not installed → required-keys-only fallback validator),
  ``test_fund_backend::test_bootstrap_admin_token_from_secret_manager``
  (documented in prompt 28's status notes), and a few engine /
  telemetry / migration-registry assertions; all confirmed failing
  on the baseline before this prompt's changes.

Operational follow-up:

* Real-transcript persist sites (workflow orchestrator + application
  service) still write legacy ``db://`` placeholders to
  ``Application.transcript_uri``. Wiring the live call sites to
  ``transcript_quality.store_transcript(...)`` is owned by the next
  workflow-revision prompt; this prompt's scope was the adapter and
  the read paths.
* Cluster-side hard-purge is a separate ``coherence-engine storage
  purge --older-than <window>`` admin verb to be added alongside the
  retention scheduler.

Next: prompt 30 (Wave 9 continues).


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SUPERSEDED — 2026-04-25 (Wave 8, prompt 28/70 — API-key v2:
                          service accounts, Argon2id, scopes)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Replaced the legacy SHA-256-hashed single-``role`` API-key model with a
v2 design built around hashed-at-rest credentials (**Argon2id**),
explicit per-key scopes, per-key rate limit, hard 1-year expiry default,
and a ``ServiceAccount`` row that owns one or more keys. The plaintext
token is exposed exactly **once** at create / rotate time and never
persisted server-side.

- ``server/fund/models.py`` (MODIFIED):
  * ``ServiceAccount`` (``fund_service_accounts``: ``id``, unique
    ``name``, ``description``, ``owner_email``, ``created_at``).
  * ``ApiKey`` extended with ``service_account_id`` (FK), 8-char
    ``prefix`` (public discriminator, indexed), ``scopes_json`` (JSON
    list), ``rate_limit_per_minute``. Legacy columns (``label`` /
    ``role`` / ``key_fingerprint`` / ``key_hash`` / ``is_active``) are
    retained as compatibility shims so the still-in-flight admin UI /
    fund middleware / workflow router keep working without out-of-scope
    edits. ``key_hash`` widened to ``String(255)`` to hold an
    Argon2id-encoded hash.

- ``alembic/versions/20260425_000004_service_accounts_and_api_keys_v2.py``
  (NEW) — drops the legacy ``fund_api_keys`` table (NULL-out
  ``api_key_id`` on existing audit rows so they survive as orphans;
  the SHA-256 → Argon2id algorithm change makes secret-preserving
  migration impossible) and recreates it with the v2 schema. Creates
  ``fund_service_accounts``. On Postgres, drops + re-establishes the
  ``fund_api_key_audit_events.api_key_id`` FK; SQLite carries the
  embedded constraint. Operators must re-issue any in-use keys
  post-migration.

- ``server/fund/services/api_key_service.py`` (REWRITTEN):
  * ``KNOWN_SCOPES`` = ``applications:read | applications:write |
    decisions:read | admin:read | admin:write | worker:claim |
    worker:complete``.
  * ``_PASSWORD_HASHER = PasswordHasher(time_cost=3,
    memory_cost=64*1024, parallelism=4, type=Type.ID)``.
  * Tokens formatted ``ce_<prefix8>_<secret32b64>``;
    ``_split_token(token)`` parses the prefix.
  * ``create_key_v2(db, *, service_account_id, scopes, created_by,
    label, expires_at, rate_limit_per_minute)`` returns a
    ``CreatedKey`` dataclass containing the plaintext token. Default
    expiry is ``now + 365d`` if ``expires_at`` is None.
  * ``verify_key(db, presented) -> ApiKey`` does a prefix lookup +
    constant-time Argon2id verify. Burns a dummy hash on prefix miss
    to avoid a timing oracle. Raises ``InvalidKey(reason=...)`` for
    ``unknown_key | malformed_token | expired | revoked``.
  * ``revoke_key_v2(db, prefix)`` and ``rotate_key_v2(db, *, prefix,
    actor, grace_seconds=0, expires_at=None)`` — rotation creates a
    fresh key with the same scopes / rate limit / service account and
    shrinks the old key's ``expires_at`` to ``now + grace_seconds``
    (defaults to immediate revoke).
  * Legacy ``create_key`` / ``verify_token`` / ``revoke_key`` /
    ``rotate_key`` signatures preserved as wrappers that translate the
    coarse ``role`` into the corresponding scope set
    (``admin``/``analyst``/``viewer``/``worker``/``service``).

- ``server/fund/security/api_key_auth.py`` (NEW):
  * ``require_scopes(*scopes)`` FastAPI dep with subset semantics.
    Reads ``X-API-Key`` or ``Authorization: Bearer …``, calls
    ``ApiKeyService.verify_key``, enforces per-key in-process token-
    bucket rate limiting, then checks the scope subset.
  * Token bucket: capacity = refill = ``rate_limit_per_minute``,
    refilled per second (process-local; cluster-wide limiting deferred
    to the gateway prompt).
  * Distinct error codes: ``UNAUTHORIZED`` / ``UNAUTHORIZED_EXPIRED``
    / ``UNAUTHORIZED_REVOKED`` / ``INSUFFICIENT_SCOPE`` /
    ``RATE_LIMITED``.

- ``server/fund/routers/admin_api_keys.py`` (MODIFIED):
  * Legacy role-based endpoints (``POST /``, ``GET /``,
    ``POST /{key_id}/revoke``, ``POST /{key_id}/rotate``) preserved.
  * New v2 surface: ``POST /admin/api-keys/service-accounts``,
    ``GET /admin/api-keys/service-accounts``,
    ``POST /admin/api-keys/v2``, ``GET /admin/api-keys/v2[?
    service_account_name=...]``,
    ``POST /admin/api-keys/v2/{prefix}/revoke``,
    ``POST /admin/api-keys/v2/{prefix}/rotate``. Plaintext token
    returned exactly once with a "shown once" warning.

- ``cli.py`` — adds ``api-keys create | list | revoke | rotate``
  subcommands. ``create`` accepts ``--account``, ``--scope``
  (repeatable), ``--label``, ``--expires YYYY-MM-DD``,
  ``--rate-limit-per-minute``, plus ``--description`` / ``--owner-email``
  used to create the service account on the fly when it does not
  already exist. Plaintext token is printed exactly once to stdout
  with a stderr warning; ``list`` prints prefixes only.

- Tests: ``tests/test_api_key_service_v2.py`` (14 cases) and
  ``tests/test_api_key_auth.py`` (8 cases) — Argon2id round-trip,
  tampered + unknown-prefix + malformed rejections, expired and
  revoked distinct ``reason`` paths, default 1-year expiry, rotate
  immediate-revoke + grace-window, legacy compat round-trip, scope
  subset enforcement (allowed + rejected), admin-write gating,
  bearer-header acceptance, rate-limit 429.

- Docs: ``docs/specs/api_keys_v2.md`` — scope catalog, token format,
  rotation playbook, prohibitions (no SHA-family hashing, no plaintext
  at rest, no plaintext logging, no bypass of ``require_scopes``).

Verification:

  python -m pytest tests/test_api_key_service_v2.py tests/test_api_key_auth.py -v
  → 22 passed.

  python -m pytest tests/test_fund_backend.py tests/test_admin_dashboard.py
                   tests/test_openapi_and_sdk.py
                   tests/test_api_key_service_v2.py tests/test_api_key_auth.py
  → 73 passed; 1 pre-existing failure
    (``test_bootstrap_admin_token_from_secret_manager``) caused by the
    in-progress ``security.py → security/`` package refactor's
    ``get_secret_manager`` re-export resolution; that file is out of
    this prompt's scope.

Operational follow-up:

* Existing operational keys are invalidated by the migration and must
  be re-issued via ``coherence-engine api-keys create`` post-deploy.
* The legacy admin / workflow / middleware layers still call the
  ``ApiKeyService`` shim; subsequent prompts will migrate them to
  ``security.api_key_auth.require_scopes(...)``.
* Cluster-wide per-key rate limiting is deferred to the upstream API-
  gateway prompt.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SUPERSEDED — 2026-04-25 (Wave 8, prompt 27/70 — Unified
                          secrets-manager interface)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Consolidates every runtime secret read behind a single ``SecretManager``
resolver composed of pluggable ``SecretBackend`` implementations
(``EnvBackend`` default, plus ``DopplerBackend``, ``HashicorpVaultBackend``,
``SupabaseVaultBackend``). The declarative manifest at
``data/governed/secret_manifest.yaml`` enumerates every named secret
with a policy (``prod_required|prod_optional|dev_optional``); the
production startup hook calls ``verify_manifest("production")`` and
aborts the boot if any ``prod_required`` entry is unresolved.

- ``server/fund/services/secret_backends.py`` (NEW):
  * ``SecretBackend`` Protocol with ``get(name) -> Optional[str]`` and
    ``health() -> bool``.
  * ``EnvBackend`` reads ``os.environ``; treats empty / whitespace
    values as missing; always healthy.
  * ``DopplerBackend`` calls
    ``GET https://api.doppler.com/v3/configs/config/secret?name=…``
    with ``Authorization: Bearer $DOPPLER_TOKEN``; optional
    ``DOPPLER_PROJECT`` / ``DOPPLER_CONFIG`` for service-token scope;
    per-name 60s in-memory cache.
  * ``HashicorpVaultBackend`` reads KV v2 at
    ``$VAULT_ADDR/v1/$VAULT_KV_MOUNT/data/$VAULT_KV_PATH`` with
    ``X-Vault-Token: $VAULT_TOKEN``; bundles the entire path's KV
    map and caches for ``lease_duration`` (capped at 300s).
  * ``SupabaseVaultBackend`` calls ``client.rpc('get_secret', {
    secret_name: name }).execute()`` via service-role client; useful
    when the app already has Supabase admin access.
  * Each backend takes an injectable ``http_fetch`` (or ``client``)
    so tests run without network. ``build_backend(name)`` factory
    raises ``SecretBackendError`` on unknown name.

- ``server/fund/services/secret_manifest.py`` (NEW):
  * Schema constant ``SCHEMA_VERSION = "secret-manifest-v1"``.
  * ``ManifestEntry`` (``name`` / ``category`` / ``policy`` /
    optional ``owner`` + ``description``) validates required fields
    + policy in ``ALLOWED_POLICIES`` at construction.
  * ``ResolvedEntry`` and ``ManifestReport`` deliberately serialize
    only metadata + status; ``to_dict()`` is test-asserted to
    contain no resolved values.
  * ``MissingRequiredSecret`` (RuntimeError) raised by the resolver
    in production env when any ``prod_required`` entry is missing.
  * ``SecretManifest.load(path)`` + ``SecretManifest.default()``
    (resolves to ``data/governed/secret_manifest.yaml``).

- ``data/governed/secret_manifest.yaml`` (NEW):
  19 entries spanning ``db``, ``auth``, ``kyc``, ``bootstrap``,
  ``ops`` categories. Header documents the three policy values.

- ``server/fund/services/secret_manager.py`` (MODIFY):
  * Renames the legacy ABC ``SecretManager`` to ``ManagedSecretStore``
    (the AWS / GCP / Vault legacy adapters now inherit from it).
    No external callers ever imported the ABC by name — only
    ``SecretManagerError`` and ``get_secret_manager()`` — so the
    rename is transparent.
  * Adds the new top-level ``SecretManager`` resolver class:
    ``from_env()`` factory reads ``SECRETS_BACKEND`` (default
    ``env``); ``get(name)`` chains primary → env fallback with an
    in-memory process-lifetime cache and an audit log of which
    backend resolved each name (value never logged);
    ``verify_manifest(env)`` returns a ``ManifestReport`` and
    raises ``MissingRequiredSecret`` only when ``env=="production"``.
  * ``get_secret_resolver()`` is the process-wide accessor;
    ``set_secret_resolver_for_tests`` is the injection seam.

- ``server/fund/app.py`` (MODIFY):
  After the existing managed-secret-manager probe, the startup
  hook calls ``get_secret_resolver().verify_manifest(env)``.
  ``MissingRequiredSecret`` propagates on production env to abort
  uvicorn (non-zero exit); non-prod environments log unresolved
  ``prod_required`` entries at WARNING and continue.

- ``cli.py`` (MODIFY):
  * ``secrets manifest [--env <env>] [--json]`` prints the table
    or JSON report — name / category / policy / status / backend.
    Values NEVER appear in the output. Test asserts that an env
    var holding ``hidden`` is not echoed by manifest output.
  * ``secrets resolve --name X --allow-unsafe-print`` prints the
    value to stdout, but ONLY if all three of:
      1. ``--allow-unsafe-print`` is on the command line,
      2. ``CONFIRM_PRINT_SECRET=YES`` in the env,
      3. runtime env (``COHERENCE_FUND_ENV`` / ``APP_ENV``) is not
         ``production``.
    If any one of these is missing, exit non-zero with a clear
    error.

- ``docs/specs/secret_management.md`` (NEW):
  Manifest schema + how to add / remove a secret, backend list,
  resolution + caching semantics, the boot gate contract, the
  never-log invariant, the rotation playbook (per-category cadence
  and procedure), and the coexistence story with the legacy
  ``ManagedSecretStore``.

- ``tests/test_secret_backends.py`` (NEW, 19 tests):
  Env reads (set / missing / empty / whitespace), Doppler with
  fake fetcher (typed error on missing token, 60s cache, missing
  value as None, malformed payload raises), Vault KV v2 read,
  Supabase Vault rpc with a fake client (single value, list-payload
  unwrap, missing returns None), missing ``SUPABASE_URL`` raises,
  ``build_backend`` factory.

- ``tests/test_secret_manifest.py`` (NEW, 19 tests):
  Manifest schema (default loads, rejects unknown ``schema_version``,
  empty ``secrets``, invalid policy, duplicates, missing fields),
  resolver chain (cache holds across calls, two-backend audit log,
  None when all miss), ``verify_manifest`` (production-missing-
  raises, production-all-present-returns-report, dev-never-raises),
  ``to_dict()`` never leaks values, CLI defense-in-depth
  (refuses-without-flag, refuses-without-confirm-env, refuses-in-
  prod, prints-with-all-three-gates), CLI ``secrets manifest`` does
  not echo values.

Verification:
  python3 -m pytest tests/test_secret_backends.py
                    tests/test_secret_manifest.py -v
    # 38 passed.
  python3 -m pytest tests/test_secret_manager_preflight.py
                    tests/test_secret_manager_policy_matrix.py -q
    # 5 passed (legacy bootstrap-admin path untouched).
  python3 -m coherence_engine secrets manifest --env development
    # prints 19-entry table, schema=secret-manifest-v1, env=development.

Prohibitions honored:
* Secret values are NEVER logged. Every audit-log line emits
  ``name`` + ``backend`` only; ``ManifestReport.to_dict()`` is
  test-asserted to contain no resolved value.
* No on-disk cache. ``SecretManager._cache`` is in-memory only;
  rotation is documented as restart-driven.
* No "default" value for ``prod_required`` entries.
* No edits outside SCOPE.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
EARLIER PROMPT — 2026-04-25 (Wave 8, prompt 26/70 — Accredited
                              investor verification adapter)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Adds a pluggable ``AccreditedInvestorVerification`` adapter pattern with
``Persona``, ``Onfido``, and ``Manual`` (operator-attested) backends.
Persists a per-investor ``VerificationRecord`` row with provider,
status (``pending|verified|rejected|expired``), method (``income |
net_worth | professional_certification | self_certified``), expiry,
and provenance metadata. **Founder applications and the scoring
pipeline are unaffected** — this is an LP-side intake gate. SQLite
remains the default; ``python -m pytest`` works unchanged with no env
vars (the manual backend's upload secret falls back to a built-in
dry-run default; Persona/Onfido return ``503 PROVIDER_UNAVAILABLE``
unless their env vars are set).

- ``server/fund/services/accredited_backends.py`` (NEW):
  * ``AccreditedBackend`` Protocol with ``initiate(investor, *,
    redirect_url)``, ``fetch_status(record)``,
    ``webhook_signature_ok(payload, headers)``.
  * ``InitiationResponse`` (redirect_url, provider_reference,
    upload_token) and ``StatusResponse`` (status, method,
    evidence_uri, evidence_hash, error_code) dataclasses.
  * ``PersonaBackend.from_env()`` reads ``PERSONA_API_KEY``,
    ``PERSONA_WEBHOOK_SECRET``, ``PERSONA_TEMPLATE_ID``. Webhook
    signature: HMAC-SHA-256 over ``f"{ts}.{raw_body}"``, accepts
    either the Stripe-style ``t=...,v1=...`` packed header or
    separated ``persona-signature`` + ``webhook-timestamp``.
  * ``OnfidoBackend.from_env()`` reads ``ONFIDO_API_TOKEN``,
    ``ONFIDO_WEBHOOK_TOKEN``. Same HMAC contract; checks
    ``X-SHA2-Signature`` + ``Webhook-Timestamp``.
  * ``ManualBackend.from_env()`` reads
    ``ACCREDITATION_MANUAL_UPLOAD_SECRET`` (optional; default
    ``"manual-dryrun"``). Operator-attested only — there is no
    webhook, so ``webhook_signature_ok`` returns ``False``
    unconditionally (no silent grant of trust to a request claiming
    to be from a "manual provider").
  * Shared ``_verify_hmac_sha256`` helper does
    ``hmac.compare_digest`` over equal-length inputs and rejects
    skew > ``WEBHOOK_SKEW_SECONDS = 300`` (5 minutes) — captured
    deliveries can't be replayed indefinitely.
  * ``backend_for_provider(provider)`` factory raises ``ValueError``
    on unknown provider strings (typos fail loudly) and
    ``AccreditedBackendConfigError`` if required env vars are
    missing.

- ``server/fund/services/accredited_verification.py`` (NEW):
  * ``initiate_verification(db, *, investor, backend, redirect_url)``
    — calls ``backend.initiate``, persists a ``pending``
    ``VerificationRecord`` with idempotency key
    ``sha256(investor_id|provider|provider_reference)``. Duplicate
    initiates collapse onto the same row.
  * ``apply_webhook(db, *, backend, raw_payload, headers,
    parsed_payload=None, trace_id="")``:
    1. ``backend.webhook_signature_ok(raw_payload, headers)`` —
       raises ``VerificationError("webhook_signature_invalid")`` on
       mismatch. **No row is mutated on signature failure.**
    2. JSON-parses the payload; locates the record by
       ``(provider, provider_reference)``.
    3. Replay protection: if ``record.status == new_status`` and
       record is already terminal (``verified``/``rejected``), the
       call is a no-op — same row returned, no fields rewritten,
       no event re-emitted.
    4. On ``verified``: sets ``completed_at`` and ``expires_at =
       completed_at + 90 days`` (per SEC re-verification convention).
       On ``rejected``: clears ``expires_at``.
    5. Updates ``Investor.status`` (``verified``/``rejected``) and
       enqueues an ``investor_verification_updated`` event in the
       outbox via ``EventPublisher`` (idempotency key
       ``"ivu:{record.id}:{record.status}"``).
  * ``latest_record_for_investor(db, investor_id)`` returns the most
    recent row by ``created_at``.
  * ``evaluate_effective_status(record)`` — read-only; reports
    ``"expired"`` for verified rows whose ``expires_at`` has passed,
    without mutating history. Re-verification is a fresh row, not a
    mutation.
  * ``ALLOWED_METHODS`` = ``{income, net_worth,
    professional_certification, self_certified}`` (Rule 501 paths).
  * ``ALLOWED_STATUSES`` = ``{pending, verified, rejected, expired}``.
  * ``VERIFICATION_TTL_DAYS`` = 90.

- ``server/fund/models.py`` (MODIFY):
  * ``Investor`` table (``fund_investors``): id, ``founder_user_id``
    (Supabase ``sub``, unique nullable=False), legal_name,
    residence_country, investor_type
    (``individual|entity|qualified_purchaser``), status, created_at.
  * ``VerificationRecord`` table (``fund_verification_records``): id,
    investor_id FK, provider, method, status, expires_at,
    evidence_uri (object-storage path), evidence_hash (SHA-256),
    provider_reference, ``idempotency_key`` (unique index),
    error_code, created_at, completed_at.
  * Storage discipline: row holds only the SHA-256 hash + opaque
    object-storage URI. Raw evidence bytes never enter the DB.

- ``alembic/versions/20260425_000003_investor_verification.py`` (NEW):
  Down-revision is ``20260425_000002`` (founder_user_id from prompt 25).
  Creates both tables with the indexes above. Stock ``op.create_table``
  / ``op.create_index`` — no dialect branching needed (SQLite +
  Postgres handled identically).

- ``server/fund/routers/investor_verification.py`` (NEW):
  * ``current_investor`` FastAPI dependency, parallel to
    ``current_founder`` from prompt 25: JWT path verifies the
    Supabase token, lazily upserts an ``Investor`` row keyed by
    ``sub``, returns it; service-role-bypass path returns ``None``;
    otherwise 401.
  * ``POST /investors/{id}/verification:initiate`` — body picks

    ``current_investor`` (or service-role principal).
  * ``GET /investors/{id}/verification`` — returns the latest record
    plus the *effective* status (``expired`` if past ``expires_at``,
    even when stored row says ``verified``).
  * ``POST /webhooks/persona`` and ``POST /webhooks/onfido`` —
    verify HMAC signature on the raw body, apply update, commit.
    Invalid signature → 401 ``UNAUTHORIZED``, no state change.
    Replay (same body) → 200, no-op. Unknown record → 200, ignored
    (provider doesn't keep retrying forever).
  * ``set_backend_factory_for_tests`` /
    ``reset_backend_factory_for_tests`` injection seam — tests
    override the backend factory without monkey-patching the
    import.
  * ``FundSecurityMiddleware`` does not gate ``/investors/...`` or
    ``/webhooks/...`` paths (its allowlist only covers
    ``/applications`` + ``/admin/api-keys``), so the JWT
    dependency / signature check is the only authentication.

- ``tests/test_accredited_verification.py`` (NEW, 19 tests):

Prohibitions honored:
* Webhook signature verification is **never** bypassed, even in dry-run

EARLIER PROMPT — 2026-04-25 (Wave 8, prompt 25/70 — Supabase Auth +
                              JWT verification middleware for the
                              founder portal)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Adds Supabase-issued JWT verification on the founder-scoped routes,
introduces a JWKS cache with kid-aware refresh, maps the ``sub`` claim
onto a new ``founder_user_id`` column on ``fund_founders`` via an
expand-pattern migration, and adds liveness/readiness probes that stay
unauthenticated.

- ``server/fund/security/jwks_cache.py`` (NEW):
  * ``JwksCache`` keyed by ``kid``; first request fetches via ``httpx``,
    caches for ``JWKS_CACHE_TTL_SECONDS`` (default 3600), refreshes on
    ``kid`` cache-miss with a 30s rate-limit per ``kid``.
  * ``JWKSUnavailable`` typed exception so callers can distinguish
    JWKS-down (503) from auth-failure (401/403).
  * ``set_key_for_test`` / ``reset_default_cache_for_tests`` injection
    seams so tests never touch the network.
  * ``is_reachable()`` is the seam used by ``/readyz``.

- ``server/fund/security/auth.py`` (NEW):
  * ``verify_supabase_jwt(token, *, cache=None, audience=None,
    issuer=None)`` — PyJWT-based decode with strict allowlist of
    ``RS256/RS384/RS512/ES256/ES384`` (HMAC explicitly rejected to keep
    the service-role secret from being usable as a signer), 30s clock
    skew, and explicit error mapping: 401 (unauth/expired/tampered),
    403 (wrong ``aud``/``iss``), 503 (JWKS unavailable).
  * ``current_founder`` FastAPI dependency: dual-mode. JWT path verifies
    and lazily upserts the ``Founder`` row keyed by ``founder_user_id``;
    service-role path (existing API-key principal already on
    ``request.state``) returns ``None`` so ownership checks are skipped
    without breaking workers/admin tooling.
  * Audit posture: only the truncated ``sub`` reaches log lines — never
    the raw token, ``Authorization`` header, or full claim dict.

- ``server/fund/models.py`` (MODIFY):
  Adds ``founder_user_id`` (``String(64)``, nullable, unique index) on
  ``Founder``. Nullable per the expand/backfill/contract pattern from
  prompt 24; pre-existing rows are not associated with a Supabase user
  until they sign in via the portal.

- ``alembic/versions/20260425_000002_founder_user_id.py`` (NEW):
  Adds the column + ``ix_fund_founders_founder_user_id`` (unique).
  Down-revision is ``20260425_000001`` (RLS policies). Down-migration
  drops both. SQLite and Postgres handled by stock ``op.add_column`` /
  ``op.create_index`` (no dialect branching needed).

- ``server/fund/routers/applications.py`` (MODIFY):
  * ``POST /applications`` now declares ``Depends(current_founder)``;
    on the JWT path the route re-links the application to the
    authenticated founder so the service cannot be tricked into
    associating an application with a founder identity the caller
    didn't authenticate as.
  * New ``GET /applications/{id}`` returns the application summary,
    gated by ``current_founder`` and the ownership check.
  * ``GET /applications/{id}/decision`` now ownership-checks before
    returning.
  * ``_founder_owns_application`` helper centralizes the
    ``application.founder_id == founder.id`` test (defense in depth
    even with RLS, since the API-key path bypasses RLS).

- ``server/fund/routers/health.py`` (MODIFY):
  Adds ``GET /healthz`` (liveness, no DB / JWKS) and ``GET /readyz`` (DB
  + JWKS reachability). Both stay unauthenticated by living outside

EARLIER PROMPT — 2026-04-25 (Wave 7, prompt 24/70 — Zero-downtime
                              Postgres migration patterns + Alembic CI
                              gate)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Refactors the two migrations the prompt-21 audit flagged with errors so
they are dialect-safe (SQLite still parses them; Postgres still drops
the temporary server_default), adds a CI gate that proves
``alembic upgrade head → downgrade -1 → upgrade head`` is reversible
against a real Postgres, wires that gate into the release-readiness
checklist, and ships an operator playbook for the expand-backfill-
contract pattern.

- `alembic/versions/20260409_000002_scoring_queue_and_artifact_fields.py`
  (MODIFY): the three trailing
  ``op.alter_column(..., server_default=None)`` calls (which SQLite
  rejects) are now ``op.execute("ALTER TABLE ... DROP DEFAULT")`` calls
  guarded by ``op.get_bind().dialect.name == "postgresql"``. Final
  Postgres schema is unchanged; SQLite carries the literal default into
  existing rows (which is fine — its ``ADD COLUMN`` already did so).

- `alembic/versions/20260409_000004_worker_reliability_fields.py`
  (MODIFY): same pattern, applied to the ``attempts``,
  ``max_attempts``, ``locked_by`` columns.

  After both refactors, ``data/governed/migration_registry.json`` shows
  ``errors == []`` for every revision and the auditor's exit code is
  ``0``.

- `deploy/scripts/migration_ci_gate.py` (NEW):
  * ``run_gate(pg_url, *, alembic_runner=..., dump_runner=...)``: drives
    ``alembic upgrade head`` → ``pg_dump --schema-only`` →
    ``alembic downgrade -1`` → ``alembic upgrade head`` →
    ``pg_dump --schema-only``; normalizes both dumps (strips ``--``
    comments, blank lines, trailing whitespace) and compares
    line-by-line. Exit codes: ``0`` reversible, ``1`` transient,
    ``2`` schema drift. ``alembic_runner`` / ``dump_runner`` are
    monkeypatchable seams the unit tests use to script subprocess
    behavior without a real Postgres.
  * ``main()``: skip-on-unconfigured by default (exit ``0`` with a
    "Postgres CI gate not configured" message) so local devs are not
    blocked. ``--require-configured`` flips that to a hard error so CI
    fails loudly if the secret was not wired up.

- `deploy/scripts/release_readiness_check.py` (MODIFY):
  Adds the ``migration_ci_gate`` check. When ``MIGRATION_GATE_PG_URL``
  is unset, status is ``pass`` with reason
  ``migration_ci_gate_skipped``; when set, the gate runs and the
  result is mapped to ``pass`` / ``fail`` (``schema_drift``) /
  ``error`` (``transient``).

- `.github/workflows/migrations.yml` (NEW):
  GitHub Actions workflow with a ``services: postgres`` block running
  ``postgres:15`` on a PR that touches ``alembic/versions/**``,
  ``server/fund/models.py``, the gate, or the workflow itself.
  Resolves ``MIGRATION_GATE_PG_URL`` from the GitHub Actions secret if
  set, else from the service container; installs ``postgresql-client``
  for ``pg_dump``; invokes ``--require-configured``; then re-runs the
  static audit as a belt-and-braces check.

- `tests/test_migration_ci_gate.py` (NEW, 11 unit tests + 1
  integration-marked test):
  * Normalization: ``--`` comment / blank-line stripping,
    diff-equality of dumps that differ only in headers.
  * ``run_gate`` happy path: matching dumps return
    ``EXIT_OK`` with "reversible" message.
  * Schema drift: returns ``EXIT_SCHEMA_DRIFT`` with the unified diff
    embedded in the message.
  * Transient branches (parametrized): each subprocess seam can be
    failed independently — initial upgrade, downgrade, second upgrade,
    pg_dump.
  * CLI: skip-on-unconfigured returns ``EXIT_OK``;
    ``--require-configured`` flips to ``EXIT_TRANSIENT``;
    ``--pg-url`` flag overrides the env var.
  * ``@pytest.mark.integration`` test runs the live cycle when
    ``MIGRATION_GATE_PG_URL`` is set, skips otherwise.

- `docs/ops/migration_playbook.md` (NEW):
  Sections: expand-backfill-contract pattern with worked
  ``ADD COLUMN ... NOT NULL`` example; rationale for raw-SQL
  ``DROP DEFAULT`` over ``op.alter_column(server_default=None)``
  (audit + dialect parity); ``NOT VALID``/``VALIDATE CONSTRAINT``
  two-step for foreign keys on large tables;
  ``MIGRATION_PHASE_<N>`` flag pattern when app code must move with
  the schema; maintenance-window pattern for the rare
  zero-downtime-impossible cases; the CI gate end-to-end and the local
  workflow checklist.

Verification:
  python3 -m pytest tests/test_migration_ci_gate.py -v -p no:pytest-qt
    # 11 passed, 1 skipped (integration test, no Postgres locally)
  python3 deploy/scripts/audit_migrations_postgres_parity.py
    # Every revision shows ERR=0; previously-flagged 20260409_000002
    # and 20260409_000004 now have errors==[].

Prohibitions honored: schemas produced by the migrations are byte-
identical (only the migration code path changed); no zero-downtime
changes were introduced that would require app-code coordination
(so no ``MIGRATION_PHASE_<N>`` flag was added — the playbook documents
the pattern for future use); ``secrets.MIGRATION_GATE_PG_URL`` is
read from GitHub Actions only — never written into the repo; no
SCOPE-external files touched.

EARLIER PROMPT — 2026-04-25 (Wave 7, prompt 23/70 — DB pooling +
                              read-replica routing + transient retry
                              decorator)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Adds a configurable read-replica engine + session factory, and a
transient-error retry decorator with bounded full-jitter backoff applied
to the scoring worker's job-claim and job-finish paths. SQLite remains
the default — `python -m pytest` works unchanged with no env vars.

- `server/fund/database.py` (MODIFY):
  * `resolve_replica_database_url(env=None) -> str` honors the same
    Supabase `?sslmode=require` enforcement as the primary; returns
    "" when `SUPABASE_DB_REPLICA_URL` is unset / blank, signaling
    fallback to primary.
  * `_replica_engine_kwargs_for_url(url)` halves direct-Postgres
    `pool_size` (10 -> 5) and `max_overflow` (20 -> 10); identical
    to primary kwargs for SQLite + pgbouncer (NullPool has no
    useful "half").
  * `create_replica_engine(url) -> Engine` is the standalone
    constructor.
  * `get_read_engine(env=None) -> Engine`: cached production path
    returns the replica when configured (lazily built on first
    call), primary otherwise. Test path (`env={...}`) bypasses the
    cache so individual tests don't pollute one another.
  * `SessionFactory(read_only=False) -> Session`: thin callable
    (NOT a class) that returns a session bound to either engine.
    Resolves engine at call time so flipping
    `SUPABASE_DB_REPLICA_URL` doesn't require a process restart.
  * `retry_transient_db_errors(*, max_attempts=4, base_delay_ms=50,
    max_delay_ms=2000, sleeper=None, rng=None, logger=None)`:
    decorator factory. Retries `OperationalError`,
    `DBAPIError(connection_invalidated=True)`, and Postgres
    SQLSTATEs `40001` / `40P01` / `57P01`. Never retries
    `IntegrityError` or `DataError` (logic bugs). Full-jitter
    exponential backoff capped by `max_delay_ms`; uses
    `secrets.SystemRandom` by default (NOT `random.random()`).
    Emits `db.retry.attempt` (warning) per retry and
    `db.retry.exhausted` (error) on exhaustion. Validates args at
    construction.

- `server/fund/config.py` (MODIFY):
  Adds `SUPABASE_DB_REPLICA_URL` (env `SUPABASE_DB_REPLICA_URL`),
  `DB_RETRY_MAX_ATTEMPTS` (env
  `COHERENCE_FUND_DB_RETRY_MAX_ATTEMPTS`, default 4),
  `DB_RETRY_BASE_DELAY_MS` (default 50),
  `DB_RETRY_MAX_DELAY_MS` (default 2000).

- `server/fund/repositories/__init__.py` (MODIFY):
  Now exports `resolve_read_session(explicit, primary, *,
  read_only) -> contextmanager`. Resolution order: explicit
  caller-supplied session > constructor primary > freshly opened
  `SessionFactory(read_only=...)` (closed on exit). The
  read-replica routing convention is documented in the module
  docstring: writes always use primary; reads MAY opt into replica.

- `server/fund/repositories/portfolio_repository.py` (MODIFY):
  Constructor's `db` is now optional (`Session | None`). Read
  methods accept keyword-only `session=None, read_only=False` and
  route through `resolve_read_session`. Write methods call
  `_require_primary()` which raises a `RuntimeError` if no primary
  session was provided to the constructor — the package never
  silently routes a write to the replica.

- `server/fund/repositories/applications_repository.py` (NEW):
  `ApplicationsReadRepository` — read-only sibling of the
  lifecycle `application_repository.py`. Methods:
  `get_application(...)`, `get_decision(...)`,
  `list_applications_by_founder(...)`, all accepting
  `session=None, read_only=False`.

- `server/fund/scoring_worker.py` (MODIFY):
  Imports `retry_transient_db_errors` and module-level decorated
  helpers `claim_next_job(repository, *, worker_id, lease_seconds)`
  and `mark_job_completed(repository, job_id)` (decorator built
  from settings). `_wrap_repository_with_retry(repo)`
  per-instance monkey-patches the same decorator onto
  `claim_next_scoring_job` / `mark_scoring_job_completed`, applied
  in `process_once` so the service's internal calls inherit the
  retry budget without spreading the decorator across the service
  surface.

- `tests/test_db_retry_decorator.py` (NEW, 18 tests):
  Pure-Python unit tests; no real DB. Synthetic
  `OperationalError` / `DBAPIError` instances with the SQLSTATEs
  the decorator inspects. Deterministic `_RecordingSleeper` +
  `_DeterministicRNG` so call counts and per-attempt delays match
  the predicted full-jitter schedule (`50ms, 100ms, 200ms, ...`
  capped at `max_delay_ms`). Covers: classifier marks
  transient (incl. `57P01`); rejects `IntegrityError` /
  `DataError` / non-DBAPI errors / unknown SQLSTATE;
  retries-then-success; exhaustion raises and logs
  `db.retry.exhausted`; non-transient errors never sleep; backoff
  cap; argument validation; `max_attempts=1` performs no retry;
  decorator preserves `__name__` / `__doc__`.

- `tests/test_read_replica_routing.py` (NEW, 15 tests):
  Pure-Python; no real Postgres. Covers:
  `resolve_replica_database_url` precedence + sslmode behavior;
  `get_read_engine` falls back to primary when unset / returns a
  distinct engine when set / test-path bypasses the cache;
  replica engine kwargs halve direct-Postgres pool / match primary
  for pgbouncer / SQLite; repository routing (`read_only=True` on
  a repo with `db=None` opens a session bound to the replica,
  unset replica falls back to primary).

- `docs/specs/db_pooling_and_retries.md` (NEW):
  Pooling table per dialect, replica SLA (which tables are safe
  on a replica vs. must use primary, with a 30-second lag
  budget); transient-error classification + backoff formula;
  default retry budget table with env-var names; where the
  decorator is applied (worker only — API handlers do NOT inherit
  the decorator).

Verification:
  python3 -m pytest tests/test_db_retry_decorator.py \
                    tests/test_read_replica_routing.py -v -p no:pytest-qt
    # 33 passed
  python3 -m pytest tests/ -p no:pytest-qt -q
    # 729 passed; 9 pre-existing failures unrelated (arm64/x86_64
    # native-extension mismatches with torch / pydantic_core /
    # psycopg2 / PyQt6 on this machine, plus one missing-jsonschema
    # path; none touch the changes in this prompt).

Prohibitions honored: `IntegrityError` / `DataError` are NOT retried;
`max_delay_ms` is a hard cap (validated at construction); decorator
never calls `time.sleep` directly — every sleep goes through the
injectable `sleeper` (defaults to `time.sleep`); no SCOPE-external
files touched. SQLite path preserved.

EARLIER PROMPT — 2026-04-25 (Wave 7, prompt 22/70 — Supabase Postgres
                              connection layer + RLS policy scaffold)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Dialect-aware database URL resolution and engine pooling, plus a
declarative Row-Level-Security (RLS) policy registry and Alembic
migration that installs those policies on Postgres. SQLite remains the
default for unit tests and CI — `python -m pytest` and `alembic upgrade

- `server/fund/database.py` (MODIFY):
  * `resolve_database_url(env=None) -> str` — precedence:
      1. `DATABASE_URL` (explicit override) wins.
      2. `SUPABASE_DB_POOLER_URL` (pgbouncer transaction-pool URL,
         used by long-lived FastAPI / uvicorn workers).
      3. `SUPABASE_DB_URL` (direct connection, used by Alembic).
      4. `COHERENCE_FUND_DATABASE_URL` (legacy) -> SQLite default.
  * `?sslmode=require` is appended in code (not just docs) when the
    chosen URL targets a `*.supabase.co` / `*.supabase.com` host;
    existing `sslmode` values (e.g. `verify-full`) are preserved.
  * `_engine_kwargs_for_url(url)` returns dialect-aware kwargs:
      - SQLite: `connect_args={"check_same_thread": False}`.
      - Direct Postgres: `pool_size=10, max_overflow=20,
        pool_pre_ping=True, pool_recycle=1800`.
      - Supabase pgbouncer pooler (host contains `pooler` OR
        `pgbouncer=true` query param): `poolclass=NullPool` plus
        `pool_pre_ping=True` so SQLAlchemy does not pool on top of
        pgbouncer transaction-mode (which corrupts session state).
  * `safe_url_for_logging(url) -> str` returns
    `<dialect>://<user>@<host>:<port>/<db>` with the password
    stripped — for any code path that wants to log the active URL.

- `server/fund/config.py` (MODIFY):
  Adds optional fields `DATABASE_URL_EXPLICIT`,
  `SUPABASE_DB_POOLER_URL`, `SUPABASE_DB_URL`,
  `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY`. Legacy `DATABASE_URL` field is left
  intact so `alembic/env.py` and existing tests continue to work
  unchanged.

- `server/fund/security/rls.py` (NEW):
  Declarative `RLSPolicy` dataclass + `RLS_POLICIES` registry.
  Initial coverage:
    * `fund_applications` — `authenticated SELECT` gated on
      `auth.uid() = founder_user_id`; `service_role ALL`.
    * `fund_decisions` — `authenticated SELECT` via subquery on the
      owning application; `service_role ALL`.
    * `fund_event_outbox`, `fund_idempotency_records` —
      `service_role ALL` only.
    * `argument_artifacts` — `authenticated SELECT` via owning
      application subquery; `service_role ALL`.
  `apply_rls_policies(connection, policies=RLS_POLICIES)` emits
  `ALTER TABLE ... ENABLE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` then idempotent
  `DROP POLICY IF EXISTS` + `CREATE POLICY` on Postgres; no-op on
  SQLite (and any non-Postgres dialect). `revert_rls_policies(...)`,
  `render_policy_ddl(...)`, and `rls_tables(...)` round out the API.
  Validation in `RLSPolicy.__post_init__` rejects unknown commands,
  empty role lists, and INSERT policies without `with_check_clause`.

- `server/fund/security/` (PACKAGE CONVERSION):
  Former `server/fund/security.py` is now `security/middleware.py`.
  `security/__init__.py` is a slim lazy `__getattr__` shim that
  forwards attribute access to `.middleware`. Existing
  `from coherence_engine.server.fund.security import X` imports
  continue to work; importing `security.rls` does NOT drag in the
  FastAPI / pydantic dependency chain.

- `alembic/versions/20260425_000001_rls_policies.py` (NEW):
  Down-revision `20260417_000006`. Postgres-only — calls
  `apply_rls_policies(bind, RLS_POLICIES)` on upgrade and
  `revert_rls_policies(...)` on downgrade. Exits cleanly on SQLite
  with no-op semantics.

- `tests/test_database_dialect_selection.py` (NEW):
  Pure-unit (no real DB connection). Parametrized precedence tests,
  sslmode-require enforcement, sslmode preservation when already
  set, per-dialect engine-kwarg assertions
  (SQLite / direct Postgres / pooler / `pgbouncer=true` query param),
  and password-stripping in `safe_url_for_logging`.

- `tests/test_rls_policies.py` (NEW):
  Declarative-only. Asserts each registry entry is a valid
  `RLSPolicy`, expected protected-table coverage, the
  `service_role ALL` invariant per protected table, validation
  rejects bogus command / empty roles / INSERT-without-WITH-CHECK,
  `apply_rls_policies` against `sqlite:///:memory:` does not raise,
  and a pinned-DDL snapshot test that fails on registry drift.

- `docs/specs/rls_policies.md` (NEW):
  Why RLS is required even with FastAPI in front of Postgres, the
  protected-table table, install path, drift-detection note, and
  the prompt 25 follow-up (`founder_user_id` column).

- `.env.example` (NEW):
  Documents `DATABASE_URL`, `SUPABASE_DB_POOLER_URL`,
  `SUPABASE_DB_URL`, `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY`, the legacy
  `COHERENCE_FUND_DATABASE_URL`, and service-identity vars. No
  Supabase project URL is hardcoded.

Verification:
  python3 -m pytest tests/test_database_dialect_selection.py \
                    tests/test_rls_policies.py -v -p no:pytest-qt
  PYTHONPATH=.. python3 -m alembic upgrade head    # SQLite no-op for RLS
  python3 -c "from coherence_engine.server.fund.security.rls import \
              RLS_POLICIES, render_policy_ddl; \
              print(len(RLS_POLICIES), 'policies')"

Prohibitions honored: SQLite path preserved (still the default);
URLs are never logged in full (stripping helper provided); no
Supabase project URL hardcoded; SCOPE files only — except for the
required `security.py -> security/__init__.py` package conversion,
