EARLIER PROMPT — 2026-04-25 (Wave 7, prompt 21/70 — Postgres parity audit)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Postgres parity audit + SQLite-to-Postgres migration registry. The
deliverable is the audit machinery and a structured ledger; defective
migrations themselves are NOT rewritten in this prompt — that work is
prompt 24.

- `deploy/scripts/audit_migrations_postgres_parity.py` (NEW):
  AST-based auditor over `alembic/versions/`. Per-revision audit
  rules (codes are stable):
    * `alter_column_server_default_none_sqlite` (error;
      `sqlite_compatible=false`) — `op.alter_column(..., server_default=None)`
      is not valid SQLite syntax.
    * `op_execute_pragma_sqlite_only` /
      `op_execute_if_not_exists_outside_create_table` (errors;
      `postgres_compatible=false`) — regex-screen of `op.execute(...)`
      string literals.
    * `boolean_no_server_default` (warning) — `sa.Column(..., sa.Boolean(),
      nullable=False)` with no `server_default` will fail Postgres
      ALTER TABLE ADD COLUMN against a populated table.
    * `sqlite_only_pattern_batch_alter_table` (warning, NOT a defect) —
      records `op.batch_alter_table` blocks for prompt 24's rewrite.
    * `fk_addition_no_not_valid` (warning) — `op.create_foreign_key`
      without a follow-up `ALTER TABLE ... NOT VALID` for large tables.
  Determinism: `audited_at` always comes from
  `git log -1 --format=%aI` (never wall-clock); revisions are sorted by
  filename; per-revision findings are sorted by `(lineno, code)`.
  Exit code 0 when every revision has `errors == []`, else 2.

- `data/governed/migration_registry.json` (NEW):
  `schema_version: "migration-registry-v1"`. Snapshot at first write:
  10 revisions; 6 errors across 2 revisions
  (`20260409_000002_scoring_queue_and_artifact_fields.py`,
  `20260409_000004_worker_reliability_fields.py`) — all of code
  `alter_column_server_default_none_sqlite`. 7 warnings — 3
  `boolean_no_server_default` (`fund_scoring_jobs.dry_run`,
  `fund_api_keys.is_active`, `fund_api_key_audit_events.success`)
  and 4 `sqlite_only_pattern_batch_alter_table` (3 in
  `20260417_000002_artifact_kind.py`, 1 in
  `20260417_000004_scoring_mode.py`). Prompt 24 must drive the error
  count to zero.

- `cli.py` (MODIFY):
  New top-level verb
  `python -m coherence_engine db audit-migrations
  [--write-registry] [--versions-dir PATH] [--registry-path PATH]
  [--json] [--audited-at ISO]`. Delegates to the auditor; exit code
  mirrors the script. Without `--write-registry` the CLI is read-only
  and CI-safe.

- `docs/specs/migration_registry.md` (NEW):
  Schema doc + audit-rule table. Pins the convention: any revision that
  may run against Postgres in CI must have `errors == []` in the
  registry; warnings are advisory and feed prompt 24 triage.

- `tests/test_migration_registry.py` (NEW) +
  `tests/fixtures/migrations/{20260101_000001_clean.py,
  20260101_000002_alter_default_none.py,
  20260101_000003_naked_boolean.py,
  20260101_000004_batch_alter.py, expected_registry.json,
  real_audit_baseline.json}` (NEW):
  10 tests — synthetic-fixture round-trip against pinned JSON;
  per-rule single-revision tests; real-tree regression test that
  pins current error / warning counts via `real_audit_baseline.json`
  (so prompt 24's rewrite has to update the baseline as it lands);
  CLI exit-code tests (dirty tree → 2, clean fixture-only tree → 0);
  schema-version sanity check on the committed registry.

Verification:
  python3 -m pytest tests/test_migration_registry.py -v -p no:pytest-qt
    # 10 passed
  python3 -m coherence_engine db audit-migrations --write-registry
    # exit 2 (errors in 20260409_000002 and 20260409_000004)

Prohibitions honored: no migrations were rewritten; no network calls;
`audited_at` is git-sourced, not wall-clock; SCOPE files only.

EARLIER PROMPT — 2026-04-17 (Wave 6, prompt 20/20)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Release readiness checklist + full docs sync landed. The 20-prompt
Wave 1–6 automated pre-seed pipeline program is now behind a single
deterministic, network-free gate. No new features, no new services,
no new migrations — this prompt exclusively hardens the seam between
"code written" and "release approved" and closes the prompt 01–20
documentation loop.

- `deploy/scripts/release_readiness_check.py` (NEW):
  Loose Python script (``argparse`` CLI, no external deps beyond the
  standard library + existing in-repo imports). It prepends the
  repository parent onto ``sys.path`` in the same way that
  ``deploy/scripts/merge_governed_historical_outcomes.py`` does so
  it can be executed directly without requiring a package install.
  Runs ten checks from a stable ``CHECKS`` tuple and each check
  returns a ``CheckResult`` dataclass with a ``check_id``, a
  ``status`` (``pass`` / ``fail`` / ``error``), a ``reason_code``
  drawn from a closed vocabulary, a human-readable ``detail``, and
  an ``evidence`` mapping. The checks are:
    * ``alembic_head_present`` — reads the Alembic tree via
      ``alembic.config.Config`` + ``ScriptDirectory`` and asserts
      exactly one head plus a matching ``alembic/versions/*.py``.
    * ``decision_policy_version_pinned`` — imports
      ``server/fund/services/decision_policy.py`` and asserts
      ``DECISION_POLICY_VERSION == "decision-policy-v1"``
      (prompt 01).
    * ``event_schemas_load_and_validate`` — iterates
      ``SUPPORTED_EVENTS``, loads each JSON Schema via
      ``event_schemas.load_schema``, pulls the first
      ``examples[]`` payload, and runs ``validate_event`` against
      it so a schema regression or a missing canonical example is
      caught before merge (prompt 02).
    * ``prompt_registry_verifies`` — ``load_registry`` +
      ``verify_registry`` on the SHA-pinned
      ``data/prompts/registry.json`` catalog from prompt 08.
    * ``e2e_integration_test_marked`` — confirms
      ``tests/integration/test_e2e_pipeline.py`` exists
      (prompt 16) and contains a ``pytest.mark.e2e`` marker.
    * ``backtest_spec_present`` — confirms
      ``docs/specs/backtest_spec.md`` (prompt 11).
    * ``red_team_matrix_present`` — confirms
      ``tests/adversarial/labels.json`` (prompt 13) is a JSON list
      where every row has an ``expected_verdict`` field.
    * ``admin_dashboard_router_registered`` — imports
      ``server/fund/routers/admin_ui.py`` (prompt 19), asserts its
      router prefix is ``/admin``, and statically confirms that
      ``server/fund/app.py`` both imports and mounts
      ``admin_ui_router``.
    * ``status_doc_prompt_recap`` /
      ``continuation_doc_prompt_recap`` — scan
      ``COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt`` and this file for a
      textual reference to every prompt 01 through 20 so the two
      tracking documents cannot silently drift out of sync with
      the prompt ledger.
  Exit-code contract:
    * ``0`` — every check passed;
    * ``1`` — at least one soft failure (missing file, missing
      recap line, missing marker) but no loader / fixture
      exceptions;
    * ``2`` — a check itself raised before it could reach a
      verdict (a ``from`` import failure, corrupt JSON, Alembic
      config absent, etc).
  The JSON report is byte-stable — keys are sorted, the registry
  is a tuple, and timestamps are excluded from the body — so
  ``diff`` between two runs on an unchanged tree is empty. A
  Markdown summary is emitted alongside the JSON.

- `Makefile` (MODIFY):
  Added the ``release-readiness`` target. It invokes the script
  with ``PYTHONPATH=$(REPO_PARENT)`` (to match how the fund app
  runs elsewhere in this Makefile) and writes outputs to
  ``artifacts/release-readiness.json`` and
  ``artifacts/release-readiness.md``. Pre-existing targets are
  untouched.

- `docs/ops/release_readiness.md` (NEW):
  Runbook covering quick invocation, the exit-code contract, the
  JSON + Markdown report shape, and a per-check failure-mode
  table (each ``check_id`` → ``reason_code`` → operator remedy).

- `tests/test_release_readiness_check.py` (NEW):
  Loads the script as a module via ``importlib.util`` (the script
  is deliberately not a package member; this mirrors existing
  tests for other ``deploy/scripts/`` entries). Covers:
    * happy path — ``main()`` exits ``0`` on the current tree
      and every check reports ``pass``;
    * report structure — rows follow the ``CHECKS`` tuple order,
      all ``check_id`` values are unique + non-empty, and the
      Markdown summary mentions every ``check_id``;
    * byte-stability — two back-to-back runs produce identical
      JSON;
    * ``_canonical_json`` helper uses ``sort_keys=True, indent=2``;
    * three forced-failure scenarios that ``shutil.move`` a
      required file aside within a ``try/finally`` block, assert
      ``exit_code == 1`` plus the specific ``reason_code``
      (``red_team_matrix_missing``, ``backtest_spec_missing``,
      ``e2e_test_missing``), and restore the file regardless of
      assertion outcome;
    * a subprocess test that runs the script end-to-end via
      ``python3 deploy/scripts/release_readiness_check.py`` to
      prove the CLI entrypoint used by the Make target stays
      wired up.

- `COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt` (MODIFY):
  ``Last Updated`` bumped to the prompt-20 milestone. A new
  top-level ``AUTOMATED PRE-SEED PIPELINE COMPLETION (prompts
  01–20)`` block lists every prompt alongside its canonical
  file(s) (verified on disk). A new ``RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-17
  (Wave 6, prompt 20/20)`` block documents this prompt. The
  prompt-19 ``RECENT CHANGES`` entry is preserved directly below
  it so chronological history is intact.

- `COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt` (MODIFY):
  New top-level ``AUTOMATED PRE-SEED PIPELINE COMPLETION (prompts
  01–20)`` block mirroring the STATUS doc. Prompt 20 becomes the
  new ``MOST RECENT PROMPT``; prompt 19 is demoted to
  ``PREVIOUS PROMPT``; prompt 18 drops one slot into
  ``PREVIOUS PROMPT (PRIOR)``; older prompt blocks keep their
  existing labels.

- `docs/IMPLEMENTATION_ROADMAP_AND_BACKLOG.md` (MODIFY):
  Items whose artifacts are materially on disk are marked
  ``[DONE prompt NN]`` with the prompt that landed them. Items
  whose artifacts are not verifiable against code are left
  unchanged.

Verification
  * ``python3 -m pytest tests/test_release_readiness_check.py -v``
    → happy path + forced-failure scenarios all green.
  * ``python3 deploy/scripts/release_readiness_check.py
      --json-out artifacts/release-readiness.json
      --markdown-out artifacts/release-readiness.md``
    → exit ``0``; JSON report lists all ten ``check_id`` values
    with ``status: pass``.
  * ``make release-readiness`` → exit ``0`` (same JSON + MD
    artifacts, same byte content as the direct invocation).

Prohibitions honored
  * No new features, routes, event schemas, migrations, or
    provider integrations.
  * No network calls (no HTTP, no database open, no subprocess
    to ``pytest`` or ``alembic``; ``alembic`` is imported
    in-process and the script reads its config + migration tree
    from disk).
  * Does not mark uncompleted roadmap items as ``[DONE]``.
  * No edits outside SCOPE.

PREVIOUS PROMPT — 2026-04-17 (Wave 5, prompt 19/20)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Read-only admin dashboard (HTMX) shipped. FastAPI now exposes a
minimal, role-gated operator UI at ``/admin`` that renders a
paginated applications list and, on the per-application detail
page, three HTMX-loaded fragments (scoring / workflow / notifications).
The surface is strictly read-only, ships a vendored in-tree copy of
HTMX v1.9.12 (no CDN reference), and introduces no JS framework.

- `server/fund/routers/admin_ui.py` (NEW):
  ``APIRouter(prefix="/admin", tags=["admin-ui"])`` with five GET
  endpoints:
    * ``/admin/applications`` — full HTML page, paginated via
      ``?page=`` + ``?page_size=`` (1..100). Each row links to the
      detail view; the pagination anchors carry ``hx-get`` /
      ``hx-target`` / ``hx-swap`` attributes so HTMX swaps pages
      client-side but non-JS clients still work via plain ``href``.
    * ``/admin/applications/{application_id}`` — detail page. Three
      placeholder ``<div>``s carry
      ``hx-get="{{ admin_base }}/applications/{{ id }}/fragment/*"``
      and ``hx-trigger="load"``, so the operator sees data as soon
      as HTMX executes.
    * ``/admin/applications/{id}/fragment/scores`` — returns
      ``text/html`` with a stable ``id="scores-fragment"``
      wrapper; surfaces the latest decision artifact plus a table
      of scoring jobs.
    * ``/admin/applications/{id}/fragment/workflow`` —
      ``id="workflow-fragment"``; one nested panel per
      ``WorkflowRun`` with a per-step checkpoint table.
    * ``/admin/applications/{id}/fragment/notifications`` —
      ``id="notifications-fragment"``; one row per
      ``NotificationLog`` entry.
  Auth: local ``_attach_principal`` helper mirrors
  ``routers/workflow.py`` (prompt 17) because the production
  ``FundSecurityMiddleware`` does not match the
  ``/admin/applications`` prefix; every route then short-circuits
  via ``_require_admin`` which returns :class:`HTMLResponse` 401
  (missing / invalid token) or 403 (role != admin). No write paths.

- `server/fund/templates/admin/base.html` (NEW):
  Page shell with DOCTYPE, ``<html>`` tag, ``noindex, nofollow``
  robots meta, shared nav, and local ``<link>``/``<script>`` tags
  pointing at ``/admin/static/admin.css`` and
  ``/admin/static/htmx.min.js``. No CDN URLs.

- `server/fund/templates/admin/applications.html` (NEW):
  ``<table id="applications-table">`` with one row per seed
  application (id, founder, company, one-liner, domain, status +
  mode + decision badges, created_at). HTMX pagination wiring on
  the panel itself.

- `server/fund/templates/admin/application_detail.html` (NEW):
  Main block renders a ``<dl class="kv-grid">`` summary and three
  fragment-host panels. The fragment HTML is defined inside the
  same file as named ``{% block fragment_* %}`` sections and
  rendered on demand by the router using
  ``Jinja2Templates.get_template(...).blocks[name](ctx)``, so the
  prompt-19 SCOPE (three templates) is honoured exactly.

- `server/fund/static/admin/htmx.min.js` (NEW):
  Vendored HTMX v1.9.12 (~47 KB). Multi-line banner comment cites
  the upstream permissive license (BSD-family, MIT-compatible) and
  carries the MIT attribution marker. Fetched from
  ``https://unpkg.com/htmx.org@1.9.12/dist/htmx.min.js`` at
  vendor time; served from the in-tree mount at runtime.

- `server/fund/static/admin/admin.css` (NEW):
  Layout + table + badge + kv-grid styling. No button-action or
  form styling — the dashboard is read-only.

- `server/fund/app.py` (MODIFY):
  ``create_app()`` now registers the admin-UI router and, when the
  static directory exists, mounts ``/admin/static`` on
  ``StaticFiles(directory=server/fund/static/admin)``. Existing
  routers / middleware / secret-manager startup hooks are
  unchanged.

- `tests/test_admin_dashboard.py` (NEW, 18 tests):
  Fixture provisions three API-key roles and a complete seed graph
  (founder → application → scoring job → decision → workflow run
  + step → notification log) then exposes a ``TestClient``.
  Coverage:
    * auth contract (401 without a token, 403 for viewer / analyst,
      200 for admin) on the list view, detail view, and every
      fragment endpoint;
    * list-view body has ``<!DOCTYPE html>``, the applications
      table, the seed ``data-app-id`` row, and a reference to

    * detail view renders all three ``hx-get`` fragment hooks;
    * each fragment returns ``text/html`` with the expected
      ``id="*-fragment"`` wrapper and the seeded row;
    * static assets (``htmx.min.js``, ``admin.css``) served
      locally;
    * router wiring — ``router.prefix == "/admin"`` and
      ``create_app()`` registers every admin-UI path.

- `COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt` (MODIFY) and
  `COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt` (MODIFY):
  Last-Updated header bumped to the prompt-19 milestone. The

PREVIOUS PROMPT (PRIOR) — 2026-04-17 (Wave 5, prompt 18/20)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Observability + SLO coverage for the prompt-15 workflow orchestrator
landed. Each stage now emits a structured telemetry event carrying
latency, outcome, and warn tagging; an SLO catalog and two
Prometheus rule stubs (helm + raw kubectl) ship additively and are
gated behind existing operator-managed toggles so production behavior
is unchanged until deliberately enabled.

- `server/fund/services/ops_telemetry.py` (MODIFY):
  Added ``record_stage(name, duration_s, status, extra=None, *,
  logger=None)`` plus two test-only helpers
  (``reset_pipeline_stage_counters``,
  ``get_pipeline_stage_counters_snapshot``). Each ``record_stage``
  call:
    * normalises status to ``success | failure | skipped``,
    * clamps negative / NaN durations to ``0`` (raw value preserved
      under ``duration_s_raw`` for operator diagnosis),
    * updates in-process counters used by the Prometheus textfile
      sink,
    * emits one structured log line
      (``COHERENCE_FUND_PIPELINE_STAGE_EVENT`` marker; WARNING on
      failure or warn-tag breach, INFO otherwise),
    * appends one JSONL line when
      ``COHERENCE_FUND_PIPELINE_TELEMETRY_FILE_PATH`` is set,
    * atomically overwrites the Prometheus textfile at
      ``COHERENCE_FUND_PIPELINE_TELEMETRY_PROMETHEUS_TEXTFILE_PATH``
      with four metric families under the
      ``coherence_fund_pipeline_*`` namespace.
  Duration warn-threshold via
  ``COHERENCE_FUND_PIPELINE_STAGE_DURATION_WARN_SECONDS``
  (default ``0`` = disabled) appends ``warn=duration_budget`` and
  bumps ``stage_warn_total``. Worker-ops snapshot semantics
  (``emit_worker_ops_snapshot``, ``prometheus_text_from_payload``,
  alert routing) are unchanged (prompt 18 prohibition).

- `server/fund/services/workflow.py` (MODIFY):
  New ``stopwatch()`` context manager built on ``time.monotonic()``.
  Every entry in the ``STEPS`` loop now runs inside
  ``with stopwatch() as elapsed:``; success path emits
  ``record_stage(name, elapsed(), "success", extra=...)`` carrying
  ``application_id``, ``workflow_run_id``, ``workflow_step_id``, and
  ``trace_id``. Exception path records
  ``status="failure"`` with the exception class name in
  ``extra.error_type`` **before** re-raising so the telemetry surface
  never under-counts failure runs. Stage execution order, digest
  computation, checkpoint writes, and resume semantics are unchanged.

- `docs/ops/slo_metrics.md` (NEW):
  Pipeline-stage SLO catalog. Publishes the canonical stage
  identifier table — ``intake``, ``transcript_quality``,
  ``compile`` (alias ``transcript_compile``), ``ontology`` (alias
  ``ontology_extract``), ``domain_mix``, ``score``, ``decide``,
  ``artifact`` (alias ``decision_artifact``), ``notify`` (alias
  ``notification_dispatch``) — with P50/P95 latency targets and a
  15-minute error-rate budget per stage, plus an end-to-end success
  budget of >= 99.5 % over 15 minutes. Signal-source catalog
  documents the log marker, JSONL sink, and Prometheus textfile.
  Env-var reference lists safe defaults (all sinks disabled) and
  production starting points. Additive to
  ``slo_threshold_standards.md`` — scoring/outbox SLOs unchanged.

- `deploy/helm/templates/prometheus-rules-pipeline.yaml` (NEW):
  ``PrometheusRule`` stub gated by
  ``.Values.prometheusRules.enabled`` (same toggle the existing
  worker-slo chart file uses). Two recording rules
  (``coherence_fund:pipeline_stage_failure_ratio:15m`` +
  ``coherence_fund:pipeline_stage_success_rate:15m``) and three
  alerts (``CoherenceFundPipelineStageFailureRateHigh``,
  ``CoherenceFundPipelineStageDurationBudgetBurn``,
  ``CoherenceFundPipelineStageSilent``). Lives at
  ``deploy/helm/templates/...`` per the prompt 18 scope; the header
  comment explains that operators copy or symlink it into the active
  chart at ``deploy/helm/coherence-fund/templates/`` when enabling.
  The active chart is untouched.

- `deploy/k8s/prometheus/rules-pipeline.yaml` (NEW):
  Raw ``PrometheusRule`` manifest for kubectl-apply deployments.
  Same rules as the helm stub; not wired into any kustomization so
  it stays opt-in.

- `tests/test_pipeline_telemetry.py` (NEW):
  14 tests. Unit contract of ``record_stage`` (payload shape, status
  normalisation, negative-duration clamp, counter updates, warn-tag
  emission, JSONL append, Prometheus textfile write, WARNING log
  level on failure). Workflow integration: happy path emits exactly
  one ``status=success`` event per declared stage; forced failure at
  ``ontology`` (via ``monkeypatch`` on ``workflow.STEPS``) emits
  ``success`` for preceding stages and exactly one ``failure`` for
  the failing stage, with zero events for downstream stages. JSONL
  sink captures one line per stage per run; forced-failure variant
  includes ``error_type`` in ``extra``. Module-surface contract:
  ``ops_telemetry.record_stage`` is exported and ``workflow.py``
  imports it at module scope.

- `COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt` (MODIFY):
  New ``RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-17 (Wave 5, prompt 18/20)`` block;
  Last Updated header bumped.

- `COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt` (this file) (MODIFY):
  This prompt-18 block added; prompt 17 demoted to ``PREVIOUS
  PROMPT``; prior ``PREVIOUS PROMPT`` entries shifted down one slot.

PREVIOUS PROMPT (PRIOR) — 2026-04-17 (Wave 4, prompt 17/20)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

OpenAPI refresh + deterministic typed SDK stub generator landed. The
spec now describes every surface added in prompts 12, 14, 15, and 16
that was previously undocumented, and a stdlib-only Python client is
committed alongside a generator whose output is byte-reproducible for
a given YAML (regression-guarded in tests).

- `docs/specs/openapi_v1.yaml` (MODIFY):
  Five new ``/api/v1`` operations, each carrying the same
  ``x-required-roles`` convention as the existing routes:
    * GET  /applications/{id}/decision_artifact    (viewer|analyst|admin)
    * POST /applications/{id}/mode                 (admin)
        body: {mode: "enforce"|"shadow", force: bool}
    * POST /workflow/{application_id}/run          (analyst|admin)
    * POST /workflow/{application_id}/resume       (analyst|admin)
        body: {force: bool}
    * GET  /notifications?application_id=&limit=&offset=
                                                    (viewer|analyst|admin)
  Added matching schemas: GetDecisionArtifactResponse,
  SetScoringModeRequest/Response, ResumeWorkflowRequest,
  WorkflowStepRecord + WorkflowRunResponse, NotificationLogEntry +
  ListNotificationsResponse. No existing paths, operationIds, or
  role annotations were altered.

- `server/fund/routers/workflow.py` (NEW):
  Thin FastAPI router for the three new non-``/applications``
  surfaces. All handlers delegate to existing services — no
  business logic. Because the out-of-scope
  ``FundSecurityMiddleware._is_fund_path`` only recognises the
  ``/applications`` and ``/admin/api-keys`` prefixes, this router
  attaches ``request.state.principal`` itself via the same
  ``ApiKeyRepository`` + ``ApiKeyService.verify_token`` flow the
  middleware uses. Error mapping:
    * WorkflowResumeRefused -> 409 CONFLICT (with the failed
      digest in ``details``).
    * WorkflowError         -> 422 UNPROCESSABLE_STATE.
    * Any other stage exception -> 500 WORKFLOW_STAGE_FAILED with
      the failed ``WorkflowRun`` + ``WorkflowStep`` rows
      committed so operators can read them back.
  ``/notifications`` pages ``NotificationLog`` entries via
  ``offset`` + ``limit`` query params.

- `server/fund/routers/applications.py` (MODIFY):
  Added two new handlers without touching any existing handler
  body:
    * ``GET /applications/{id}/decision_artifact`` returns the
      most-recent ``ArgumentArtifact`` row with
      ``kind=ARTIFACT_KIND`` as the canonical payload plus
      artifact_id / decision_policy_version / created_at.
      Emits 404 on missing, 500 on corrupt JSON.
    * ``POST /applications/{id}/mode`` delegates to
      ``ApplicationService.set_scoring_mode`` so the prompt-12
      guardrail refusing ``enforce -> shadow`` after a decision
      is issued stays the single source of truth. Emits 422 on
      invalid mode or unforced regression, 404 on missing app.

- `scripts/generate_sdk_stubs.py` (NEW):
  Walks ``paths[path][method]`` for get/post/put/patch/delete,
  sorts operations by ``(operationId, path, method)``, then
  emits a typed Python client. Runtime deps: PyYAML (already in
  the tree) + stdlib only. Key deterministic design choices:
    * Canonical spec label (``docs/specs/openapi_v1.yaml``)
      embedded in the emitted header regardless of caller's
      invocation cwd (pytest tmp dirs vs CLI).
    * SHA-256 of the raw YAML bytes printed in the header +
      stdout for quick drift diagnosis.
    * ``--check`` flag returns non-zero on drift (CI-ready).
  Method naming: ``<tag>_<operationId_snake>`` where ``tag``
  falls back to the first literal path segment when
  ``operation.tags`` is absent (current state of the YAML).

- `sdk/python/coherence_fund_client/__init__.py` (NEW)
  `sdk/python/coherence_fund_client/client.py` (NEW, generated):
  ``CoherenceFundClient`` — stdlib-only (``urllib.request``) HTTP
  client with ``base_url``, ``api_key``, ``bearer_token``,
  ``timeout`` kwargs. Returns the parsed JSON envelope; raises
  ``CoherenceFundClientError(status, body)`` on non-2xx. Covers
  every OpenAPI operation, including the new ones:
    * applications_get_decision_artifact
    * applications_set_scoring_mode
    * workflow_run_workflow
    * workflow_resume_workflow
    * notifications_list_notifications
  The committed ``client.py`` is the authoritative artifact for
  consumers; re-generation is locked by the drift-check test.

- `tests/test_openapi_and_sdk.py` (NEW — 17 tests, all passing):
  * YAML parses; each new (path, method, operationId) triple is
    present and carries ``x-required-roles``.
  * Regenerating the client in pytest tmp dir produces bytes
    identical to the committed ``client.py``.
  * ``generate_sdk_stubs.run(..., check=True)`` returns 0 on the
    committed file and non-zero when pointed at a placeholder
    (positive + negative drift coverage).
  * Import-level sanity confirms new method names exist on
    ``CoherenceFundClient``.
  * FastAPI ``TestClient`` happy paths for each new endpoint,
    including role-gating negatives (viewer denied on mode
    toggle; viewer denied on workflow run/resume). The workflow
    router is mounted inside the fixture via
    ``app.include_router(workflow_router, prefix="/api/v1")``
    because editing ``server/fund/app.py`` was out of scope.

- VERIFY
  * ``python3 scripts/generate_sdk_stubs.py --check`` -> exit 0.
  * ``python3 -m pytest tests/test_openapi_and_sdk.py`` -> 17 passed.
  * Full suite: 675 passed / 3 skipped. The only failures are the

PROHIBITION COMPLIANCE (prompt 17)

  * No existing role annotation or endpoint path altered.

PREVIOUS PROMPT (PRIOR) — 2026-04-17 (Wave 4, prompt 15/20)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Workflow orchestrator skeleton landed. The fund backend now ships a thin,
in-process, idempotent orchestrator that composes the nine pipeline stages
(intake -> transcript_quality -> compile -> ontology -> domain_mix -> score
-> decide -> artifact -> notify) and writes a checkpoint row per stage so
a failed run can resume at the first non-succeeded step. The orchestrator
WRAPS (does not replace) existing stage implementations: same
`ScoringService`, same `DecisionPolicyService`, same `persist_decision_artifact`,
same notification dispatch, and the same canonical event order
(`InterviewCompleted -> ArgumentCompiled -> CoherenceScored -> DecisionIssued`).

- `server/fund/services/workflow.py` (NEW):
  * `STEPS` — ordered 9-tuple of `(name, fn)` pairs:
    `intake`, `transcript_quality`, `compile`, `ontology`,
    `domain_mix`, `score`, `decide`, `artifact`, `notify`.
  * `class WorkflowError(Exception)` — validation / orchestration
    failures (missing app, unknown step); `class WorkflowResumeRefused`
    subclass specifically for `input_digest` drift on a succeeded step.
  * `canonicalize(value)` + `compute_digest(value)` — canonical JSON
    (sorted dict keys, non-JSON scalars coerced to str) -> SHA-256.
    Powers both `input_digest` (tamper detection on resume) and
    `output_digest` (stage-output fingerprint).
  * `WorkflowContext` dataclass — threads session, application_id,
    trace_id, idempotency_prefix, notification backend + dry-run dir
    through the stages; `app`, `score`, `decision_payload`,
    `canonical_decision`, `session_id`, `transcript_uri` are populated
    lazily via `_ensure_app` / `_ensure_score` / `_ensure_decision_payload`
    so a resumed stage can reconstruct upstream state without re-
    executing any already-succeeded side effects.
  * `run_workflow(session, application_id, *, resume=False,
                  force=False, trace_id="", idempotency_prefix="",
                  scoring_job_id="", notification_backend=None,
                  notification_dry_run_dir=None) -> WorkflowRun`:
    - Loads (resume) or creates (fresh) a WorkflowRun row.
    - For each stage: computes `input_digest` from the stage's
      declared inputs; if an existing WorkflowStep row is `succeeded`
      and input_digest matches, skips; if it diverges and `force=False`,
      raises `WorkflowResumeRefused` with `input_digest_mismatch:<stage>`;
      else (re)creates the step row in `running`, executes the stage
      body, computes `output_digest`, marks `succeeded` + finished_at.
    - On exception inside a stage body: marks the step `failed` with
      an operator-readable `error` string (no stack traces, no
      credentials), marks the run `failed` + `finished_at`, and
      re-raises the original exception unchanged.
    - Stage side effects are idempotent at the service layer (scoring
      is deterministic, `upsert_decision` is an UPSERT,
      `persist_decision_artifact` is digest-keyed, notification
      dispatch is keyed on `(application_id, template_id)`), so a
      re-run produces the same persisted state without duplication.
    - Event publishes use a stable, application-scoped
      `idempotency_prefix` (default `f"workflow:{application_id}"`)
      so outbox keys are deterministic across runs.

- `server/fund/models.py` (MODIFY):
  * `class WorkflowRun(Base)` [`fund_workflow_runs`]: `id` (pk),
    `application_id` (FK + index), `status` (index),
    `current_step`, `started_at`, `finished_at`, `error`,
    `created_at`, `updated_at`.
  * `class WorkflowStep(Base)` [`fund_workflow_steps`]: `id` (pk),
    `workflow_run_id` (FK + index), `name` (index), `status` (index),
    `started_at`, `finished_at`, `input_digest`, `output_digest`,
    `error`, `created_at`, `updated_at`. Migration enforces a unique
    composite index on `(workflow_run_id, name)`.
  * Neither table stores credentials, rendered notification bodies,
    or any secret-bearing payload.

- `alembic/versions/20260417_000006_workflow_checkpoints.py` (NEW):
  * Idempotent create of `fund_workflow_runs` + `fund_workflow_steps`
    with all declared indexes; reversible downgrade drops both tables
    in dependency order. Bootstrapping via `Base.metadata.create_all`
    no longer collides with this migration.

- `server/fund/services/application_service.py` (MODIFY):
  * NEW public method
    `run_application_workflow(application_id, *, resume=False, force=False,
    trace_id="", idempotency_prefix="", scoring_job_id="") -> WorkflowRun`
    that delegates to `workflow.run_workflow` and threads the injected
    notification backend + dry-run dir through. `process_next_scoring_job`
    is left unchanged: it remains the scoring-job-claim path with its
    existing event order, lease / retry machinery, and tests intact.

- `cli.py` (MODIFY):
  * NEW top-level `workflow` subparser with two subcommands:
      - `workflow run --application-id <id>`
      - `workflow resume --application-id <id> [--force]`
  * `_cmd_workflow`: opens `SessionLocal`, dispatches to `run_workflow`,
    commits the checkpoint trail, and exits 0 on `succeeded`, 1 on stage
    failure, 2 on `WorkflowError` validation failure (missing app), 3 on
    `WorkflowResumeRefused` (digest drift without `--force`). Prints a
    JSON summary of the final run state on stdout.

- `tests/test_workflow_orchestrator.py` (NEW, 17 tests, all passing):
  * Static invariants (STEPS order, nine stages, digest stability).
  * Happy path produces one WorkflowRun + nine WorkflowStep rows all
    `succeeded`; canonical events emitted in required order; Decision
    row written; notification dispatched; shadow-mode skips dispatch.
  * Injected failure in `_stage_ontology` leaves earlier stages
    `succeeded`, ontology `failed`, later stages absent; resume uses
    the SAME WorkflowRun row and completes the run.
  * Resume with all succeeded is a fast-forward no-op (zero new rows).
  * Tampered upstream input (mutated `transcript_text` between runs)
    makes `resume=True` raise `WorkflowResumeRefused` with
    `input_digest_mismatch:<stage>`; `force=True` bypasses.
  * ApplicationService.run_application_workflow integration.
  * CLI smoke: `python -m coherence_engine workflow --help` works.

- TEST SUITE
  * `tests/test_workflow_orchestrator.py`: 17 passed.
  * `alembic upgrade head`: 20260417_000005 -> 20260417_000006 cleanly.
  * Full suite: 658 passed, 3 skipped, 1 deselected, 36 warnings. The
    only two failures (`test_worker_ops_telemetry.py::test_emit_outbox_ops_snapshot_warn_tags`
    + `...::test_scoring_ops_metrics_and_snapshot`) are the same known
    pre-existing flakes documented in prior prompts; both telemetry
    tests pass in isolation.

PROHIBITION COMPLIANCE (prompt 15)
  * No Celery / Temporal / Prefect / Airflow dependency — in-process
    synchronous execution only.
  * No reordering of canonical events — orchestrator emits
    `InterviewCompleted -> ArgumentCompiled -> CoherenceScored
    -> DecisionIssued` in the same sequence as `process_next_scoring_job`.
  * Stage implementations WRAP the existing services; no duplication
    of scoring, policy, artifact, or notification logic
    (`_stage_artifact` reuses `ApplicationService._build_artifact_app_state`).
  * No edits outside the prompt-declared SCOPE.

PREVIOUS PROMPT (PRIOR) — 2026-04-17 (Wave 3, prompt 14/20)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Notification service (founder + partner) landed. The fund orchestrator
now ships an idempotent, template-driven notification dispatcher with
pluggable transport backends, wired into the scoring worker on the
enforce-mode branch only (shadow-mode decisions still skip all founder
and partner side effects per prompt 12).

- `server/fund/services/notifications.py` (NEW):
  * `class NotificationError(Exception)` — operator-readable
    transport + validation failure.
  * `compute_idempotency_key(application_id, template_id)` ->
    `sha256(f"{application_id}|{template_id}").hexdigest()`.
  * `dispatch(session, application_id, verdict, *, backend,
    template_id=None, recipient=None, extra_context=None)
    -> NotificationLog`.
    - Selects the founder template from
      `VERDICT_TO_FOUNDER_TEMPLATE` ({pass, reject, manual_review}).
    - Renders via `str.format_map` using the documented placeholder
      contract (`founder_name`, `founder_email`, `company_name`,
      `application_id`, `decision`, `policy_version`,
      `coherence_observed`, `threshold_required`, `margin`,
      `failed_gates_summary`). Missing keys are filled with `"-"`.
    - Extracts the `Subject:` header (if present) from the
      rendered body and passes it separately to the backend.
    - Idempotency: if a log row with the same idempotency key
      exists in `status="sent"`, returns it unchanged (no render,
      no backend call). `status="failed"` rows retry in place.
  * Legacy `"fail"` verdict aliased to `"reject"` for consumers
    that still emit the pre-canonical policy vocabulary.

- `server/fund/services/notification_backends.py` (NEW):
  * `NotificationBackend` Protocol (`channel` + `send(to, subject,
    body) -> dict`).
  * `DryRunBackend` — default backend used in CI and local runs.
    Writes a single JSON envelope per dispatch under `dry_run_dir`;
    zero network I/O; never reads or stores credentials.
  * `SMTPBackend` / `SESBackend` / `SendgridBackend` — env-gated
    optional backends. Each raises `NotificationBackendConfigError`
    if its required env vars are missing. Their `send()` methods
    are exercised in tests only through `unittest.mock` —
    no real sockets are opened under default CI.
  * `backend_for_channel("dry_run"|"smtp"|"ses"|"sendgrid")`
    factory; raises `ValueError` on typos so a wrong channel
    string fails at the call site instead of silently
    defaulting.

- `server/fund/data/notification_templates/` (NEW):
  * `founder_pass.txt`, `founder_reject.txt`,
    `founder_manual_review.txt`, `partner_escalation.md`.
    Each uses single-brace `{placeholder}` markers compatible
    with `str.format_map`.

- `server/fund/models.py` (MOD): added
  `NotificationLog(fund_notification_log)` with columns
  `(id, application_id, template_id, channel, recipient,
  idempotency_key [unique], status, error, created_at, sent_at)`.
  The table never persists raw credentials or rendered bodies
  containing sensitive material (prompt 14 prohibition).

- `alembic/versions/20260417_000005_notification_log.py` (NEW):
  idempotent upgrade that creates `fund_notification_log` plus
  indexes on `application_id`, `template_id`, `channel`,
  `status`, and a unique index on `idempotency_key`. Skips
  creation if the table / index already exists (handles
  `Base.metadata.create_all` bootstraps).

- `server/fund/services/application_service.py` (MOD):
  * `ApplicationService.__init__` now accepts optional
    `notification_backend` and `notification_dry_run_dir`. The
    default backend is a `DryRunBackend` rooted at
    `./var/notifications` (relative to cwd) — production
    callers inject an `SMTPBackend` / `SESBackend` /
    `SendgridBackend` instead.
  * After an enforce-mode decision is written,
    `process_next_scoring_job` invokes the new
    `_dispatch_enforce_notification` helper which wraps
    `notifications.dispatch`. Failures are logged via
    `_LOG_ARTIFACT.warning` but never fail the scoring job —
    delivery is a downstream best-effort side effect whose
    retries live in the `NotificationLog` ledger.
  * Shadow-mode decisions skip dispatch entirely; the pipeline
    still builds `shadow_decision_artifact` and emits
    `DecisionIssued` tagged `mode="shadow"`.

- `tests/test_notifications.py` (NEW, 38 tests):
  * Dry-run backend writes the expected JSON envelope for all
    three verdicts; body fragments asserted per template.
  * Second dispatch with the same key returns the same log row
    unchanged and does NOT invoke the backend a second time.
  * Verdict mapping is total and bijective over
    {pass, reject, manual_review}.
  * `"fail"` alias resolves to `founder_reject`.
  * SMTP / SES / Sendgrid raise `NotificationBackendConfigError`
    without env vars; with env vars, their `send()` methods are
    exercised only through mocked `smtplib` / `boto3` /
    `urllib.request` — no real sockets.
  * Backend transport errors persist `status="failed"` with an
    operator-readable error; a follow-up dispatch retries the
    same row in place.
  * `NotificationLog` never contains credentials (column scan).
  * Application-service defaults to `DryRunBackend`; the helper

PREVIOUS PROMPT (PRIOR) — 2026-04-17 (Wave 5, prompt 13/20)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Red-team adversarial harness landed. The fund orchestrator now ships
a curated, fully-offline regression harness that replays a labeled
corpus of synthetic founder pitches through the production
`ScoringService` + `DecisionPolicyService` chain (the same chain used
by `ApplicationService.process_next_scoring_job`), reports
per-case results plus false-pass / false-reject / false-review
counters, pins a 3 x 3 confusion matrix as a CI regression baseline,
and surfaces drift via a dedicated CLI verb with documented exit
codes.

- `server/fund/services/red_team.py` (NEW):
  - `run_adversarial_suite(fixtures_dir, labels_path, policy_version)
    -> RedTeamReport` orchestrates the replay. Loads + validates
    fixtures (sorted iteration, deterministic), loads labels,
    canonicalizes the decision-policy `fail` -> `reject`
    translation, and aggregates a `RedTeamReport`
    (`schema_version=red-team-report-v1`) with `total_cases`,
    `matches`, `mismatches`, `counts`
    (`false_pass`/`false_reject`/`false_review`), and a 3 x 3
    `confusion_matrix` keyed by `expected_verdict` ->
    `actual_verdict`. Per-case records carry CI95, anti-gaming
    flags, transcript-quality score, failed gate codes,
    threshold required / coherence observed / margin, and the
    label rationale.
  - `to_canonical_bytes()` serializes with `sort_keys=True` and
    fixed separators so consecutive runs are byte-identical
    (asserted in tests).
  - `RedTeamError` carries operator-readable messages for every
    load/schema failure surface (missing fixtures dir, missing
    labels, malformed JSON, unknown verdict, unknown category,
    missing label for a fixture, policy-version pin mismatch).
- `tests/adversarial/fixtures/*.json` (NEW): 12 fully synthetic
  fixtures (4 incoherent, 4 coherent + evidenced, 2
  template-echo, 2 borderline), spanning `market_economics`,
  `public_health`, and `governance` domains. One incoherent
  fixture sets `compliance_status="blocked"` to exercise the
  hard-fail compliance path; one borderline fixture sets
  `compliance_status="review_required"` to exercise the
  manual-review compliance path.
- `tests/adversarial/labels.json` (NEW): maps each fixture
  filename to `{expected_verdict, rationale}` using the
  canonical external vocabulary
  (`pass | reject | manual_review`).
- `cli.py` (MODIFIED): new top-level `red-team-run --fixtures-dir
  <dir> --labels <file> [--output <file>] [--policy-version <pin>]`
  verb. Always writes the canonical JSON report to stdout
  (mirroring to disk when `--output` is given). Exit `0` if every
  fixture's actual verdict matches its label, `1` if at least
  one mismatch, `2` on fixture / labels load failure or
  policy-version pin mismatch (per-prompt-13 contract).
- `tests/test_red_team_harness.py` (NEW): 19 cases covering:
  - The current confusion matrix is pinned as a regression
    baseline (`pass`->`reject`: 4, `reject`->`reject`: 4,
    `manual_review`->`reject`: 4; `matches=4`, `mismatches=8`,
    `false_reject=8`). Drift in the scorer, anti-gaming
    detector, decision-policy thresholds, or canonicalization
    fails the suite loudly with a diff.
  - Hygiene: >= 12 fixtures, all four required categories
    present at the prescribed counts, every fixture has a
    label, every label verdict is canonical, report is
    byte-deterministic across consecutive runs.
  - Every `RedTeamError` surface raises (missing fixtures dir,
    missing labels, policy-version pin mismatch, unlabeled
    fixture, unknown verdict in labels).
  - CLI smokes shell out to `python -m coherence_engine
    red-team-run` and assert exit `1` on the current mismatch
    baseline, exit `2` on missing fixtures dir + on
    policy-version pin mismatch, and exit `0` when labels are
    aligned to currently observed actual verdicts via a
    tmp-path `labels_aligned.json`.
- `docs/specs/red_team_harness.md` (NEW): documents fixture
  authoring (required fields, four categories, name/PII

PREVIOUS PROMPT (PRIOR) — 2026-04-17 (Wave 4, prompt 11/20)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Historical backtest pipeline landed. The project now has a
deterministic, offline replay of the governed historical-outcomes
dataset through the current scorer + decision policy, using a fixed
`PortfolioSnapshot` (loaded from disk) so that results are
reproducible regardless of the live portfolio state. The backtest
report carries verdict counts, a Brier score, a 10-bin reliability
curve, per-domain breakdowns, and all per-row replay records, and is
serialized to byte-identical JSON across repeated runs.

- `server/fund/services/backtest.py` (NEW): offline replay service.
  Exposes `@dataclass(frozen=True) BacktestConfig`
  (`dataset_path`, `decision_policy_version`,
  `portfolio_snapshot_path`, `output_path`, `seed`,
  `requested_check_usd`, `domain_default`),
  `@dataclass(frozen=True) BacktestReport` (schema version
  `backtest-report-v1`, aggregates, reliability curve, domain
  breakdown, per-row records), `BacktestRowResult`, `ReliabilityBin`,
  `BacktestError`, `load_portfolio_snapshot(path)`, and the public
  entry point `run_backtest(config) -> BacktestReport`. For each row
  the service rebuilds the 95% calibrated superiority interval via
  `calibrated_superiority_interval_95(...)`, constructs a synthetic
  `application` + `score_record`, and invokes
  `DecisionPolicyService.evaluate(...)` with the fixed snapshot.
  `BacktestReport.to_canonical_bytes()` uses
  `json.dumps(sort_keys=True, separators=(",", ":"))` + `"\n"` and
  is byte-stable across runs (enforced by test).
- `cli.py` (MODIFIED): new `backtest-run` subcommand with
  `--dataset`, `--policy-version`, `--portfolio-snapshot`,
  `--output`, `--seed`, `--requested-check-usd`,
  `--domain-default`. Exits `2` on dataset validation failure
  (reusing `validate_historical_outcomes_export`) or on
  `decision_policy_version` pin mismatch; `0` on success.
- `deploy/scripts/run_backtest.py` (NEW): thin sys.path-aware
  wrapper mirroring `merge_governed_historical_outcomes.py`.
- `tests/fixtures/backtest/mini_dataset.jsonl` (NEW): 10 curated
  governed-format rows across three domains (`market_economics`,
  `public_health`, `governance`).
- `tests/fixtures/backtest/snapshot.json` (NEW): fixed
  `PortfolioSnapshot` payload with NAV, reserve, drawdown, regime,
  per-domain invested USD.
- `tests/test_backtest.py` (NEW): 18 cases — fixture sanity,
  snapshot loader happy/error paths, report shape + metric ranges +
  reliability-bin count, byte-identical output on repeated runs,
  digest stability, Brier-score sensitivity (midpoint flip leaves
  Brier unchanged; flipping a high-predicted row to a negative
  outcome raises Brier by the expected `ΔP²/N ≈ 0.030`; asymmetric
  flip produces a directional change), policy-version-pin and
  invalid-row rejections (both `BacktestError` at service level and
  exit `2` from the CLI), output-path file write, dataset
  immutability under replay, and CLI smokes for happy path (stdout
  == file bytes), invalid dataset (exit 2), and policy-version
  mismatch (exit 2).
- `docs/specs/backtest_spec.md` (NEW): documents inputs, outputs,
  metric definitions, the `predicted_probability = clamp((CS+1)/2,
  0, 1)` affine map, the 10-bin reliability-curve convention, CLI
  contract, and the reproducibility + no-network + no-live-read
  prohibitions.

Prohibitions honored (matches prompt 11):
- No network I/O.
- No reads of the live portfolio_state / positions tables
  anywhere on the backtest path — the snapshot always comes from
  `config.portfolio_snapshot_path` (or the zero-default when
  omitted).
- No writes to `data/governed/*`.
- Files outside SCOPE were not modified.

EARLIER PROMPT — 2026-04-17 (Wave 2, prompt 10/20)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Portfolio state persistence + concentration policy landed. The decision
policy can now read real per-domain concentration, liquidity reserve,
drawdown proxy, and regime from a dedicated append-only persistence
layer instead of relying on hardcoded defaults or in-memory mappings.
The `R(S, portfolio_state)` terms are unchanged in shape; they now have
a real source of truth.

- `server/fund/models.py` (MODIFIED, additive only): two new ORM
  classes — `PortfolioState` (id, as_of [indexed], fund_nav_usd,
  liquidity_reserve_usd, drawdown_proxy ∈ [0,1], regime ∈
  {normal, stress, recovery}, optional note, created_at) and
  `Position` (id, application_id [indexed], domain [indexed],
  invested_usd, status ∈ {active, wound_down, exited} [indexed],
  created_at, updated_at). All existing models untouched.
- `alembic/versions/20260417_000003_portfolio_state.py` (NEW):
  idempotent `upgrade()` creates `portfolio_state` and `positions`
  tables (no-ops if already created via `Base.metadata.create_all`)
  with indexes `ix_portfolio_state_as_of`, `ix_positions_application_id`,
  `ix_positions_domain`, `ix_positions_status`, and the composite
  `ix_positions_domain_status`. Symmetric `downgrade()` drops both
  tables and indexes.
- `server/fund/repositories/portfolio_repository.py` (NEW):
  `PortfolioRepository(db)` with `latest_state()`,
  `latest_state_as_dict()`, `active_positions_by_domain() ->
  dict[str, float]` (sum invested_usd by domain where status="active",
  deterministic key-sorted), `active_positions_total()`,
  `domain_concentration_by_nav()`, `set_liquidity_reserve(usd, *,
  note=None)` (append-only — never mutates prior rows; carries forward
  NAV / drawdown / regime from the previous snapshot),
  `record_state(...)`, `record_position(...)`. All writes are
  append-only; no trades, transfers, or live-ledger writes occur.
- `server/fund/services/decision_policy.py` (MODIFIED, additive only):
  introduces `@runtime_checkable` Protocol `PortfolioStateProvider`
  with `get_snapshot() -> PortfolioSnapshot | None`, frozen dataclass
  `PortfolioSnapshot(fund_nav_usd, liquidity_reserve_usd,
  drawdown_proxy, regime, domain_invested_usd, as_of)`, helper
  `portfolio_snapshot_from_repository(repo)` (duck-typed; no hard import
  of the repo module), and `snapshot_to_portfolio_state(snapshot, *,
  domain_primary)` that projects the persisted snapshot vocabulary
  (regime: normal|stress|recovery) into the legacy policy mapping
  vocabulary (regime: neutral|stress|defensive|expansion via
  `_PERSISTED_REGIME_TO_POLICY`). `DecisionPolicyService.__init__` now
  accepts an optional `portfolio_provider`; `evaluate(...)` accepts
  an optional kw-only `portfolio_snapshot` and resolves the effective
  state in this order: explicit `portfolio_state` mapping >
  explicit snapshot > injected provider > pre-existing defaults. The
  legacy-envelope return shape is preserved exactly when no source is
  active. When portfolio touches occur, `portfolio_adjustments` gains
  one new key, `portfolio_snapshot_source` ∈ {explicit_mapping,
  explicit_snapshot, provider}, for audit.
- `cli.py` (MODIFIED, additive only): new `portfolio-state` subcommand
  group with verbs `show` (prints latest snapshot + per-domain active
  USD totals + per-domain concentration as JSON) and `set-reserve
  --usd <amount> [--note ...]` (writes a new append-only snapshot row
  with the liquidity reserve updated and prior NAV/drawdown/regime
  carried forward; emits the resulting row as JSON). Both verbs ensure
  the `portfolio_state` / `positions` tables exist via
  `Base.metadata.create_all` so operators can run them on a fresh
  environment without first running migrations.
- `tests/test_portfolio_state.py` (NEW, 14 tests): Alembic migration
  upgrade→downgrade→upgrade round-trip (SQLite, exercises only the new
  migration via `command.stamp` to avoid an unrelated pre-existing
  migration that emits SQLite-incompatible DDL); repository write+read
  round-trip; append-only set_liquidity_reserve preserves prior rows
  byte-for-byte; repository input validation; backward-compatibility
  envelope identity (`DecisionPolicyService(provider=None_returning).
  evaluate == DecisionPolicyService().evaluate`); provider snapshot

  `portfolio_state` overrides the provider; high domain-USD share lifts
  `threshold_required` by ≥0.005 with a non-zero `r_domain_usd` audit
  term; `portfolio_snapshot_from_repository` reflects persisted state;

The `decision_policy_v1.x` policy versioning rules from prompt 01 are

PREVIOUS PROMPT — 2026-04-16 (Wave 2, prompt 09/20)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Deterministic anti-gaming detector wired into composite scoring. The
detector produces `AntiGamingReport(score, flags, metrics)` where the
clean-convention `score ∈ [0, 1]` (1.0 = clean). The composite scorer
now multiplies its raw composite by `(0.5 + 0.5 * anti_gaming_score)`:
a bounded penalty that cannot reduce a clean score and cannot more than
halve the worst case. No new ML dependencies — all stdlib.

- `core/anti_gaming.py` (NEW): `detect_anti_gaming(propositions, *,
  prior_corpus=(), templates=()) -> AntiGamingReport` with documented
  flag-code constants `AG_TEMPLATE_OVERLAP` (weight 0.30, char-trigram
  Jaccard vs templates > 0.6), `AG_PRIOR_CORPUS_ECHO` (0.25, char-trigram
  Jaccard vs prior_corpus > 0.8), `AG_REPETITIVE_FILLER` (0.20, mean
  pairwise length-normalized sublinear-TF cosine > 0.85 — stdlib, no
  sklearn), `AG_FLUENCY_WITHOUT_CONTENT` (0.15, ratio of long+complex
  props to metric/numeric-bearing props > 3.0), `AG_CONTRADICTION_DENIAL`
  (0.25, per-sentence negation + content-token repetition without a
  concession marker). `FLAG_WEIGHTS` mapping exported for tests;
  `score = clamp(1.0 - sum_weights, 0, 1)`. `metrics` dict carries raw
  measurements for audit (`template_overlap_max`, `self_similarity_mean`,
  `prior_corpus_overlap_max`, `fluency_ratio`,
  `contradiction_denial_count`).
- `core/scorer.py` (MODIFIED, additive only): new keyword-only kwarg
  `anti_gaming: bool = True` (plus optional `prior_corpus=()` /
  `templates=()`) on `CoherenceScorer.score(...)`. Backward-compatible:
  existing single-arg callers continue to work; a clean report never
  reduces the composite. `CoherenceResult.metadata` gains
  `raw_composite_score`, `anti_gaming_score`, `anti_gaming_flags`,
  `anti_gaming_metrics`. Detector exceptions fall back to
  multiplier=1.0 (scoring never fails on anti-gaming issues). The
  n_propositions<2 early-return also fills these metadata keys with
  clean defaults.
- `server/fund/services/scoring.py` (MODIFIED): `anti_gaming_score` in
  the returned dict is now sourced from the detector via the scorer's
  metadata (replacing the previous contradiction-count heuristic),
  with the canonical clean-score convention (1.0 = clean). Also adds
  `anti_gaming_flags` (list of flag codes) and `anti_gaming_metrics`
  (raw measurements) to the dict.
- `tests/fixtures/anti_gaming/clean.json` / `template_echo.json` /
  `repetitive.json` (NEW): three scenario fixtures.
- `tests/test_anti_gaming.py` (NEW, 12 tests): clean fixture → no
  flags, score == 1.0; template_echo → `AG_TEMPLATE_OVERLAP`;
  repetitive → `AG_REPETITIVE_FILLER`; synthetic prior-corpus echo →
  `AG_PRIOR_CORPUS_ECHO`; empty propositions → clean default;
  byte-determinism across calls; bounded-penalty property
  `composite >= 0.5 * raw`; clean pitch preserves composite
  (multiplier == 1.0); `anti_gaming=False` disables the penalty;
  flag-weight shape invariant; `ScoringService.score_application(...)`
  pass-through to dict fields.

Scope note: `server/fund/services/decision_policy.py` was intentionally
left untouched (out of scope). Its existing anti-gaming gate thresholds
were authored against the placeholder "risk-score" convention (high =
bad) from the previous `scoring.py` heuristic and need to be re-tuned
for the canonical clean-score convention in a follow-up prompt.
`DecisionPolicyService` unit tests still pass because they feed
`anti_gaming_score` as hardcoded dict inputs rather than invoking the
scorer.

Verify with:
  PYTHONPATH=.. python3 -m pytest tests/test_anti_gaming.py -v
  PYTHONPATH=.. python3 -m pytest tests/ --deselect tests/test_scorer.py::TestContradictoryText::test_contradictory_pitch -q
    # 532 passed, 3 skipped, 1 deselected
  PYTHONPATH=.. python3 -c "from coherence_engine.core.anti_gaming import detect_anti_gaming; print('ok')"

PREVIOUS PROMPT — 2026-04-16 (Wave 1, prompt 08/20)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Versioned prompt registry with SHA pinning landed. Every LLM prompt now
has a stable id, semver version, owner, status ({draft, shadow, prod}),
and the SHA-256 of its body file's raw bytes, with CLI verbs to inspect,
verify, and derive a stable registry digest for the decision artifact's
`pins.prompt_registry_digest` slot.

- `data/prompts/registry.json` (NEW): schema_version `prompt-registry-v1`
  with two seed prod entries — `interview_opening` v1.0.0 and
  `self_critique` v1.0.0 — both owned by `fund-ops`. Each entry carries
  `body_path` plus lowercase hex `content_sha256` computed over the raw
  on-disk bytes (no normalization). Prompt body text is never embedded
  inline.
- `data/prompts/bodies/interview_opening.v1.md` (NEW) and
  `data/prompts/bodies/self_critique.v1.md` (NEW): short Markdown
  templates suitable as LLM system/user prompts.
- `server/fund/services/prompt_registry.py` (NEW):
  `load_registry(path=None) -> Registry`,
  `verify_registry(registry, repo_root=None) -> VerificationReport` with
  `.ok`, `.mismatches[]`, `.missing[]`,
  `registry_digest(registry) -> str` (stable SHA-256 over the sorted
  `(id, version, content_sha256)` tuples; deterministic,
  order-insensitive to declaration order, version-sensitive),
  `resolve(prompt_id, version, registry=None) -> PromptEntry`,
  `default_registry_path()`, `iter_entries`, dataclasses `PromptEntry`,
  `Registry`, `Mismatch`, `VerificationReport`, and
  `PromptRegistryError`. Loader enforces `schema_version`, required
  keys, allowed statuses, and `(id, version)` uniqueness.
- `cli.py` (MODIFIED, additive only): new `prompt-registry` subcommand
  group with verbs `list`, `verify`, `digest`. All three accept
  `--registry <path>`; `list` and `verify` accept `--json`.
  Verification failure exits 2, matching the parity convention set by
  `validate-historical-export`. `digest` prints exactly the value
  intended for `pins.prompt_registry_digest`.
- `tests/test_prompt_registry.py` (NEW, 17 tests): load/parse,
  happy-path verify OK on fresh fixtures, body-mutation detection,
  missing-body reporting, digest determinism across calls, digest
  order-insensitivity, digest changes when a body SHA changes,
  `resolve` hit/miss, schema/status/duplicate rejection, shipped
  registry self-verifies, plus four CLI subprocess smokes
  (`verify` exit 0, `list` prints seeded entries, `digest` emits a
  valid hex sha256, `verify` exit 2 on a tampered out-of-tree fixture).
- `docs/specs/prompt_registry.md` (NEW): schema, digest semantics,
  draft -> shadow -> prod lifecycle, CLI verb table, and invariants
  (raw-bytes hashing, no inline bodies, shipped registry verifies in CI).

No new runtime dependencies.

PREVIOUS PROMPT — 2026-04-16 (Wave 3, prompt 07/20)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Reproducible decision artifact generator (`decision_artifact.v1`) landed.
After scoring + decision, the worker now bundles inputs, per-layer scores,
domain mix, ontology references, decision outcome, and pinned versions into
a single canonical JSON artifact whose serialization is byte-identical
across runs over the same persisted state.

- `server/fund/schemas/artifacts/decision_artifact.v1.json` (NEW): JSON
  Schema Draft 2020-12, `additionalProperties: false`, with required
  `artifact_id` / `artifact_kind="decision_artifact"` /
  `schema_version="1"` / `application_id` / `session_id` / `occurred_at` /
  `inputs_digest` / `scoring{composite, per_layer{contradiction,
  argumentation, embedding, compression, structural}, uncertainty{lower,
  upper}, scoring_version}` / `domain{weights[], normative_profile,
  schema_version, notes}` / `ontology_graph_id` / `ontology_graph_digest` /
  `decision{verdict, cs_superiority, cs_required, reason_codes,
  decision_policy_version}` / `pins{scoring_version,
  decision_policy_version, optional prompt_registry_digest}`.
- `server/fund/services/decision_artifact.py` (NEW):
  `build_decision_artifact(app_state) -> dict` deterministically assembles
  the artifact and uses `json.dumps(sort_keys=True, separators=(",", ":"))`
  for the SHA-256 `inputs_digest`. Wall-clock is never read; `occurred_at`
  comes from the application's authored timestamps.
  `persist_decision_artifact(session, app_id, artifact_dict,
  scoring_job_id=None) -> ArgumentArtifact` validates against the v1 schema
  and writes a row with `kind="decision_artifact"` and the canonical bytes
  in `payload_json`. Verdict normalization maps internal `fail` -> canonical
  `reject` to match the `decision_issued.v1` enum.
- `server/fund/models.py`: `ArgumentArtifact` now carries `kind` (default
  `"generic"`, indexed) and optional `payload_json`; `scoring_job_id`
  relaxed to nullable.
- `alembic/versions/20260417_000002_artifact_kind.py` (NEW): adds `kind` +
  `payload_json` columns idempotently, uses server_default `"generic"` for
  backfill, and uses `batch_alter_table` on SQLite for downgrade symmetry.
  Non-SQLite dialects also relax `scoring_job_id` to nullable in-place.
- `server/fund/services/application_service.py`: after `upsert_decision`,
  builds the artifact via the new `_build_artifact_app_state` helper (uses
  `app.updated_at` ISO string, never `datetime.now()`) and persists it
  before publishing the existing `DecisionIssued` event. The event already
  carries the canonical summary fields cs_superiority / cs_required /
  decision_policy_version / scoring_version via the prompt 02 validator.
- `tests/test_decision_artifact.py` (NEW, 11 tests): schema required-key
  assertion, deterministic byte-identical build, inputs_digest changes
  when inputs change, happy-path schema validation, tampered artifact
  (missing `decision_policy_version`) is rejected, unknown top-level key
  is rejected, `fail` -> `reject` normalization, pins always include
  scoring_version + decision_policy_version, optional
  `prompt_registry_digest` round-trips, persisted row carries
  `kind="decision_artifact"` with canonical payload_json, validation
  blocks partial writes.

No new runtime dependencies; the prompt 02 event schemas remain unchanged.

Verify with:
  python3 -m pytest tests/test_decision_artifact.py -v
  PYTHONPATH=.. python3 -m pytest tests/ --deselect tests/test_scorer.py::TestContradictoryText::test_contradictory_pitch -q
  PYTHONPATH=.. python3 -m alembic upgrade head
  python3 -c "from coherence_engine.server.fund.services.decision_artifact import build_decision_artifact, persist_decision_artifact; print('ok')"


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
PREVIOUS PROMPT — 2026-04-16 (Wave 3, prompt 06/20)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Hybrid domain reconstruction. Domain detection now produces a weighted
`DomainMix` that fuses four signals (topical embeddings, premise
overlap, ontology entities, and normative markers) without removing or
renaming the existing single-domain `DomainDetector.detect()` API.

- `core/types.py`: added frozen `NormativeProfile(rights, utilitarian,
  deontic)` and frozen `DomainMix(weights, normative,
  ontology_graph_id=None, notes=None, schema_version="domain-mix-v1")`.
  `DomainMix.top()` returns the highest-weight `(domain, weight)` entry
  or `None` for empty mixes. Existing dataclasses are untouched.
- `server/fund/data/normative_markers.json` (NEW): per-axis lemma lists
  under `axes.rights` / `axes.utilitarian` / `axes.deontic`, with
  `schema_version="normative-markers-v1"`.
- `domain/normative.py` (NEW):
  `compute_normative_profile(propositions) -> NormativeProfile`. Uses
  simple regex tokenization on lowercased text, counts token matches
  against each axis's marker list, and returns the share of tokens per
  axis clamped to [0, 1]. Empty input yields an all-zero profile.
  Lexicon load falls back to sane defaults on IO/JSON failures.
- `domain/premises.py`: added module-level `DOMAIN_NORMATIVE` table
  with declared `(rights, utilitarian, deontic)` triples for all 10
  domains, plus `get_domain_normative(key)` that returns
  `(0.33, 0.33, 0.33)` for unknown keys. Existing
  `DOMAINS`/`TENSIONS`/loaders are unchanged.
- `domain/detector.py`: added
  `detect_domain_mix(propositions, ontology, *, embedder=None,
  top_k=3) -> DomainMix`. Legacy `DomainDetector` class is untouched.
  - `w_topic`: cosine similarity between mean proposition embedding
    and per-domain premise centroids (SBERT-or-TF-IDF via
    `embeddings.base.get_embedder` when `embedder is None`).
  - `w_premise`: Jaccard between the argument's content lemmas and
    each domain's premise lemmas after stopword filtering.
  - `w_ontology`: for each domain, normalized count of ontology entity
    surface forms that appear as word-boundary matches inside the
    domain's premise text.
  - `w_normative`: cosine between the argument's `NormativeProfile`
    vector and each domain's declared normative profile.
  - Final per-domain score:
    `0.4*w_topic + 0.25*w_premise + 0.2*w_ontology + 0.15*w_normative`.
  - Graceful degradation: if a signal cannot be computed (missing
    embedder, empty ontology, empty content, empty arg normative
    vector, etc.) it is skipped, its coefficient is redistributed
    across surviving signals, and a `"signal_skipped: <name>"` string
    is appended to the returned `DomainMix.notes` tuple.
  - Sort desc, clamp `top_k` to at least 1, renormalize the retained
    weights so they sum to exactly 1.0. When every signal is skipped
    (e.g. empty propositions and empty ontology), weights is `()` and
    notes lists all four skipped signals.
  - `ontology_graph_id` is a stable sha256-prefix fingerprint of the
    ontology's entities+edges (or `None` for empty/missing ontology).
- `tests/fixtures/hybrid_domain/rights_argument.json` (NEW): 4-
  proposition rights-leaning fixture.
- `tests/fixtures/hybrid_domain/market_argument.json` (NEW): 4-
  proposition market-leaning fixture.
- `tests/test_hybrid_domain.py` (12 tests): legacy single-domain API
  preservation; rights fixture returns a valid `DomainMix` with
  weights summing to 1.0 in descending order; determinism across
  fresh TF-IDF embedders; TF-IDF fallback keeps `market_economics`
  in the top-k for the market fixture; empty `OntologyGraph` adds
  `signal_skipped: ontology`; `None` ontology also skips;
  weights-sum-to-1 invariant across `top_k ∈ {1, 2, 3, 5}`; empty
  propositions path returns empty weights and all four `signal_skipped`
  notes; `DomainMix.top()` returns the highest-weight entry;
  `ontology_graph_id` is a 16-character string when the ontology has
  entities; `compute_normative_profile` puts rights-heavy text above
  the utilitarian axis; empty-input normative profile is all zeros.

No new runtime dependencies. `domain/comparator.py` is intentionally
unchanged; callers that want a single-domain handoff can use
`DomainMix.top()`.

Verify with:
  python3 -m pytest tests/test_hybrid_domain.py -v
  python3 -m pytest tests/ --deselect tests/test_scorer.py::TestContradictoryText::test_contradictory_pitch -q
  python3 -c "from coherence_engine.domain.detector import detect_domain_mix; print('ok')"

Prompt 40 — STT abstraction (Whisper / Deepgram / AssemblyAI) with
deterministic fallback
================================================================================

Wave 11. Depends on prompts 38 (Twilio voice intake) and 39 (browser
WebRTC intake). Adds a SpeechToText interface in
`server/fund/services/stt/` plus three backends and a router that
owns provider selection, transient-failure fallback, and the
LOW_STT_CONFIDENCE quality-flag handoff to transcript_quality.

- `server/fund/services/stt/__init__.py` (NEW): re-exports the public
  surface — `SpeechToText`, `STTResult`, `STTProvenance`, `STTError`,
  `STTUnavailable`, `WhisperNotAvailable`, `LOW_STT_CONFIDENCE`,
  `STTRouter`, `transcribe`.
- `server/fund/services/stt/interface.py` (NEW): the `SpeechToText`
  Protocol (`transcribe(audio_uri, *, language=None, hints=())
  -> STTResult`). Returns an `STTResult` wrapper rather than a bare
  `Transcript` because `core.types.Transcript` is frozen and lacks a
  metadata slot — `STTResult` carries the canonical `Transcript`
  plus an `STTProvenance` record (`stt_provider`, `model`,
  `avg_confidence`, `word_count`, `attempts`, `fallback_used`) and a
  tuple of `quality_flags` consumed downstream.
  - `LOW_STT_CONFIDENCE` constant.
  - `average_word_confidence(words)` helper (returns 0.0 on empty
    so the gate fails closed).
  - `build_quality_flags(avg, *, min_avg_confidence, extra)` helper.
  - `fetch_audio_bytes(audio_uri)` resolves `file://` and absolute
    filesystem paths directly; falls through to
    `object_storage.get` for everything else.
- `server/fund/services/stt/whisper_backend.py` (NEW):
  `WhisperLocalBackend(name="whisper", model=WHISPER_MODEL)`.
  - Lazy `_import_whisper_module()` tries `faster_whisper` first,
    then `whisper`. If neither importable → raises
    `WhisperNotAvailable` (NOT `ImportError`). The native deps are
    therefore never loaded merely by importing the STT package.
  - `_set_fake_engine(fake)` test seam — fake's `transcribe(path,
    language=None, hints=())` returns `(turns, words)`.
  - Production path materializes the audio to a temp file (the
    ctranslate2 reader needs a seekable filesystem path), then
    `_segments_to_turns_faster` / `_segments_to_turns_legacy` map
    Whisper's segment objects to `TranscriptTurn` + per-word
    tuples. Whisper does not diarize; every segment is emitted as a
    single `founder` speaker turn (diarization is a future prompt).
- `server/fund/services/stt/deepgram_backend.py` (NEW):
  `DeepgramBackend(api_key=..., model="nova-2")`.
  - HTTP via stdlib `urllib` with `set_transport_for_tests` seam.
  - `POST /v1/listen?diarize=true&utterances=true&punctuate=true&...`.
  - 5xx → `STTError("deepgram_5xx ...")`; 4xx → `STTError(...)`
    (NOT silently fellback — surfaces config bugs); transport
    errors → `STTError`.
  - `_parse_deepgram_response` prefers diarized utterances; falls
    back to first alternative when utterances are absent.
- `server/fund/services/stt/assemblyai_backend.py` (NEW):
  `AssemblyAIBackend(api_key=..., poll_interval=1.0,
  poll_max_seconds=300.0, sleep=time.sleep)`.
  - Two-phase: `POST /upload` (raw bytes) → `POST /transcript`
    (job submit) → `GET /transcript/{id}` (poll until completed).
  - Bounded polling — `STTError("assemblyai_poll_timeout ...")`
    when budget exhausted.
  - Injectable `sleep` so tests do not actually sleep.
- `server/fund/services/stt/router.py` (NEW):
  `STTRouter(primary, fallback=None, min_avg_confidence=...)` plus
  `STTRouter.from_env()` and a module-level `transcribe(...)`.
  - Calls primary; falls back when primary raised `STTError` OR
    `avg_confidence < STT_MIN_AVG_CONFIDENCE` (default 0.6).
  - Both backends fail → raises `STTUnavailable` with both
    diagnostics joined.
  - Both below threshold → returns the higher-confidence result
    with `LOW_STT_CONFIDENCE` stamped on `quality_flags`.
  - Provenance: stamps `attempts=("primary","fallback")` and
    `fallback_used=bool` so callers can audit which provider
    actually produced the transcript.
- `server/fund/services/voice_intake.py` (MODIFIED):
  - New `transcribe_session_audio(audio_uri, *, session_id,
    language=None)` helper — no-op when `STT_PROVIDER_PRIMARY` is
    unset, so existing fixtures (synthetic non-audio chunk bytes)
    still pass.
  - Called from `finalize_browser_session` immediately after
    `stitch_chunks`. On success persists the resulting Transcript
    via `transcript_quality.store_transcript` and embeds an `stt`
    metadata block (`status`, `stt_provider`, `model`,
    `avg_confidence`, `quality_flags`, `transcript_uri`,
    `fallback_used`, `attempts`) in the
    `interview_session_completed` event payload.
- `tests/test_stt_router.py` (NEW, 10 tests): primary success;
  primary 5xx → fallback; primary low-conf → fallback; both low-conf
  returns best with `LOW_STT_CONFIDENCE`; both fail raises
  `STTUnavailable`; no-fallback paths; `from_env` env lookup;
  unknown provider raises `STTError`; `_build_backend` alias map.
- `tests/test_stt_backends.py` (NEW, 9 tests): Whisper fake-engine
  end-to-end (asr_model = "whisper:tiny", word_count = 2,
  avg_confidence = 0.85); Whisper lazy-import probe raises
  `WhisperNotAvailable` when both modules are masked via
  `monkeypatch.setitem(sys.modules, name, None)`;
  `WhisperLocalBackend.transcribe` surfaces the same exception;
  Deepgram utterance parsing (avg = (0.9+0.9+0.95)/3, Authorization
  header set, `diarize=true` in URL); Deepgram 503 → `STTError`;
  Deepgram missing-key → `STTError`; AssemblyAI two-phase upload →
  submit → poll happy path; AssemblyAI job-error response → `STTError`;
  AssemblyAI 503 on upload → `STTError`.
- `tests/fixtures/audio/short_clip.wav` (NEW): 0.6s 16kHz mono sine
  (220 Hz) + light speech-shaped noise, ≈19 KB. Generated with
  stdlib `wave` so the fixture creation script needs no numpy.
- `docs/specs/stt.md` (NEW): backend table; provider-selection
  semantics (when fallback fires, what 4xx vs 5xx mean);
  cost-per-minute estimates (April 2026 list prices) for Whisper
  local CPU/GPU, Deepgram Nova-2 General/Phonecall, AssemblyAI
  Universal-1 best/nano; language and accent fitness notes; per-word
  confidence contract; voice_intake wiring; test strategy.
- `.env.example` (MODIFIED): `STT_PROVIDER_PRIMARY`,
  `STT_PROVIDER_FALLBACK`, `STT_MIN_AVG_CONFIDENCE`, `WHISPER_MODEL`,
  `DEEPGRAM_API_KEY`, `ASSEMBLYAI_API_KEY`.

LOW_STT_CONFIDENCE handoff to `transcript_quality`: the existing
`evaluate_transcript` already gates on per-turn confidence
(`TQG_ASR_CONFIDENCE_LOW`), so feeding the canonical Transcript
inside the STTResult into the quality gate naturally surfaces the
low-confidence reason code. No edit to `transcript_quality.py` was
needed (that file is also out of SCOPE for this prompt).

No new runtime dependencies are pulled in by simply importing the
package; managed-provider HTTP uses stdlib `urllib` and the Whisper
native imports are deferred to first call.

Verify with:
  python3 -m pytest tests/test_stt_router.py \

  python3 -m pytest tests/ -p no:pytest-qt -q
  python3 -c "from coherence_engine.server.fund.services.stt import STTRouter, transcribe, LOW_STT_CONFIDENCE; print('ok')"


PROMPT 41 — ADAPTIVE INTERVIEW POLICY ENGINE + INTERRUPTION HANDLING (Wave 11)
------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Replaces the linear topic walk in voice_intake (prompts 38–39) with
a deterministic, rules-based policy over a directed-acyclic topic
graph; adds dropped-call recovery within a 24h window, capped at
one recovery attempt per session.

Files
- `server/fund/data/interview_topic_graph.json` (NEW): nodes for
  problem / solution_mechanism / evidence / moat / execution /
  self_critique plus follow-up nodes. Edges keyed by predicates
  `if_high_anti_gaming`, `if_low_evidence`, `default`.
  `duration_seconds_cap`=1800, `confidence_threshold`=0.6,
  `anti_gaming_threshold`=1, `max_follow_ups_per_topic`=1,
  `high_priority_topics`=[problem, solution_mechanism, evidence,
  self_critique]. Acyclic by construction; the loader runs an
  iterative three-colour DFS and refuses any cycle or unknown
  edge target.
- `server/fund/services/interview_policy.py` (NEW): TopicGraph /
  TopicNode / Question / AnswerFeatures dataclasses;
  `load_topic_graph` (validation); `init_state`; `apply_answer`;
  `coverage_complete`; `duration_exhausted`; `next_question` —
  deterministic, no LLM, no clock branching. Predicate priority:
  if_high_anti_gaming > if_low_evidence > default. The selected
  Question is also written back to `state["next_question"]` so
  recovery can resume from it.
- `server/fund/services/interview_recovery.py` (NEW):
  `should_recover` predicate (status / state.completed / coverage
  / recovery_attempts cap / 24h window). `recover_session(db,
  session, *, notifier=None, redialer=None)` — both callables
  injected so tests can drive the flow without SMTP/Twilio.
  Bumps `state.recovery_attempts`. A second attempt raises
  `RecoveryRefused`. `resume_question(session)` reads
  `state.next_question` for the webhook handler.
- `server/fund/models.py` (MOD): InterviewSession.state_json TEXT
  NOT NULL DEFAULT ''. Empty string == "no policy state yet"; the
  policy initialises lazily on first use.
- `alembic/versions/20260425_000008_interview_session_state.py` (NEW):
  add fund_interview_sessions.state_json column with empty server
  default so backfill is a no-op against existing rows.
- `server/fund/services/voice_intake.py` (MOD): start_call seeds
  state_json with init_state on session creation. New helper
  `next_question_for_session(db, session, features=None)` loads /
  runs / saves state via the policy. Existing TwiML render
  helpers + the pinned snapshot test stay untouched.
- `tests/test_interview_policy.py` (NEW, 13 tests): graph load
  + acyclic; cycle + unknown-edge rejection; init_state;
  first-call returns start; high-evidence walk skips followups;
  low-evidence routes to follow-up + max_follow_ups guard;
  anti-gaming overrides low-evidence; duration cap terminates;
  coverage_complete terminates; determinism; full canonical walk;
  follow-up counter increment.
- `tests/test_interview_recovery.py` (NEW, 8 tests): should_recover
  true / false-when-completed / false-out-of-window; resume from
  next_question; refuses second attempt; refuses when no
  next_question; resume_question round-trip; works without
  notifier/redialer.
- `docs/specs/interview_policy.md` (NEW): goals, components,
  topic-graph format, predicate priority rules, coverage criterion,
  session-state schema, 24h recovery flow, determinism + replay
  guarantees.

Determinism + replay: the policy makes no LLM call, no network
call, and no clock-based branching in the question-selection path.
Given the same `(state, AnswerFeatures)` pair the result is
bit-identical — the fixture-walk test pins the canonical sequence
problem → solution → evidence → moat → execution → self_critique.

Recovery contract: AT MOST ONE recovery per session. The 24h
window is anchored to InterviewSession.created_at. A second
recover_session call always raises RecoveryRefused; an out-of-window
or already-complete session is also refused.

Verify with:
  python3 -m pytest tests/test_interview_policy.py \
                    tests/test_interview_recovery.py -v \
                    -p no:pytest-qt -p no:pytestqt
  python3 -m pytest tests/test_voice_intake.py -v \
                    -p no:pytest-qt -p no:pytestqt
  python3 -m pytest tests/ -p no:pytest-qt -p no:pytestqt -q \
                    --ignore=tests/test_arq_worker.py
