PRIOR PROMPT — Prompt 42 of 70 (Wave 12)
================================================================================

Task: Stand up the historical-startups validation corpus data layer for
the predictive-validity study (500 rows target). Initial PR ships the
ingestion harness plus 25 synthetic seed rows; the operator backfills
real-source rows under the consent invariant.

What shipped:
- `server/fund/schemas/datasets/historical_pitch.v1.json` (NEW): strict
  v1 schema. pitch_id (UUIDv7), anonymized company_name,
  domain_primary (10-value enum), pitch_year [2005, 2030], country
  (ISO alpha-2), transcript_uri / deck_uri / memo_uri (object-storage
  URIs), evidence_floor, eligibility, provenance.
  additionalProperties=false everywhere.
- `server/fund/services/historical_corpus.py` (NEW): pure
  compute_eligibility(row) → EligibilityFlags (date window 2005..2024,
  evidence floor n_props≥10 / metrics≥3 / sources≥2, no training
  overlap, consent rule that exempts synthetic rows). ingest(path, *,
  source, dry_run=True, manifest_path=None) walks files / directories,
  stamps provenance, refuses non-synthetic rows lacking documented
  consent, recomputes eligibility, schema-validates, dedupes by
  pitch_id, optionally appends to manifest.jsonl. validate() re-checks
  the manifest and reports eligibility drift. stat() returns a
  deterministic JSON summary pinned by the test suite.
- `data/historical_corpus/seeds/seed_*.json` (NEW): 25 fully-fabricated
  synthetic rows across 5 domains and 4 coherence bands.
  `seeds/README.md` calls out the synthetic-only constraint.
- `data/historical_corpus/manifest.jsonl` (NEW): 25 ingested seed rows.
- `cli.py` (MOD): adds `historical-corpus ingest|stat|validate`.
  ingest is dry-run by default; --apply writes. validate exits 2 on
  schema failure.
- `tests/test_historical_corpus.py` (NEW, 17 tests): tampered seeds
  fail (missing key / bad UUID / bad enum / extra key); ingest
  produces expected accept/reject counts; consent-missing rejection
  for non-synthetic; idempotent re-ingest; stat output matches
  pinned EXPECTED_STAT; validate reports eligibility drift without
  failing the run; corrupted lines surface in failures; shipped
  seeds are all source=synthetic.
- `docs/specs/historical_corpus.md` (NEW): on-disk layout, row
  shape, eligibility rules, consent invariant, ingest / validate /
  stat usage.

Consent invariant (load-bearing): every real founder pitch must have
`provenance.consent_documented = true`. Synthetic rows
(`provenance.source = "synthetic"`) are exempt. ingest() refuses any
non-synthetic row with consent_documented=false — this is the gate
that lets the corpus be used in published validation work.

Pinned stat for the seed manifest (asserted by tests):
  total_rows=25, by_source={synthetic: 25}, by_domain has 5 each in
  fintech / healthtech / biotech / deeptech / consumer, by_year has
  2012:4, 2014:4, 2016:5, 2018:5, 2020:5, 2025:1, 2029:1, eligibility

Task: Add a leakage-audit pass that runs before any validation-study
report can be rendered. The audit verifies (a) no holdout pitch was
used to fit any embedding / anti-gaming / contradiction-direction
artifact, (b) the corpus splits cleanly across the pre/post-2020
buffer year, and (c) per-feature training/holdout marginals do not
drift (KS + PSI). A failure raises LEAKAGE_DETECTED and blocks the
final report from being written.

What shipped:
- `server/fund/services/temporal_split.py` (NEW): SplitConfig,
  SplitResult, pitch_year_of, split. Defaults pinned at
  train_end="2019-12-31", buffer_year=2020,
  holdout_start="2021-01-01"; pitches dated 2020 are placed in
  buffer_excluded and never reach either side. Inverted-window
  configurations raise TemporalSplitError at construction.
- `server/fund/services/leakage_audit.py` (NEW): pure-stdlib audit.
  ks_two_sample (two-sample KS with tie handling, alpha=0.05 critical
  1.36/sqrt((n1+n2)/(n1*n2))); population_stability_index
  (training-quantile bins, ε-floored log term); PSI ≥ 0.25 → warn,
  PSI ≥ 0.50 → error. audit() composes membership + temporal split +
  drift into a structured LeakageReport with a stable audit_digest;
  enforce() raises LeakageDetectedError(code=LEAKAGE_DETECTED) on any
  failed assertion. Buffer override requires
  buffer_override_rationale.

  training_set_hash="PENDING_FIRST_FIT". Operator updates the index
  whenever an artifact is recomputed; the audit warns when the
  declared hash does not match the recomputed sha256 over sorted
  training_pitch_ids.
- `server/fund/services/validation_study.py` (MOD): StudyConfig adds
  training_artifacts_index_path + audit_feature_extractors. run_study
  calls leakage_audit.audit + enforce AFTER fit/metric computation
  and BEFORE writing canonical bytes — a failure raises and no
  output is produced. generated_with records leakage_audit_digest
  and leakage_audit_passed. Existing 14 validation-study tests
  unchanged and still pass.
- `cli.py` (MOD): new ``leakage audit`` verb. Flags --manifest,
  --training-artifacts-index, --feature (repeatable), --train-end,
  --buffer-year, --holdout-start, --buffer-override-rationale,
  --output. Exit 0 on pass, 2 on LEAKAGE_DETECTED.
- `tests/test_leakage_audit.py` (NEW, 15 tests):
  * temporal_split buffer-year exclusion + undated-row sequestration
    + inverted-window rejection.
  * Planted artifact-membership leak detected; LeakageDetectedError
    carries the LEAKAGE_DETECTED code attribute.
  * Distribution-drift planted shift trips the PSI ≥ 0.50 error band.
  * Clean case passes; KS / PSI sanity (zero on identical,
    alarm on disjoint).
  * Buffer override without rationale fails; with rationale passes.
  * Declared holdout pitches outside the post-buffer window flagged

Mandatory-block contract (load-bearing): the audit runs on every
``validation-study run`` invocation; there is no bypass flag. The audit
is invoked AFTER fit/metric computation but BEFORE any canonical bytes

Buffer-year default (load-bearing): 2020. Shrinking it requires an

buffer_override_rationale. Both gates are tested.

Determinism: same corpus + same training-artifacts index + same feature

PREVIOUS PROMPT — Prompt 44 of 70 (Wave 12)
================================================================================

Task: Build a deterministic, replayable coherence-vs-outcome regression
study harness. Loads the joined corpus + outcomes, fits
``logit(survival_5yr) ~ coherence_score + domain_primary +
log(check_size_usd)`` plus per-domain sub-models, and emits a report
with point estimates, 95/99 % bootstrap CIs (n=10000), Brier score,
AUC, calibration curve, and pre-registered hypothesis decisions.

What shipped:
- `data/governed/validation/preregistration.yaml` (NEW): frozen study
  contract. version=v1.0; primary hypothesis H1 (coherence_score
  positively associated with survival_5yr at α=0.01); secondary H2
  (monotonic dose-response across coherence quintiles, Q5 - Q1 ≥ 0.05
  with a 0.05 slack); Bonferroni correction across per-domain
  sub-models (family_alpha=0.05, divided by k fitted sub-models);
  bootstrap iterations=10000 with deterministic stdlib RNG;
  stopping_rule.minimum_n_with_known_outcome=200, on_violation=raise
  INSUFFICIENT_SAMPLE; negative_results_policy commits to publishing
  null and wrong-sign results; scope_boundary marks the claim as
  prediction (NOT causation). Bumping any pinned constant requires a
  new version + amendments stanza.
- `server/fund/services/validation_study.py` (NEW): StudyConfig,
  StudyRow, StudyReport dataclasses; pure-stdlib Newton-Raphson IRLS
  with a 1e-6 ridge for stability; row-level bootstrap via
  random.Random(config.seed); brier_score, auc_roc (Mann-Whitney with
  average ranks for ties), calibration_curve (10 equal-width bins),
  _percentile (linear interpolation); _evaluate_primary (rejects H0
  when 1-α CI excludes 0 *and* direction matches);
  _evaluate_quintile_dose_response (5 rank-quintiles, monotonicity +
  Q5-Q1≥0.05); _per_domain_models (Bonferroni-corrected sub-models for
  domains with N≥30; smaller domains in insufficient_subgroups);
  _detect_optional_libs records numpy/statsmodels/sklearn versions in
  generated_with for audit only — math is stdlib regardless; tiny
  stdlib YAML reader for the preregistration (no PyYAML at runtime).
  InsufficientSampleError raised when N < pre-registered minimum.
- `server/fund/services/validation_report.py` (NEW): pure-function
  Markdown renderer over the canonical JSON. Mentions N, primary +
  secondary decisions, AUC/Brier, the calibration table, the
  coefficient table with 95 / 99 % CIs, per-domain Bonferroni-
  corrected sub-models, and the disclosure section.
- `cli.py` (MOD): `validation-study run --output ... [--seed N
  --manifest ... --outcomes ... --scores ... --preregistration ...
  --bootstrap-iters N]` and `validation-study report --in
  <report.json>`. run exits 2 with INSUFFICIENT_SAMPLE if the joined
  frame is too small.
- `deploy/scripts/run_validation_study.py` (NEW): operator entry point
  with the same flags as the CLI verb.
- `tests/test_validation_study.py` (NEW, 14 tests): determinism (same
  config + frame → byte-identical artifact); planted-effect recovery
  across 3 (data_seed, boot_seed) parameterizations rejects H0 at
  α=0.01; quintile dose-response on the planted frame is monotonic;
  stopping rule raises InsufficientSampleError carrying the
  INSUFFICIENT_SAMPLE token; preregistration with missing required
  keys raises PreregistrationError; pure-metric sanity (Brier/AUC/
  calibration); fit_logit recovers sign on clean simulated data;
  Markdown renderer mentions headline facts.
- `docs/specs/validation_study.md` (NEW): pre-registration policy,
  report shape, determinism contract, negative-results commitment,
  prediction-not-causation boundary, runbooks, glossary.

Determinism contract (load-bearing): same StudyConfig + same frame →
byte-identical canonical bytes. Bootstrap RNG is random.Random(seed)
— never global. The canonical dict is round-tripped through
json.dumps(sort_keys=True) before being returned, so a caller cannot
corrupt internal state by mutating fields like config.output_path.

Stopping rule (load-bearing): N(known outcome) < 200 ⇒ raise
InsufficientSampleError("INSUFFICIENT_SAMPLE: ..."). No partial report
is ever emitted — the harness exits cleanly, the CLI returns 2.

Preregistration as a contract: any change to a pinned constant
requires bumping ``version:`` and adding an ``amendments:`` entry. The
loader rejects documents missing required top-level keys, and the
report carries the full preregistration document so a reader can
verify the hypotheses were not rewritten after the data.

CLI behavior today: ``validation-study run --output /tmp/study.json``
exits 2 with INSUFFICIENT_SAMPLE because the corpus has 25 manifest
rows and no scores artifact. The harness will run end-to-end as soon
as outcomes.jsonl + a coherence-scores artifact bring the joined
frame above 200 known-outcome rows.

PROMPT 47 — Cosine Paradox replication harness (Wave 13)
================================================================

Independent replication of the working paper headline that
entailment and contradiction NLI pairs are statistically
indistinguishable in raw all-mpnet-base-v2 cosine space. The
harness is deterministic, stdlib-only, and pre-registered.

- `Experiments/Cosine_Paradox_Replication/preregistration.yaml`
  (NEW): frozen alpha=0.01, n_permutations=10000,
  n_bootstrap=10000, seed=47, minimum_n_per_label=200, encoder
  pinned to sentence-transformers/all-mpnet-base-v2, leakage
  assumption documented (SNLI/MultiNLI plausibly in encoder pre-
  training mix), prohibited_actions enumerated.
- `Experiments/Cosine_Paradox_Replication/run_replication.py`
  (NEW): Mann-Whitney U with tie correction, Wendt rank-biserial
  effect size with stratified bootstrap 95% CI, two-sided
  permutation p-value with (count+1)/(iters+1) smoothing.
  Cosines load from a JSON file, a raw NLI .jsonl + embedder, or
  the bundled fixture. Refuses network unless --allow-network.
  Stopping rule applies to non-fixture sources. Canonical JSON
  output is byte-identical given (cosines_digest, seed, iter
  counts). Falsification rule: |r| >= 0.20 AND p < 0.01 ->
  paradox_refuted (publish either way).
- `Experiments/Cosine_Paradox_Replication/expected_report.json`
  (NEW): pinned baseline from --dry-run on the bundled fixture.
- `Experiments/Cosine_Paradox_Replication/fixtures/
   tiny_nli_fixture.json` (NEW): 24 hand-picked cosines (8 per
  label) constructed so entailment/contradiction overlap and
  neutral is clearly separable; lets dry-run + tests run in
  seconds.
- `cli.py` (MOD): adds `replication cosine-paradox` with
  --dry-run / --cosines / --dataset / --output / --seed /
  --n-permutations / --n-bootstrap-iterations /
  --allow-network / --preregistration / --minimum-n-per-label.
- `tests/test_cosine_paradox_replication.py` (NEW, 18 tests):
  statistical primitives (ranks-with-ties, U on perfect-
  separation, rank-biserial bounds, descriptive stats,
  permutation p extremes); preregistration parse + required
  keys; dry-run matches pinned expected_report.json to 1e-6
  AND byte-identical across runs; falsification confirmed on
  fixture; secondary tests separate neutral with |r| >= 0.95;
  inputs digest sensitive to cosine perturbation; seed alters
  bootstrap CI but not point estimates; INSUFFICIENT_SAMPLE
  raised below stopping rule on non-fixture sources;
  NetworkAccessDenied on --dataset without --allow-network;
  falsification threshold pinned at 0.20; CLI smoke via
  subprocess yields a numerically-matching report.
- `docs/research/cosine_paradox_replication.md` (NEW): design
  table, falsification criterion, operating procedure,
  determinism contract, statistical methods, leakage caveat,
  file index, out-of-scope.

Determinism invariant (load-bearing): same cosines + same seed
+ same iter counts -> byte-identical canonical JSON modulo
`generated_with` (which records detected library versions and
is intentionally excluded from determinism comparisons in the
test).

Falsification invariant (load-bearing): the threshold 0.20 lives
in both preregistration.yaml AND
run_replication._FALSIFICATION_EFFECT_THRESHOLD; a regression
test enforces the constant. Loosening either requires a new
preregistration version with a written justification.

Verify with:
  arch -arm64 python3 -m pytest \
    tests/test_cosine_paradox_replication.py -v
  arch -arm64 python3 -m coherence_engine replication \
    cosine-paradox --dry-run


================================================================
PROMPT 48 — Contradiction-direction (ĉ) cross-domain stability (Wave 13)
================================================================

Cross-domain stability study for the contradiction-direction
vector ĉ derived in apps/site/.../research/contradiction_direction
.mdx. Tests whether one global ĉ generalises across MultiNLI
domains or whether the engine must carry one ĉ per domain.
Negative result is the publishable result.

- `core/contradiction_direction.py` (NEW): production surface for
  ĉ. `fit_c_hat(pairs) -> np.ndarray` builds per-pair Householder
  normals n_i = (u_i - v_i) / ||u_i - v_i|| and returns the
  leading right singular vector of the stacked normals as the
  principal contradiction axis, with a deterministic sign-fix
  (first non-zero coordinate positive). Companions: `pair_-
  directions`, `project` (sign-invariant |⟨u-v, ĉ⟩| score for
  ROC), `cosine`, `abs_cosine` (sign-invariant cosine — the right
  metric for comparing ĉ vectors).
- `Experiments/Contradiction_Direction_Stability/preregistration
  .yaml` (NEW): frozen n_subsamples=50, subsample_sizes={200, 500,
  1000}, bootstrap iterations=1000, seeded master streams for
  per_domain_fit / cross_domain_eval / subsample_master /
  bootstrap_master, minimum_pairs_per_domain_label=200, MultiNLI
  matched-dev `genre` field as the domain proxy. Decision rule
  (H1): single ĉ holds when pairwise abs-cosine min >= 0.70 AND
  median cross-domain AUC drop <= 0.05. Cross-fit protocol pinned:
  ĉ fit on A is evaluated only on held-out B pairs; within-domain
  baseline uses a deterministic 50/50 split. Prohibitions list
  no in-sample AUC, no post-hoc threshold relaxation, no domain-
  averaging before reporting, no metric swap.
- `Experiments/Contradiction_Direction_Stability/run_stability_-
  study.py` (NEW): numpy + stdlib deterministic harness that
  reuses the cosine-paradox YAML parser, ranks-with-ties,
  percentile, optional-package detector, and round-floats helpers
  so both studies emit reports under one contract. Reports five
  blocks: per_domain_c_hat, pairwise_cosine (full N×N abs-cosine
  matrix with 95% bootstrap CIs), cross_domain_auc (within-domain
  baseline + cross-domain matrix annotated with auc_drop_vs_-
  baseline), subsample_sensitivity (mean/std/CI of abs-cosine to
  ĉ(full pool) at each pre-registered N), and decision (criterion
  text, thresholds, observed quantities, single_c_hat_holds bool,
  outcome string ∈ {single_c_hat_generalises,
  per_domain_c_hat_required}). Falsification thresholds pinned in
  module: _FALSIFICATION_PAIRWISE_COSINE = 0.70 and
  _FALSIFICATION_AUC_DROP = 0.05. Bootstrap CIs use
  random.Random for index sampling so byte-identity does not
  depend on numpy.random version drift.
- `Experiments/Contradiction_Direction_Stability/fixtures/tiny_-
  two_domain_fixture.json` (NEW): 2 synthetic domains, 16
  contradiction + 16 entailment pairs each, dim=4. Domain A's
  contradiction axis is e_0; domain B's is e_1 — orthogonal by
  construction. Harness end-to-end recovers ĉ_a ≈ e_0,
  ĉ_b ≈ e_1, pairwise abs-cosine ≈ 0, within-domain AUC = 1.0,
  cross-domain AUC = 0.0, decision = per_domain_c_hat_required.
  Stopping rule is skipped on source=="fixture".
- `cli.py` (MOD): adds `replication c-hat-stability` with
  --dry-run / --corpus / --output / --seed /
  --n-bootstrap-iterations / --n-subsamples / --preregistration /
  --minimum-pairs-per-domain-label. `_cmd_replication` refactored
  to dispatch between `cosine-paradox` and `c-hat-stability`.
- `tests/test_c_hat_stability.py` (NEW, 19 tests): fit_c_hat
  geometry (single-pair Householder, sign canonicalisation,
  principal-axis recovery on 20 e_1-aligned pairs + 2 e_2-aligned
  outliers, normalised pair_directions, sign-invariant abs_cosine,
  sign-dropping project, error-on-empty / error-on-wrong-shape);
  synthetic 2-domain fixture (orthogonal ĉ recovered with abs-
  cosine < 0.30, within-domain AUC > 0.85, cross-domain AUC <
  0.70, decision = per_domain_c_hat_required, subsample
  sensitivity reports each N); determinism (byte-identical across
  runs modulo `generated_with`, same seed → same run_id, different
  seed changes bootstrap CIs but not per-domain ĉ vectors or
  pairwise abs-cosine point estimates — both seed-free by SVD);
  preregistration loads with required keys, missing corpus +
  fixture path raises StabilityError; CLI smoke via subprocess
  produces report with expected schema_version and outcome.
- `docs/research/contradiction_direction_stability.md` (NEW):
  operationalisation table, decision rule stated word-for-word
  with both thresholds, cross-fit protocol explanation,
  determinism contract, operating procedure with corpus JSON
  shape, synthetic-fixture sanity check, report-block walkthrough,
  limits, file index.

Determinism invariant (load-bearing): same StabilityConfig + same
input pairs -> byte-identical canonical JSON modulo
`generated_with`. All bootstrap and subsample index sampling is
driven by random.Random seeded from preregistration.seeds.*; numpy
is used only for SVD and matrix arithmetic, never for randomness.

Falsification invariant (load-bearing): the two thresholds (0.70
abs-cosine, 0.05 AUC drop) live both in preregistration.yaml AND
in run_stability_study._FALSIFICATION_PAIRWISE_COSINE /
_FALSIFICATION_AUC_DROP. Loosening either requires a new
preregistration version with a written justification.

Cross-fit invariant (load-bearing): no in-sample AUC anywhere — ĉ
fit on A is evaluated only on held-out B pairs (cross-domain) or
on a deterministic 50/50 split of A (within-domain baseline).
Prereg's prohibited_actions lists "evaluating ĉ on the same pairs
used to fit it" first; cross_fit_protocol stanza spells out the
rule.

Verify with:
  arch -arm64 python3 -m pytest \
    tests/test_c_hat_stability.py -v
  arch -arm64 python3 -m coherence_engine replication \
    c-hat-stability --dry-run


================================================================
PROMPT 49 — Hoyer-sparsity vs raw-cosine head-to-head ROC (Wave 13)
================================================================

Head-to-head ROC comparison of three discriminators of NLI
contradiction vs entailment: raw cosine, Hoyer-sparsity of
(u - v), and ĉ-projection |⟨u-v, ĉ⟩|. Tests the Guide-3 claim
that the engine's signal is *meaningfully different* from raw
cosine. DeLong's two-sided z-test is the load-bearing inferential
statistic for the AUC comparison. All three outcomes (Hoyer wins,
cosine wins, no difference) are publishable per the negative-
results policy.

- `Experiments/Hoyer_vs_Cosine/preregistration.yaml` (NEW): frozen
  alpha=0.01, n_bootstrap=10000, random_seed=49,
  minimum_eval_pairs_per_label=200 (post 50/50 split, so corpus
  must carry >=400 per label), encoder pinned to sentence-
  transformers/all-mpnet-base-v2, neutral excluded from binary
  task. Decision rule (H1): DeLong two-sided p < alpha rejects
  AUC equality; direction read off sign of auc_diff. Cross-fit
  protocol: ĉ fit on fit-half of contradiction pairs ONLY; all
  three scores evaluated on eval-halves (paired). The
  directionality_note explicitly justifies two-sided (Guide-3 is
  "different", not "better"; one-sided would let cosine-wins
  slip past the gate). prohibited_actions: in-sample evaluation
  of ĉ, unpaired AUC comparison, post-hoc one-sided switch, AUC
  point estimates without CIs, eval-pair discards, encoder
  tuning.
- `Experiments/Hoyer_vs_Cosine/run_comparison.py` (NEW): numpy
  + stdlib deterministic harness reusing the cosine-paradox YAML
  parser, ranks-with-ties, percentile, optional-package
  detector, and round-floats helpers so all three Wave-13
  studies emit reports under one contract. Implements DeLong
  directly (no scipy dep): psi(a,b) matrix, V10/V01 placement
  values, sample covariance via centered outer product, and
  z = (AUC_a - AUC_b) / sqrt(S[a,a] + S[b,b] - 2*S[a,b]) with
  two-sided p via the erf normal CDF. Three score functions:
  cosine = 1 - cos(u,v), hoyer = hoyer_sparsity(u-v),
  projection = |<u-v, ĉ>|. Paired bootstrap: one resampled index
  set, three AUCs per iteration. Reports four blocks: auc
  (point + CI per classifier), delong (hoyer_vs_cosine +
  projection_vs_cosine, each with auc_diff, var_diff, z, p,
  reject_null, winner, null_hypothesis), interpretation, inputs.
- `Experiments/Hoyer_vs_Cosine/fixtures/tiny_pair_fixture.json`
  (NEW): 24 contradiction + 24 entailment pairs in dim=8. Both
  labels' difference vectors are constructed orthogonal to u
  with matching magnitudes -> cosines overlap heavily across
  labels (cos AUC ~0.5); entailment deltas dense (low Hoyer),
  contradiction deltas single-axis impulses (Hoyer = 1.0).
  Hoyer dominates cosine *by construction*. Stopping rule
  skipped on source=="fixture".
- `cli.py` (MOD): adds `replication hoyer-vs-cosine` with
  --dry-run / --corpus / --output / --seed /
  --n-bootstrap-iterations / --preregistration /
  --minimum-eval-pairs-per-label. `_cmd_replication` extended to
  dispatch among cosine-paradox | c-hat-stability |
  hoyer-vs-cosine.
- `tests/test_hoyer_vs_cosine.py` (NEW, 20 tests): ROC AUC
  primitives (perfect / inverted / tied / empty); DeLong
  (identical-classifiers var_diff=0+p=1, synthetic-dominance
  rejects at alpha, unequal-length raises, two-sided p
  symmetric in argument ordering); preregistration loads with
  required keys + pinned alpha/n_bootstrap/seed/minimum_eval +
  test field contains "two-sided"; end-to-end on fixture
  (AUC(hoyer)>=0.95, AUC(cosine)~0.5, DeLong rejects,
  primary_outcome="hoyer_signal_differs_from_cosine",
  winner="hoyer", projection also beats cosine); determinism
  (byte-identical bytes, seed alters CI/eval split, digest
  sensitive to single-coord perturbation); stopping rule raises
  InsufficientEvalSampleError on non-fixture below minimum;
  missing fixture+corpus path raises ComparisonError; report
  has all required blocks AND every AUC carries its CI (the
  "no point estimates without CIs" guard); schema_version
  pinned at "hoyer-vs-cosine-v1"; CLI smoke via subprocess.
- `docs/research/hoyer_vs_cosine.md` (NEW): operationalisation
  table, falsification criterion stated word-for-word with two-
  sided justification, DeLong walk-through (psi matrix, V10/V01
  placement values, sandwich variance, why paired beats
  unpaired), cross-fit protocol, determinism contract,
  operating procedure with corpus JSON shape, synthetic-fixture
  sanity check with expected numbers, report-block walkthrough,
  limits, file index.

Determinism invariant (load-bearing): same ComparisonConfig +
same input pairs -> byte-identical canonical JSON modulo
`generated_with`. Bootstrap and 50/50 split index sampling are
driven by random.Random seeded from config.seed; numpy is used
only for SVD inside fit_c_hat, the matrix-form psi of DeLong,
and score arithmetic — never for randomness.

Test-choice invariant (load-bearing): the test is two-sided
DeLong, pinned in preregistration.yaml's primary_hypothesis.test
AND asserted by test_preregistration_pins_two_sided_test. A post-
hoc switch to one-sided is in prohibited_actions because the
Guide-3 claim under test is "different from cosine", not "better
than cosine" — letting cosine-wins slip past a one-sided gate
would silently invert the negative-results policy.

Cross-fit invariant (load-bearing): no in-sample evaluation of
ĉ. Both labels are split 50/50 deterministically; ĉ is fit on
the fit-half of contradiction pairs only; all three scores
(cosine, hoyer, projection) are evaluated on the eval-halves of
both labels — paired across classifiers so DeLong's covariance
term and the bootstrap CI both reflect the same observations
per pair.

Verify with:
  arch -arm64 python3 -m pytest \
    tests/test_hoyer_vs_cosine.py -v
  arch -arm64 python3 -m coherence_engine replication \
    hoyer-vs-cosine --dry-run


PROMPT 50 — Reverse-Marxism reflection-recovery rigor (Wave 13)
================================================================

Replicates the headline 84.3% Householder-reflection recovery
claim under stricter conditions. The original number was reported
on the same Marx text used to fit the class axis. This study tests
whether the recovery property survives (a) held-out concept axes,
(b) bootstrapped CI on recovery rate, (c) a random-reflection null
baseline, and (d) a pre-registered alpha sensitivity sweep.

- `Experiments/Reverse_Marxism_Rigor/preregistration.yaml` (NEW):
  frozen random_seed=50, n_random_axes=100, n_bootstrap=10000,
  ci_percent=95.0, alpha_grid=[0.5, 1.0, 1.5, 2.0, 2.5, 3.0],
  minimum_holdout_sentences=50, minimum_axis_seeds=5. Encoder
  pinned to sentence-transformers/all-mpnet-base-v2. Axis built
  by averaging axis_seed_embeddings then L2-normalising. Reflection
  formula: v - alpha*dot(v, axis)*axis. held_out_protocol forbids
  axis fit on holdout sentences (HeldOutLeakageError). The
  random_baseline section documents that the 0.5 idealised null is
  NOT the decision threshold; the empirical CI is. prohibited_
  actions forbid axis fit on evaluation data, single point
  estimate without null, post-hoc alpha selection, holdout
  discards after seeing scores, operationalisation swap, seed
  amendment without version bump.
- `Experiments/Reverse_Marxism_Rigor/run_rigor_study.py` (NEW):
  numpy + stdlib deterministic harness reusing the cosine-paradox
  YAML parser, percentile, optional-package detector, and round-
  floats helpers. Implements generalised Householder reflection,
  centroid-then-L2-normalise axis fit, sign-on-axis recovery
  operationalisation, random unit-vector sampling, bootstrap CI
  on the recovery rate, per-alpha random-axis null distribution
  summary, and the decision block (primary_held_out_ci_low vs
  primary_random_baseline_ci_high at alpha=2). Alpha keys
  canonicalised as f"alpha_{value:.4f}".
- `Experiments/Reverse_Marxism_Rigor/fixtures/tiny_rigor_fixture.json`
  (NEW): 8 axis seeds clustered along e_0 + 60 holdout sentences
  in dim=16 with explicit ideology_label in {-1, +1}. Recovery is
  perfect at alpha>=1.5 by construction; random-axis baseline is
  far below the held-out CI.
- `cli.py` (MOD): adds `replication reverse-marxism-rigor` with
  --dry-run / --corpus / --output / --seed / --n-bootstrap /
  --n-random-axes / --preregistration / --minimum-holdout-sentences
  / --minimum-axis-seeds. `_cmd_replication` extended to dispatch
  cosine-paradox | c-hat-stability | hoyer-vs-cosine |
  reverse-marxism-rigor.
- `tests/test_reverse_marxism_rigor.py` (NEW, 28 tests):
  reflection math (alpha=2 flips sign + leaves orthogonal
  components untouched, alpha=1 zeroes axis projection, alpha=0 is
  identity); axis fit centroid-then-normalise; recovery rate
  primitives (perfect axis -> 1, orthogonal axis -> 0); random
  unit-vector shape + norm; bootstrap CI (all-1s -> [1,1],
  all-0s -> [0,0], balanced -> ~0.5); preregistration loads with
  required keys + pinned values; alpha=2 in grid; held_out_protocol
  + random_baseline + prohibitions present; end-to-end on fixture
  (recovery >=0.95 at alpha=2, baseline mean far below 0.5,
  decision generalises); alpha sweep includes the full grid;
  determinism (byte-identical bytes, seed alters baseline only,
  digest sensitive to perturbation); held-out leakage detected;
  insufficient-holdout raises on non-fixture; missing fixture +
  corpus raises RigorError; invalid ideology_label raises;
  report has all required blocks AND every alpha carries CI on
  BOTH blocks (the no-point-estimate-without-CI guard);
  schema_version pinned at "reverse-marxism-rigor-v1"; decision
  uses empirical baseline (NOT 0.5); CLI smoke via subprocess.
- `docs/research/reverse_marxism_rigor.md` (NEW): operationalisation
  table, falsification criterion stated word-for-word with the
  empirical-baseline rationale, held-out and random-baseline
  protocol, determinism contract, operating procedure with corpus
  JSON shape, synthetic-fixture sanity check with expected
  numbers, limits, file index.

Determinism invariant (load-bearing): same RigorConfig + same
input corpus -> byte-identical canonical JSON modulo
`generated_with`. All sampling (bootstrap, random-axis draws)
uses random.Random seeded from the pre-registration; numpy is
used only for vector arithmetic, never for randomness.

Held-out invariant (load-bearing): the axis is fit ONLY on
training_corpus.axis_seed_embeddings; the recovery test runs
ONLY on holdout_corpus.sentences. The harness raises
HeldOutLeakageError before emitting any bytes if it detects
overlap between the two slabs to 1e-8 precision.

Decision invariant (load-bearing): primary_generalises requires
held_out_recovery_ci_low > random_baseline_ci_high at alpha=2,
where random_baseline_ci_high is the EMPIRICAL CI (not the 0.5
idealisation) computed from n_random_axes draws. test_decision_
uses_empirical_baseline_not_idealised_05 enforces this.

Verify with:
  arch -arm64 python3 -m pytest \
    coherence_engine/tests/test_reverse_marxism_rigor.py -v
  arch -arm64 python3 -m coherence_engine replication \
    reverse-marxism-rigor --dry-run

MOST RECENT PROMPT — Prompt 51 of 70 (Wave 14)
================================================================================

Task: Stand up the capital-deployment surface. Add a CapitalDeployment
service interface with two pluggable backends (Stripe Connect for
non-US founder payouts, BankTransfer / Mercury for ACH/wire) that
*prepare* investment-transfer instructions and emit an
investment_funding_prepared event. An authenticated `treasurer` must
explicitly approve before execute, and amounts ≥ $250k require dual
approval. The software does NOT execute transfers autonomously.

What shipped:
- `alembic/versions/20260425_000009_capital_deployment.py` (NEW):
  fund_investment_instructions + fund_treasurer_approvals tables.
  Unique index on (instruction_id, treasurer_id) so the same human
  cannot double-sign to satisfy dual approval.
- `server/fund/models.py` (MOD): InvestmentInstruction +
  TreasurerApproval ORM rows; ``approvals`` relationship between
  them.
- `server/fund/services/capital_backends.py` (NEW): CapitalBackend
  protocol; StripeConnectBackend (reads STRIPE_SECRET_KEY +
  STRIPE_CONNECT_ACCOUNT_ID + optional STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET);
  BankTransferBackend (reads MERCURY_API_TOKEN + MERCURY_API_BASE,
  validates counterparty token via verify_counterparty before
  prepare); verify_stripe_webhook_signature does constant-time
  HMAC-SHA-256 with a 5-min skew check; backend_for_method factory.
- `server/fund/services/capital_deployment.py` (NEW):
  CapitalDeployment.prepare / approve / execute / cancel.
  prepare() collapses on idempotency_key (one instruction +
  one outbox event per key). execute() enforces single approval
  always and dual approval at amounts ≥ DUAL_APPROVAL_THRESHOLD_USD
  (default $250k, override via CAPITAL_DUAL_APPROVAL_THRESHOLD_USD).
  Backend failure marks the instruction ``failed`` and writes the
  error_code to the row before re-raising.
- `server/fund/routers/capital.py` (NEW): four endpoints, each
  gated by _gate() (an inline _attach_principal helper that mirrors
  partner_api). prepare → 201 (partner / treasurer / admin); approve
  → 200 (treasurer / admin); execute → 200 (treasurer / admin), 403
  if not approved or dual-approval shortfall; webhooks/stripe
  rejects unsigned/skewed/forged HMACs with 401, otherwise updates
  the matched instruction's status.
- `server/fund/schemas/events/investment_funding_prepared.v1.json`
  + `investment_funded.v1.json` (NEW): Draft 2020-12 schemas with
  required fields instruction_id, application_id, founder_id,
  amount_usd, currency, preparation_method (enum stripe|bank_transfer).
- `tests/test_capital_deployment.py` (NEW): backend unit tests,
  service-level state-machine tests (prepare idempotency, execute-
  requires-approve, full happy path, dual-approval gate at
  threshold, repeat-approve-by-same-treasurer does not double
  count), Stripe signature accept/reject, router via TestClient
  with a tiny middleware that stamps ``request.state.principal``
  for role tests.
- `docs/specs/capital_deployment.md` (NEW): state machine table,
  endpoint table, backend list, event list, storage discipline,
  prohibitions list (cites prompt 51), operational runbook.
- `.env.example` (MOD): STRIPE_SECRET_KEY,
  STRIPE_CONNECT_ACCOUNT_ID, STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET,
  MERCURY_API_TOKEN, MERCURY_API_BASE,
  CAPITAL_DUAL_APPROVAL_THRESHOLD_USD.

Non-autonomy invariant (load-bearing): execute() always raises
InstructionStateError without a prior TreasurerApproval row, and
without a second distinct approval at amounts ≥ DUAL_APPROVAL_
THRESHOLD_USD. The router translates these to HTTP 403. There is no
scheduler, no auto-approval, and no code path that calls
CapitalDeployment.execute outside the explicit treasurer route.

Storage discipline (load-bearing): target_account_ref is an opaque
counterparty token. Raw bank account / routing numbers never enter
the database; the BankTransferBackend.verify_counterparty step
asserts the token was minted by the upstream provider.

MOST RECENT PROMPT — PROMPT 52 (Wave 14): E-SIGNATURE ADAPTER
================================================================================

Goal: a single internal interface (ESignatureProvider) that sends
SAFE / term-sheet documents through one of two providers (DocuSign,
Dropbox Sign / formerly HelloSign), tracks lifecycle status, verifies
webhook signatures, and persists only the SIGNED PDF (never the
unsigned body) to object storage.

Files added / modified:

- `alembic/versions/20260425_000010_signature_requests.py` (NEW):
  fund_signature_requests table with the lifecycle columns, a
  unique index on idempotency_key, and indices on application_id,
  status, and provider_request_id.
- `server/fund/models.py` (MOD): SignatureRequest ORM row whose
  docstring documents the storage discipline + operator obligation.
- `server/fund/services/esignature.py` (NEW): ESignatureProvider
  protocol; PreparedDocument / Signer / SendResponse /
  SignedArtifact value types; ESignatureService owning
  prepare/send/void/apply_webhook on SignatureRequest. The
  unsigned document body is rendered IN MEMORY and discarded
  after dispatch; the database stores only document_template +
  template_vars_hash. apply_webhook is idempotent on duplicates
  and uploads the signed PDF returned by the provider to object
  storage on `signed`.
- `server/fund/services/esignature_backends.py` (NEW):
  DocuSignBackend + DropboxSignBackend. DocuSign Connect HMAC v2
  verifier (verify_docusign_webhook_signature) iterates active
  secrets × X-DocuSign-Signature-N headers. Dropbox Sign verifier
  (verify_dropbox_sign_webhook_signature) recomputes
  HMAC-SHA-256(api_key, event_time + event_type) and
  compare_digest's against event.event_hash; the backend also
  accepts an X-DropboxSign-Signature raw-body HMAC header.
- `server/fund/data/legal_templates/safe_note_v1.docx.j2` (NEW):
  PLACEHOLDER YC post-money SAFE template -- NOT counsel reviewed.
- `server/fund/data/legal_templates/README.md` (NEW): Operator
  obligation -- replace each template with a counsel-approved
  version before any production signature request. This software
  does not produce legal advice.
- `server/fund/routers/esignature_webhooks.py` (NEW):
  POST /webhooks/esignature/docusign and
  POST /webhooks/esignature/dropbox-sign. Both routes verify the
  signature against the raw body BEFORE any state mutation;
  signature failure returns 401 with no DB writes.
- `tests/test_esignature.py` (NEW, 26 tests, all passing):
  template rendering + canonical vars-hash determinism; backend
  prepare/send/fetch idempotency; DocuSign signature accept-valid
  / accept-rotated-secret / reject-bad-digest / reject-empty;
  Dropbox Sign signature accept-valid / reject-bad-hash /
  reject-empty; service-layer prepare-idempotency +
  send-after-prepare + var-substitution rejection; signed-PDF
  round-trip through LocalFilesystemBackend; router via
  TestClient: 401 on bad signature, 200 + state mutation on
  valid webhook; backend.from_env raises ESignatureConfigError.
- `docs/specs/esignature.md` (NEW): provider protocol, lifecycle
  state machine, webhook-signature schemes, endpoint table,
  storage discipline, operator obligation, prohibitions list.
- `.env.example` (MOD): DOCUSIGN_INTEGRATION_KEY,
  DOCUSIGN_USER_ID, DOCUSIGN_RSA_PRIVATE_KEY,
  DOCUSIGN_CONNECT_HMAC_SECRETS, DROPBOX_SIGN_API_KEY,
  DROPBOX_SIGN_API_BASE.

Mandatory invariants honored (load-bearing prompt-52 prohibitions):

* Webhook signature verification is NEVER skipped. Both routes
  return HTTP 401 on missing/invalid signatures and never mutate
  state. There is no env-gated dev bypass for the e-signature
  surface.
* The placeholder SAFE template is NOT published as
  counsel-reviewed -- the README, the docs spec, and the model
  docstring all state explicitly that production templates must
  be reviewed by securities counsel and that this software does
  not provide legal advice.
* The unsigned document body is NEVER persisted. render_template()
  returns a PreparedDocument whose body is in-memory only;
  ESignatureService.prepare and .send both delete the document
  reference after dispatch. The database stores only the template
  id + the SHA-256 of the canonical-JSON variables.

Verify with:

  PYTEST_DISABLE_PLUGIN_AUTOLOAD=1 python3 -m pytest \
    coherence_engine/tests -v -x -q -p anyio -p asyncio

MOST RECENT PROMPT — PROMPT 53 (Wave 14): FOUNDER KYC/AML ADAPTER
================================================================================

Goal: founder-side sanctions / PEP / ID / AML screening, mandatory
upstream of any capital instruction. Persists a KYCResult row per
founder with annual refresh cadence; re-screen on every funding
event. Distinct from prompt 26's accredited-investor flow (LP/Rule
501) -- separate tables, separate provider env vars, separate
routers, separate webhook URLs so a leaked LP-flow secret cannot
forge a founder webhook.

  fund_kyc_results table (id, founder_id, provider, status,

  persisted; raw KYC document bytes never enter the database.

  initiate_kyc, apply_webhook (HMAC-verified, replay no-op for

  the decision-policy gate), scan_refresh_due (daily-job hook:
  emits founder_kyc.refresh_due events 30d before expires_at;

- `server/fund/services/decision_policy.py` (MOD): new `kyc_clear`

  backward-compatible (gate not enforced). True = clear. False =
  adds KYC_REQUIRED to failed_gates. KYC_REQUIRED is in the
  manual_review set, so a missing/expired/failed KYC downgrades a
  would-be `pass` to `manual_review` -- never to an automatic
  `fail`.
- `server/fund/routers/founder_kyc.py` (NEW): operator portal
  POST /founders/{id}/kyc:initiate (gated by current_founder_kyc;
  service-role bypass for admin / analyst / viewer) and
  GET /founders/{id}/kyc; webhooks
  POST /webhooks/founder_kyc/persona,

  set_kyc_backend_factory_for_tests /
  reset_kyc_backend_factory_for_tests.
- `tests/test_founder_kyc.py` (NEW, 19 tests, all passing):
  HMAC accept/reject (valid / bad / skewed); service-layer
  initiate idempotency, valid-signature flips status, replay
  no-op, lazy expiry, screening-category serialization;
  decision-policy gate (`pass` -> `manual_review` with
  KYC_REQUIRED when kyc_passed=False, `pass` when True, backward
  compat when absent, hard-fail still wins); refresh-due cadence
  (event emitted within 30d window, idempotent on re-run, skipped
  far-out); router via TestClient (initiate redirect URL,
  get-latest, webhook 401 on bad signature, webhook flips to
  passed and is_kyc_clear True).
- `docs/specs/founder_kyc.md` (NEW): why founder KYC is upstream
  of capital instructions; separation from prompt 26 (table /
  env-var / router / webhook splits); lifecycle; decision-policy
  gate contract; refresh cadence + re-screen-on-funding rule;
  storage discipline; operator runbook for handling a failed KYC
  (manual review, never auto-reject the founder forever); env-var
  table.

Mandatory invariants honored (load-bearing prompt-53 prohibitions):

* `pass` is impossible without an unexpired KYCResult.passed: the
  decision-policy `kyc_clear` gate downgrades to `manual_review`
  whenever application["kyc_passed"] is explicitly False;
  is_kyc_clear treats expired rows as not-passed via lazy-expiry
  semantics.
* Raw KYC document content is never logged or persisted -- the
  table holds only evidence_hash (SHA-256) and evidence_uri
  (provider's opaque reference). No payload bytes are emitted in
  log lines or events.
* A failed KYC routes to manual_review, NOT to permanent
  rejection. KYC_REQUIRED is in the manual_review set, never the
  hard_fail set; the docs spec spells out the operator runbook
  for handling false positives, escalations, and re-screens.

================================================================================
MOST RECENT PROMPT — PROMPT 54 (Wave 14): CALENDAR / SCHEDULING ADAPTER
================================================================================

Goal: auto-book partner meetings on every enforce-mode `pass`
decision. Two pluggable backends sit behind a `Scheduler` interface
-- Cal.com (primary, hosted scheduling API) and Google Calendar
(fallback for personal calendars). On `pass`, ApplicationService
emits `scheduling_requested`; the scheduler queries availability,
proposes the top-3 slots in a `MeetingProposal` row, and on
founder click-through books the chosen slot, writes a `Booking`
row, and emits `meeting_booked`.

Files added / modified:

- `alembic/versions/20260425_000012_scheduling.py` (NEW):
  fund_meeting_proposals (id, application_id, partner_email,
  founder_email, duration_min, proposed_slots_json [Text JSON --
  not JSONB so SQLite + Postgres share one definition], token
  [unique], status [pending|booked|expired|cancelled], backend,
  created_at, expires_at, booked_at, cancelled_at) and
  fund_bookings (id, proposal_id [unique FK], application_id,
  backend, provider_event_id, partner_email, founder_email,
  scheduled_start, scheduled_end, status, created_at). Indices
  on application_id, token (unique), status; bookings unique on
  proposal_id. down_revision = "20260425_000011".
- `server/fund/models.py` (MOD): MeetingProposal + Booking ORM
  rows backing the migration; lifecycle docstrings reference
  the spec at `docs/specs/scheduling.md`.
- `server/fund/services/scheduler.py` (NEW): `Scheduler` class
  with `propose(application_id, partner_email, duration_min=30,
  ...)` and `book(token, chosen_slot_start, ...)`. Token TTL
  defaults to 72h, hard-cap of 3 proposed slots
  (MAX_PROPOSED_SLOTS = 3). Errors: `SchedulerError`,
  `ProposalNotFoundError`, `TokenExpiredError`,
  `ProposalCancelledError`. Idempotent book: a second call with
  the same token returns the existing Booking with
  `idempotent_replay=True` and never invokes the backend twice.
  Helper `emit_scheduling_event(events, ...)` publishes the
  `scheduling_requested` outbox event.
- `server/fund/services/scheduler_backends.py` (NEW):
  SchedulerBackend protocol; CalComBackend (lazy-imports
  `requests`, reads CALCOM_API_KEY / CALCOM_API_BASE /
  CALCOM_EVENT_TYPE_ID); GoogleCalendarBackend (lazy-imports
  google-auth + google-api-python-client, reads
  GOOGLE_CALENDAR_OAUTH_*); InMemorySchedulerBackend (test seam,
  raises on double-book). Slot/BookedEvent dataclasses are UTC-
  enforced. `_pick_top_three` collapses duplicate starts and
  hard-caps at 3. `scheduler_backend_from_env()` factory keyed
  on SCHEDULER_PROVIDER (defaults to "calcom"). Neither SDK is
  a hard dependency.
- `server/fund/routers/scheduling.py` (NEW):
  POST /scheduling/proposals (analyst/admin gated, 503 on
  PROVIDER_UNAVAILABLE) and POST /scheduling/book (404 on
  unknown token, 410 GONE on expired token, 409 on cancelled,
  200 with idempotent_replay=true on a repeated successful
  booking). Test seams:
  set_scheduler_factory_for_tests / set_scheduler_backend_factory_for_tests
  with reset helpers.
- `server/fund/services/application_service.py` (MOD): on
  `pass` + enforce-mode, emits `scheduling_requested` via the
  existing EventPublisher (idempotency_key
  `<scoring_job.idempotency_key>:SchedulingRequested`). Failure
  is logged but does NOT fail the scoring job. New helper
  `_resolve_partner_email(application)` reads
  SCHEDULER_DEFAULT_PARTNER_EMAIL with a deterministic
  fallback.
- `tests/test_scheduler.py` (NEW, 24 tests, all passing):
  value-type Slot validation; InMemoryBackend returns 3 distinct
  slots; CalCom / Google constructors raise
  SchedulerBackendConfigError on missing config; service-level
  propose persists 3 distinct slots with TTL == 72h; propose
  with empty availability marks proposal "expired"; book writes
  Booking + flips status; book idempotent on repeated token
  (single Booking row, idempotent_replay=True); book raises
  TokenExpiredError after TTL with lazy expiry transition;
  unknown token raises ProposalNotFoundError; chosen slot not in
  proposal raises SchedulerError; meeting_booked event payload;
  emit_scheduling_event publishes; router 201 with 3 slots,
  403 without role, 410 on expired token, 200 idempotent on
  re-book, 404 on unknown token, 503 on PROVIDER_UNAVAILABLE.
- `docs/specs/scheduling.md` (NEW): why, lifecycle diagram,
  backend table, slot bandwidth rationale (cap of 3), token
  model (NO env-gated bypass of expiry), idempotency contract,
  storage discipline, event table, HTTP error mapping, operator
  obligations.
- `.env.example` (MOD): SCHEDULER_PROVIDER,
  SCHEDULER_DEFAULT_PARTNER_EMAIL, CALCOM_API_KEY,
  CALCOM_API_BASE, CALCOM_EVENT_TYPE_ID,
  GOOGLE_CALENDAR_OAUTH_CLIENT_ID, GOOGLE_CALENDAR_OAUTH_CLIENT_SECRET,
  GOOGLE_CALENDAR_OAUTH_REFRESH_TOKEN, GOOGLE_CALENDAR_CALENDAR_ID.

Mandatory invariants honored (load-bearing prompt-54 prohibitions):

* Never propose more than 3 slots: `_pick_top_three` is the
  sole pathway and hard-caps the output; `Scheduler.propose`
  also slices defensively.
* No env-gated bypass of token expiry: `Scheduler.book` checks
  `expires_at <= now` unconditionally and raises
  `TokenExpiredError`; the route surfaces 410 GONE.
* Cal.com / Google Calendar are NOT hard dependencies: the
  SDKs (`requests`, `google-auth`, `google-api-python-client`)
  are imported lazily inside the methods that use them so the
  scheduler module imports cleanly with neither installed.
* No edits outside SCOPE.

Prompt 56 — Regulatory pathway selector (Reg D 506(b) /
Reg D 506(c) / Reg CF / Reg S) + jurisdictional gate.

Wave 15. Depends on prompts 26 (accredited verification) and
53 (founder KYC). Classifies each application against the
operator-configured registry of securities pathways and gates
the decision-policy `pass` outcome on a clear resolution. The
software does NOT pick a pathway autonomously and does NOT
provide legal advice — the YAML registry is owned by the
operator's licensed securities counsel.

Files:

- `data/governed/regulatory_pathways.yaml` (NEW): operator-
  edited registry. `schema_version: regulatory-pathways-v1`.
  Ships four placeholder pathways (`reg_d_506b`, `reg_d_506c`,
  `reg_cf`, `reg_s`) all with `counsel_signoff_at: null` so
  they default to `unclear` until counsel signs off. Global
  `counsel_signoff_ttl_days: 90`. Per-pathway fields:
  `jurisdiction` (US | non_US), `investor_requirement`
  (accredited_verified | self_certified | none),
  `advertising` (permitted | prohibited), `max_investors`
  (null = unlimited), `integration_window_days`,
  `counsel_signoff_required`, `counsel_signoff_at`,
  `counsel_signoff_by`.
- `server/fund/services/regulatory_pathway.py` (NEW):
  `Pathway` / `PathwayRegistry` / `PathwayMatch` frozen
  dataclasses. `load_pathway_registry(path=None)` parses the
  YAML, validates the schema version, rejects unknown
  jurisdictions and duplicate ids. `classify(application,
  *, registry, now=None) -> PathwayMatch` runs the
  deterministic match algorithm: (1) filter by jurisdiction
  (US vs non-US), (2) filter by advertising mode (or leave
  full set when application's mode is `unspecified`), (3)
  0 or > 1 candidate -> `ambiguous`, (4) exactly 1
  candidate but `investor_requirement` not satisfied ->
  `unclear`, (5) counsel signoff required and missing/stale
  -> `unclear`, (6) otherwise -> `clear`. Boolean shortcut
  `regulatory_pathway_clear(...)` returns True only when
  status == `clear`.
- `alembic/versions/20260425_000013_regulatory_pathway.py`
  (NEW): adds nullable
  `fund_applications.regulatory_pathway_id` (`String(64)`)
  plus index. `down_revision = "20260425_000012"`.
- `server/fund/models.py` (MOD): adds
  `Application.regulatory_pathway_id` (String(64), nullable,
  indexed). The column persists the resolved pathway id; a
  null value does NOT mean "fail" — the gate is driven by
  the threaded `regulatory_pathway_status`, not the column.
- `server/fund/services/decision_policy.py` (MOD): new gate
  `regulatory_pathway_clear` reads
  `application["regulatory_pathway_status"]`. Absent ->
  silent (backwards compatible). `unclear` -> reason
  `REGULATORY_PATHWAY_UNCLEAR`. `ambiguous` -> reason
  `REGULATORY_PATHWAY_AMBIGUOUS`. Any other non-`clear`
  value defensively folds to UNCLEAR. Both reason codes
  added to the `manual_review` set so a passing scoring
  envelope downgrades to `manual_review` (never to `fail`).
- `tests/test_regulatory_pathway.py` (NEW, 19 tests, all
  passing): YAML loader (default loads with the four
  expected pathways; rejects bad schema, bad jurisdiction,
  duplicate ids); classifier happy paths (506(c) clear when
  verified + signoff fresh, Reg S clear for non-US founder,
  506(b) clear with self-certified investor + advertising
  prohibited); classifier unclear (506(c) without verified
  investor, stale signoff, missing signoff); classifier
  ambiguous (no pathway matches jurisdiction, multiple
  match when advertising unspecified, jurisdiction missing);
  decision-policy integration (silent without field, clear
  passes, unclear/ambiguous/unknown all downgrade with the
  right reason code); Application model round-trip persists
  `regulatory_pathway_id`.
- `docs/specs/regulatory_pathway.md` (NEW): leading
  disclaimer (NOT legal advice; counsel owns the YAML),
  scope, YAML schema reference, deterministic match
  algorithm, decision-policy integration table, persistence
  notes, operator obligations, prompt-56 prohibitions.

Mandatory invariants honored (load-bearing prompt-56
prohibitions):

* Do NOT silently default to a pathway: ambiguity ALWAYS
  routes to `manual_review`; the classifier returns
  `ambiguous` whenever 0 or > 1 candidate matches, and the
  decision policy treats unknown values defensively as
  `UNCLEAR`.
* Do NOT advertise or solicit on a 506(b) pathway: the
  advertising filter rejects 506(b) as a candidate the
  moment `application["advertising_mode"] == "permitted"`.
* Do NOT permit a `pass` decision without
  `counsel_signoff_required` being met when configured:
  `_signoff_fresh()` returns False for both missing
  `counsel_signoff_at` and `counsel_signoff_at` older than
  `counsel_signoff_ttl_days`, forcing `unclear` and
  downgrading the decision.
* No edits outside SCOPE.

Verify with:
  python3 -m pytest -p "no:pytest-qt" \
    coherence_engine/tests/test_regulatory_pathway.py -v
  → 19 passed.

Prompt 57 (Wave 15) is complete. Data retention + GDPR /
CCPA right-to-delete with crypto-shredding shipped.

What landed:
* Per-row AES-256-GCM in
  `server/fund/services/per_row_encryption.py`. 96-bit
  random nonce; AAD bound to row_id (a ciphertext from row
  A reused under row B fails authentication). Pluggable
  EncryptionKeyStore -- default `_ModelKeyStore` reads /
  writes `fund_encryption_keys.key_material_b64`; the
  contract is the same when a KMS-backed store is injected
  via `set_encryption_key_store(...)`.
* Crypto-shredding in `server/fund/services/crypto_shred.py`.
  `shred_key(db, key_id)` zeros the stored key bytes and
  stamps `shredded_at`; the row is preserved as a tombstone
  so audit references stay interpretable. Idempotent;
  unknown key_id raises `KeyNotFoundError`.
* Governed retention policy in
  `data/governed/retention_policy.yaml` (schema_version:
  `retention-policy-v1`). Classes: transcript (90d,
  tombstone_and_shred), interview_recording (90d), kyc_evidence
  (1825d, BSA 5-yr), founder_pii (2555d, ~7-yr long-tail),
  decision_artifact (indefinite, KEEP), audit_log
  (indefinite, KEEP).
* Daily sweep + targeted erasure in
  `server/fund/services/retention.py`. `apply_retention(db)`
  walks every class, finds rows past horizon, tombstones the
  URI via `object_storage.delete`, crypto-shreds the per-row
  key, marks `redacted=True`. `execute_erasure(db, request_id)`
  runs after the 30-day grace, splits requested classes, and
  refuses any class flagged `on_expiry: keep` with
  `ERASURE_REFUSED_AUDIT_HOLD`.
* Two-phase privacy endpoints in
  `server/fund/routers/privacy.py`. POST
  `/privacy/erasure/issue` (admin/support) mints a one-shot
  URL-safe verification token; only its SHA-256 hash is
  persisted on a pending `ErasureRequest`. POST
  `/privacy/erasure` (subject) hashes the submitted token,
  matches it server-side, refuses audit-hold class targets,
  and otherwise schedules erasure for `now + 30d`. The
  handler returns `status="scheduled"` only -- never
  `"completed"`. `immediate=true` is admin-gated. Replays
  are idempotent.
* `server/fund/models.py` adds `EncryptionKey`,
  `ErasureRequest`, `<class>_key_id` + `redacted` /
  `redacted_at` / `redaction_reason` tombstone columns on
  `fund_applications`, `fund_interview_recordings`,
  `fund_kyc_results`. Migration
  `20260425_000014_retention_and_erasure.py` applies the
  schema; all new columns nullable / default-false (safe
  expand without backfill).
* Tests: `tests/test_retention.py` (7) covers policy
  parsing + validation, the aged-transcript sweep,
  audit-hold no-op, idempotency, and AAD-binding rejection.
  `tests/test_erasure_endpoint.py` (8) covers token
  issuance + matching, 401 paths, audit-hold refusal,
  idempotent replay, immediate-admin-gate, and the
  "no completion before worker runs" + 410-Gone-on-read
  contracts.
* `docs/specs/data_retention.md` documents the threat
  model, the policy table, crypto-shred mechanics, the
  daily worker contract, the two-phase erasure endpoint,
  the operator runbook (router wiring, cron, KMS swap,
  token revocation), and the prompt-57 prohibitions.

Mandatory invariants honored (load-bearing prompt-57
prohibitions):

* Do NOT erase audit-trail data: decision_artifact and
  audit_log are `on_expiry: keep`. The endpoint refuses
  any request whose class set intersects them with
  `ERASURE_REFUSED_AUDIT_HOLD`. The daily sweep inspects
  but never modifies kept classes.
* Do NOT confirm erasure before the deletion job runs: the
  handler returns `"scheduled"`. The DB row flips to
  `"completed"` only inside `execute_erasure(...)`, which
  runs from the worker after `scheduled_for`.
* Do NOT trust client-supplied `verification_token`: the
  handler hashes the submitted token and looks the row up
  by SHA-256. Subject_id mismatch on a valid token still
  returns 401. The plaintext token is returned exactly
  once at issue time and never persisted.
* No edits outside SCOPE.

Follow-ups intentionally left for future prompts (out of
prompt-57 SCOPE):

* Wire `privacy.router` into `server/fund/app.py` and add a
  `cli privacy issue-erasure-token --subject ...` shim
  that wraps `issue_verification_token`.
* Schedule `apply_retention` on the daily cron in
  `services/scheduled_jobs.py`.
* Re-encrypt existing in-place transcripts under per-row
  keys (backfill). New writes use per-row encryption
  immediately; legacy plaintext rows continue to read but
  are not crypto-shreddable until they are re-encrypted.

Verify with:
  python3 -m pytest -p "no:pytest-qt" \
    coherence_engine/tests/test_retention.py \
    coherence_engine/tests/test_erasure_endpoint.py -v
  → 7 + 8 = 15 passed.

Prompt 58 (Wave 15) is complete. PII tokenization + audit-log
RLS shipped.

What landed:
* Format-preserving tokenizer in
  `server/fund/services/pii_tokenization.py`. `tokenize(value,
  kind=, tenant_salt=)` returns `tok_<kind>_<32hex>` where the
  hex is the first 16 bytes of HMAC-SHA-256 over `kind + ":" +
  value` keyed by the per-tenant salt. Deterministic per
  (kind, salt); non-reversible without the salt; allowed
  kinds: `{email, name, phone, address}`. Salt resolves from
  explicit kwarg → `PII_TENANT_SALT` env var →
  `SecretManager.get("PII_TENANT_SALT")`; missing salt raises
  `PIITokenizationError`. Email values are lower-cased and
  stripped before tokenization so capitalisation drift never
  produces two tokens for the same person. Empty inputs raise
  `ValueError` rather than collapsing to a single global "empty"
  token.
* Scope-gated clear-PII reads in
  `server/fund/services/pii_clear_audit.py`. `read_clear(...)`
  (1) checks `principal.has_scope("pii:read_clear")`, raising
  `ClearReadDenied` (a `PermissionError`) when missing, (2)
  decrypts the per-row AES-GCM ciphertext under the row's
  key id via `per_row_encryption.decrypt`, (3) inserts a
  `PIIClearAuditLog` row carrying the *token* (never the
  clear value), the principal id+kind, the field kind, the
  subject table+id, the route, and the request id. The audit
  row is flushed on the request session so a rollback rolls
  back both sides — an audit row exists iff the caller
  observed the clear value.
* `server/fund/models.py` — `Founder` gains three columns:
  `email_token` (the deterministic token, indexed),
  `email_clear` (per-row AES-GCM ciphertext of the clear
  email), `email_clear_key_id` (foreign reference into
  `fund_encryption_keys`). `Founder.read_clear_email(db=,
  principal=, route=, request_id=, reason=)` is the only
  sanctioned path to the clear value. The legacy `email`
  column is intentionally retained as the **expand** half of
  an expand-backfill-contract rollout — a follow-up prompt
  drops it once every caller has been switched.
* `alembic/versions/20260425_000015_pii_tokenization.py` adds
  the three founder columns, the `pii_clear_audit_log` table
  (six indexed columns: principal_id, field_kind, token,
  subject_id, request_id, created_at), and on Postgres
  installs `PII_AUDIT_RLS_POLICIES` plus a defence-in-depth
  trigger `pii_clear_audit_log_no_update` that raises on any
  UPDATE / DELETE statement (catching attempts that bypass
  RLS). Best-effort backfill computes `email_token` and
  encrypts `email_clear` for existing founders; missing salt
  exits cleanly and re-runs on the next migration.
* `server/fund/security/rls.py` adds `PII_AUDIT_RLS_POLICIES`
  as a sibling registry to `RLS_POLICIES` (preserves the
  prompt-22 snapshot test). Declares INSERT for `service_role`
  only, SELECT for `service_role` + `admin`, and **no UPDATE
  or DELETE policy for any role** — combined with default-deny
  RLS this is the on-disk tampering invariant.
* `tests/test_pii_tokenization.py` (14 tests) +
  `tests/test_pii_audit_rls.py` (9 tests), all 23 green —
  cover tokenizer determinism per (kind, salt), salt and kind
  separation, email normalisation, empty-input rejection,
  missing-salt error, `read_clear_email` denied without scope,
  `read_clear_email` with scope returns clear and writes one
  audit row per call, the audit row never contains the clear
  value, the no-UPDATE / no-DELETE policy contract for the
  audit table, and the application guard against UPDATE /
  DELETE on SQLite (where the Postgres trigger doesn't apply).
* `docs/specs/pii_handling.md` — operator-facing reference:
  storage shape (token + ciphertext + key_id triple),
  tokenization invariant, salt management with the
  documented rotation play, the `pii:read_clear` scope wiring
  (and the follow-up to add it to `KNOWN_SCOPES`), the audit
  log schema, the RLS + trigger immutability contract, and
  the load-bearing prohibitions.

Mandatory invariants honored (load-bearing prompt-58
prohibitions):

* Do NOT log clear PII anywhere. Only the *token* form is
  written to the audit row, and the `note` / `reason` columns
  are documented as token-only as well.
* Do NOT permit DELETE on `pii_clear_audit_log` from any role.
  No UPDATE or DELETE policy is declared for any role; the
  defence-in-depth trigger raises on any UPDATE / DELETE
  statement at the table level.
* Do NOT use a non-cryptographic hash for tokenization. The
  tokenizer uses `hmac.new(salt, msg, hashlib.sha256)`; md5 /
  sha1 / fnv would all be review-blocking.
* No edits outside SCOPE. (Adding `pii:read_clear` to
  `KNOWN_SCOPES` in `api_key_service.py` is the documented
  follow-up integration step; until then test principals are
  constructed directly via `ClearReadPrincipal(...)`.)

Follow-ups intentionally left for future prompts (out of
prompt-58 SCOPE):

* Add `pii:read_clear` to `KNOWN_SCOPES` in
  `server/fund/services/api_key_service.py` so admins can
  issue keys with the scope through the existing UI.
* Apply the same triple (token + clear + key_id) to
  `full_name`, `phone`, and `residence_address` columns
  wherever they exist on `Founder` / KYC / signature
  surfaces.
* Run the contract migration: drop the legacy `email`
  column from `fund_founders` once every caller (CRM sync,
  retention, decision overrides, etc.) is on `email_token`
  + `read_clear_email`.
* Schedule a re-tokenization migration as part of the
  documented salt-rotation play.

Verify with:
  python3 -m pytest -p "no:pytest-qt" \
    coherence_engine/tests/test_pii_tokenization.py \
    coherence_engine/tests/test_pii_audit_rls.py -v
  → 14 + 9 = 23 passed.

══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
Prompt 67 — Release pipeline (semver + changelog + signed
              images + helm chart)                           [DONE]
══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

Wave 17. Lands the tag-triggered release pipeline that publishes
container images, helm chart, GitHub Release, and opens the
post-release VERSION-bump PR.

What landed:

* `scripts/release/changelog.py` — conventional-commit parser
  (feat|fix|perf|refactor|docs|test|build|ci|chore|revert,
  optional scope and `!` breaking marker, body
  `BREAKING CHANGE:` honored). Renders deterministic Markdown
  with canonical section ordering. Headers that don't match
  the pattern fall through into `chore` rather than being
  silently dropped.
* `scripts/release/cut_release.py` — release driver. Reads
  `VERSION`, parses commits (git or JSON fixture), infers
  next semver bump (major if breaking, minor if any feat,
  else patch), renders the release-scoped changelog, and on
  `--require-readiness` invokes
  `deploy/scripts/release_readiness_check.py` and refuses to
  proceed on a non-zero exit.
* `Dockerfile` — multi-stage backend image
  (python:3.11-slim-bookworm, builder venv → runtime),
  non-root user, tini PID-1, `/live` healthcheck, OCI labels
  populated from build args.
* `apps/founder_portal/Dockerfile`,
  `apps/partner_dashboard/Dockerfile` — multi-stage Next.js
  14 standalone images (deps → build → runtime), non-root
  user, tini, OCI labels.
* `deploy/helm/Chart.yaml` + `deploy/helm/values.yaml` —
  umbrella chart wrapping the existing
  `deploy/helm/coherence-fund/` subchart (file:// dependency
  resolved via the `deploy/helm/charts/coherence-fund`
  symlink so `helm template deploy/helm` renders without a
  prior `helm dependency build`). Existing
  `deploy/helm/templates/prometheus-rules-pipeline.yaml` stub
  stays as-is (gated `if .Values.prometheusRules.enabled`,
  defaults to false).
* `.github/workflows/release.yml` — tag-triggered jobs
  (`release_lint_test`, `release_readiness_gate`,
  `release_changelog`, `release_build_sign`,
  `release_helm_chart`, `release_publish`) added alongside
  the existing `workflow_dispatch` deploy path. Existing
  jobs gated `if: github.event_name == 'workflow_dispatch'`.
  cosign keyless OIDC signs every image digest and the
  helm chart; cosign attests SLSA provenance. The publish
  job ends with a `gh pr create --base main` against
  `release/post-<version>-version-bump` so the VERSION-bump
  PR is unmissable. Permissions block elevated to
  id-token:write, contents:write, packages:write,
  pull-requests:write.
* `tests/test_release_pipeline.py` — 10 tests covering
  determinism, conventional-commit grouping, helm chart
  structure, helm template render (skipped when helm is not
  on PATH), workflow trigger + cosign references, and
  Dockerfile non-root multi-stage shape.
* `docs/ops/release.md` — operator runbook: semver policy,
  per-job pipeline, cosign verify recipes (image, chart,
  SLSA), prohibition guardrails, hot-fix flow.

Prompt 68 — Cap-table integration (Carta primary, Pulley alternate).
Wave 18 opener. Adds the post-investment cap-table sync layer:
record-keeping only, never unilaterally issues securities.

Landed:
* `server/fund/services/cap_table_backends.py` -- `CapTableBackend`
  protocol with `CartaBackend` (primary) and `PulleyBackend`
  (alternate); deterministic provider issuance ids; in-process
  ledger fallback for reconcile testing.
* `server/fund/services/cap_table.py` -- `CapTableService` owns
  the `CapTableIssuance` lifecycle (`pending -> recorded ->
  reconciled`, terminal `failed`). Load-bearing precondition:
  application MUST have BOTH a signed `SignatureRequest`
  (prompt 52) AND a sent `InvestmentInstruction` (prompt 51)
  before `record_issuance` will fire; otherwise raises
  `PreconditionsNotMet`. Idempotent on
  `sha256(application|instrument_type|salt)` (salt =
  instruction id). `reconcile(backend=...)` flags
  divergences but NEVER silently rewrites local rows from
  provider responses.
* `server/fund/models.py` -- `CapTableIssuance` ORM row.
* `alembic/versions/20260425_000018_cap_table.py` --
  `fund_cap_table_issuances` table + unique idempotency-
  key index.
* `server/fund/services/application_service.py` --
  `maybe_sync_cap_table(application_id, ...)` hook callable
  from both webhooks; whichever fires second satisfies the
  gate and performs the sync, the other returns `None`.
* `tests/test_cap_table.py` -- 17 tests (backend round-
  trip, precondition gating, reconcile divergence flag).
* `docs/specs/cap_table.md` -- lifecycle, preconditions,
  reconciliation discipline, env-var matrix.

Prompt 69 — LP reporting pipeline (quarterly NAV, capital-call
            and distribution notices, LP portal).
Wave 18 continues. Adds the LP-facing reporting layer.

Landed:
* `server/fund/services/nav_calculator.py` -- pure-functional
  per-LP NAV math. `compute_nav` consumes an `LPCommitment`,
  the fund's `PortfolioPosition`s, an operator-attested
  `Mark` table, and a dated `CashFlow` series; returns a
  frozen `NAVSnapshot` with cost basis, FMV, unrealized
  gain, NAV (FMV + uncalled), and IRR. `compute_irr` uses
  `pyxirr` when importable; otherwise an in-tree
  Newton-Raphson XIRR with bisection over [-0.999, 10.0].
  Load-bearing: any held position without a signed Mark
  raises `UnsignedMarkError`.
* `server/fund/services/lp_reporting.py` -- orchestrator +
  Jinja2 / LaTeX env (square-bracket delimiters,
  StrictUndefined, byte-deterministic). Returns a frozen
  `QuarterlyStatement` with `tex_source`, SHA-256
  `content_digest`, and `statement_id`. `assemble_batch`
  emits one statement per LP without sharing intermediate
  state across LPs.
* `server/fund/services/capital_call_notice.py` --
  `CapitalCallNotice` payload + `render_notice` (.tex +
  digest) + `render_pdf` (re-uses the MRM `pdflatex`
  runner) + `dispatch_for_signature(provider=...)` that
  hands the rendered document to a caller-supplied
  `ESignatureProvider` (DocuSign backend, prompt 52).
  Idempotency: sha256(call_id|lp_id).
* `server/fund/services/distribution_notice.py` --
  `DistributionNotice` payload + acknowledgement-only
  dispatch helper. `treasurer_approval_ref` is REQUIRED
  (validated at render AND dispatch). LP signer role is
  `lp_acknowledger` -- the type-system marker that the
  LP is acknowledging receipt, NOT authorising a wire.
* `data/governed/lp_reports/templates/{quarterly_nav,
  capital_call,distribution_notice}.tex.j2` -- governed
  LaTeX templates.
* `apps/lp_portal/` -- Next.js 14 (App Router) scaffold on
  port 3002 mirroring `apps/founder_portal/`. Pages: `/`,
  `/lp`, `/lp/statements`, `/lp/notices`. RBAC in
  `src/lib/rbac.ts`: `app_metadata.roles` MUST contain
  `"lp"` (legacy: `app_metadata.role === "lp"`) AND
  `app_metadata.lp_id` MUST be set. Shared guard
  `requireLpSession()` constructs the `LpApiClient`
  exclusively from the session's own `lp_id` -- no
  user-supplied id is ever honoured.
* `tests/test_nav_calculator.py` (10 tests) +
  `tests/test_lp_reporting.py` (15 tests) +
  `apps/lp_portal/__tests__/{rbac,lp_api}.test.ts`
  (vitest). Local run:
  `python3 -m pytest -p no:pytest-qt
   coherence_engine/tests/test_nav_calculator.py
   coherence_engine/tests/test_lp_reporting.py -v`
  -> 25 passed in 0.42s.
* `docs/specs/lp_reporting.md` -- module map, math, IRR
  contract, RBAC, prohibitions, operator obligations.

Verification markers:
  * server/fund/services/nav_calculator.py
        : `def compute_nav\b|IRR` ✓
  * server/fund/services/capital_call_notice.py
        : `def render_notice\b` ✓
  * apps/lp_portal/src/app/lp/statements/page.tsx
        : `nav|statement` ✓
  * docs/specs/lp_reporting.md
        : `NAV|capital call|distribution` ✓

Follow-ups intentionally left for future prompts:

* `Mark`, `LPCommitment`, `CapitalCall`, `DistributionNotice`
  persistence is intentionally NOT in
  `server/fund/models.py` yet -- the LP-reporting services
  operate on dataclass inputs the caller supplies. A future
  prompt will land the migration once the operator UI for
  marks + capital-call schedule generator lands.
* Backend `/api/v1/lp/<lp_id>/{overview,statements,notices}`

  `apps/lp_portal/src/lib/lp_api.ts` but the routes are

Next: prompt 70 (final prompt of the 70-prompt program).

══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
RECENT CHANGES — Wave 18, prompt 70/70
            Reserve-allocation optimizer + decision-policy
            parameter proposals                          [DONE]
══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

The deterministic reserve-allocation optimizer + the proposal
lifecycle that gates promotion behind explicit operator approval.

What landed:

* `server/fund/services/reserve_optimizer.py` -- pure-functional
  optimizer. `optimize(OptimizerInputs)` returns an
  `OptimizerResult` with proposed/current parameter sets, the
  cost-of-error model derived from the validation study report,
  the populated backtest delta (pass-rate / false-pass exposure /
  reserve coverage / objective), and the optimizer method
  (`grid` or `scipy`). Constrained formulation:
  `minimize lost_ev(theta) s.t. false_pass_exposure <= budget`,
  `CS0_d in [0.10, 0.40]`, `alpha_d in [0.10, 0.50]`. Default
  path is a deterministic 9x9 grid; `--prefer-scipy` lazy-imports
  `scipy.optimize.minimize` (SLSQP). The current parameters are
  always seeded into the candidate list so the proposal is never
  strictly worse than the running policy on the in-sample
  objective.
* `server/fund/services/policy_parameter_proposals.py` --
  persistence + lifecycle. `create` enforces a 30-day rate limit
  on overlapping domains (`PROPOSAL_RATE_LIMITED`). `approve` is
  admin-only (`PROPOSAL_FORBIDDEN` otherwise) and emits
  `policy_parameter_approved.v1` with idempotency key
  `proposal:<id>:approved`. **Approval does NOT promote.**
  Promotion to the running decision policy is an explicit
  out-of-SCOPE operator runbook step.
* `server/fund/models.py` -- `PolicyParameterProposal` (id,
  proposed_by, parameters_json, rationale, backtest_report_uri,
  status, approved_by, approved_at, created_at, updated_at) +
  `PolicyParameterApproval` (append-only audit row).
* `alembic/versions/20260425_000019_policy_parameter_proposals.py`
  -- `fund_policy_parameter_proposals` and
  `fund_policy_parameter_approvals` with indexes on `status` /
  `created_at` / `proposal_id` / `decision`.
* `cli.py` -- `policy propose|review|approve`. The `propose`
  subcommand reads `--inputs portfolio_snapshot.json`,
  optionally overrides the validation study via
  `--validation-study`, runs the optimizer + backtest replay,
  writes the canonical JSON to `--output`, persists a
  `PolicyParameterProposal` row, and prints a one-line summary.
* `tests/test_reserve_optimizer.py` (9 tests) +
  `tests/test_policy_parameter_proposals.py` (10 tests) +
  `tests/fixtures/policy/{snapshot,study}.json`. Local run:
  `python3 -m pytest -p no:pytest-qt
   coherence_engine/tests/test_reserve_optimizer.py
   coherence_engine/tests/test_policy_parameter_proposals.py -v`
  -> 19 passed in 2.50s.
* `docs/specs/reserve_optimizer.md` -- cost-of-error model,
  decision frequency (monthly), rollback plan (re-promote
  the prior approved proposal), determinism guarantees.

Verification markers:
  * server/fund/services/reserve_optimizer.py
        : `def optimize\b|scipy\.optimize` ✓
  * server/fund/services/policy_parameter_proposals.py
        : service is `PolicyParameterProposalService`; the
        ORM class `PolicyParameterProposal` lives in
        `server/fund/models.py` (re-exported by the service
        via `models.PolicyParameterProposal`).
  * cli.py
        : `policy propose|policy approve` ✓
  * docs/specs/reserve_optimizer.md
        : `optimizer|backtest|rollback` ✓
  * tests/test_reserve_optimizer.py
        : `optimize|reserve` ✓

Follow-ups intentionally left for future prompts:

* Decision-policy promotion script -- the explicit operator
  runbook step that consumes `policy_parameter_approved.v1`
  and writes a new pinned parameter set into the running
  `DecisionPolicyService._params_for_domain`. Out of SCOPE
  here; the prompt explicitly mandates that promotion be a
  separate, explicit step.
* Per-domain false-pass-budget weighting. The optimizer
  currently splits the total budget evenly across
  `inputs.domains`; an exposure-weighted split is a future
  enhancement keyed off the prompt-44 domain breakdown.

This was the final prompt (70/70) of the build program. The
fund stack now has a deterministic optimizer + an
operator-approval workflow for decision-policy parameter
tuning, with the explicit guarantee that the running policy
is never mutated by the optimizer or its approval emit
without a human-in-the-loop runbook step.
